First, boil the above herbs in two bowls of water and divide it into two doses, mixing half of the cinnabar into the medicine for the patient to take. If the patient refuses to take it, give them charcoal; after consuming it, they will be happy to eat it. If they ask for more charcoal, it is fine to provide them with it. The second dose should be prepared in the same way. If the patient does not respond as well as before, they should be made to drink it quickly. If they resist, it is permissible to strike them to provoke their anger; anger will stir the liver's wood fire, generating heat for the heart, thus helping to dispel phlegm.

    Although patients with epilepsy often eat regularly, the qi of food within their intestines can nourish their life without dying; it is, however, the heart that remains unyielding.[50p]
    If the heart dies early, then even a healthy person consuming grains will also perish; how much more so for those with epilepsy? I have seen those who perish early cannot wait until today. As long as the heart remains alive, it is merely phlegm and evil that obstructs it. At that moment of epilepsy, the spleen and stomach still hold vitality. Therefore, I use ginseng to treat the heart, adding aconite, calamus, and cinnamon to warm the center and dispel the evil. I add bupleurum to soothe the liver and balance the wood element, along with nux vomica, ghost arrow, and pinellia to expel phlegm and eliminate the evil. I add cinnabar to stabilize the spirit and calm the soul, naturally reducing the evil qi and increasing the righteous qi.

    There is another remarkable method for treating epilepsy. The formula includes five qians each of bupleurum and white mustard seed, three qians each of white peony, pinellia, processed nux vomica, poria, and calamus, and one qian each of aconite and ginseng. Boil with ten bowls of water until reduced to two bowls. Give the patient one bowl to drink first, which will certainly cause fatigue. Then immediately administer another bowl, which will induce deep sleep. If they sleep for one or two days, do not awaken them suddenly, as if they were dead; let them wake naturally. When they awaken and are confused, ask for food and drink. If they mention their previous condition, do not give them anything immediately. After half a day of fasting, give them rice porridge, adding five fen each of ginseng and aged tangerine peel to the soup, and cook the porridge to serve.[51p]
    Use three qian of ginseng, one liang of atractylodes, one qian of licorice, five qian each of poria and white mustard seed, and five fen of dried tangerine peel. Boil these in water and give it to them, and they will surely take it willingly. After taking it, let them sleep again; listen for them to wake up on their own, and then they will never have another episode, which is a marvelous method.

    In cases where a person suffers from an illness analogous to flower mania, a woman might suddenly have epilepsy, seeing a man and refusing to let go of him. This represents an intense longing for a man that cannot be fulfilled, suddenly manifesting as a disease, like a violent storm, losing all sense of shame; upon seeing a man, she behaves as if he were her lover. This is due to the liver's wood being withered and an inner fire raging strongly, and the pulse will definitely be tight at the cun position. The treatment should use a formula to soothe the liver, disperse stagnation, and expel evil. Use five qian each of bupleurum, angelica, ophiopogon, and white mustard seed; one liang of white peony; and three qian each of stir-fried gardenia, poria spirit, and scrophularia; with one qian each of licorice and calamus, boiled in water to be taken.

    If she refuses to take it, force it into her via a syringe; she will undoubtedly curse incessantly. After a while, the person will become weary and want to lie down. After they awaken, feeling shame, they will tightly close the room's door for three days, and gradually, with a little food and drink, will recover on their own. After one dose, there is no need to give her more medicine.[52p]
    Epileptic illness often arises from the weakness and coldness of the spleen and stomach. When the spleen and stomach are weak and cold, the food consumed does not transform into essential qi but instead becomes phlegm. This phlegm condenses between the chest and diaphragm, unable to flow to the heart, leading to the manifestation of epilepsy. If one only treats phlegm without nourishing qi, there will inevitably be cases of sudden death.

    The recipe for the treatment is as follows: Take five qian each of ginseng and white mustard seed, one liang of white atractylodes, one qian each of cinnamon, dried ginger, and tangerine peel, five fen each of licorice and fragrant calamus, and three qian of pinellia; decoct these herbs in water to take. This formula uses ginseng and atractylodes specifically to nourish the spleen and stomach, dried ginger to dispel cold pathogens, white mustard seed and pinellia to eliminate stubborn phlegm, and licorice and fragrant calamus to guide the formula into the heart and open the orifices. Naturally, the righteous qi returns, and the phlegm disperses.

    With one dose, the spirit stabilizes; with a second dose, the spirit flourishes. What epilepsy cannot be cured? As for the manifestation of flower-related epilepsy, it stems from a woman's obsession with someone, which is also due to the coldness of the spleen and stomach allowing the evil to invade. For this condition, add one liang of white peony root, two qian of bupleurum, and three qian of stir-fried gardenia to the original recipe, omitting the cinnamon; it is also very effective, often stopping the epilepsy with just one dose. The reason is that bupleurum, white peony, and stir-fried gardenia all enter the liver to balance the wood element, dispel fire and scatter stagnant qi, thus achieving this extraordinary effect.[53p]
    Treatment of Stupor

    Stupor resembles madness, silent and uncommunicative; like hunger, it lingers but feels lost. The mind desires to act wildly yet cannot; the heart wishes to be frantic but is afraid. Sometimes one may sleep for days without waking, at other times sit for days without sleeping. Occasionally, they meticulously mend their own clothes, or deeply hide and cover someone else's belongings. When speaking with others, they are mute and seem to drift away; when alone, they whisper quietly and cry. They may express aversion to food and refuse to swallow, yet when not offered food, they consume charcoal as if it were delightful. Although these symptoms may be attributed to possession or evil influence, they are essentially caused by phlegm and qi obstructing the chest and abdomen. Thus, the treatment for stupor is no mystery; treating phlegm is the same as treating stupor.[54p]
    However, when phlegm is at its peak and dullness is profound, how can it be effectively treated with ordinary Erchen Decoction? Therefore, the method uses the Immortal Pill to expel dullness: one tael each of ginseng, white mustard seed, and dodder seed; two taels of white atractylodes; three taels of poria; five qian of pinellia; five fen of aconite; three qian each of white wood蘇 and cinnabar, ground into powder. First, decoct each herbal ingredient, then mix the cinnabar powder with half a bowl of the decoction. If he refuses to take it, administer it with charcoal, and he will gladly drink it. After giving him another half bowl, allow him to act as he wishes; he will certainly feel tired and want to sleep.

    Take advantage of his deep sleep to burn all his clothing and bedding, leaving only the garments he is wearing, and cover him with a new blanket, being careful not to wake him. This sleep may last several days; when he wakes, he will surely look for his clothes and find nothing, search for his bedding and discover it is not familiar, leading him to cry out in distress. Then present him with the same medicine again; he will surely refuse to take it, and even refuse the charcoal. It may be effective to whip him to provoke his anger, using strong individuals to hold him down and force the previous medicine into him; he will undoubtedly become very angry, and afterward, he will fall asleep again.[55p]
    At this time, one must prepare fresh clothing, bedding, and other items, awaiting his awakening in half a day. When he sees that the whole room is filled with relatives, his heart will suddenly clear as if he understands, and he will undoubtedly weep greatly. Others should gently persuade him, and he will surely speak of matters concerning spirits and deities. Relatives will then say that a certain person has treated him and has already dispelled all the spirits, so there is no need for further worry. Upon hearing this, he will feel joyful, and his illness will be completely cured. The key to this method lies in greatly nourishing the heart and spleen, using Fuling (Poria) as the primary agent, which helps to expel phlegm from the heart; the remaining phlegm-dissolving medicine, along with Aconite, guides it throughout the body, sending all phlegm into the bladder for digestion. Baiwei (White Clay) and Tusizi (Cuscuta) are both excellent soothing herbs, while Cinnabar stabilizes the soul and calms the spirit, thus having remarkable effects, which is why they are used and produce results.[56p]
    The condition of "stupor" arises from a blockage of emotions, sometimes resulting from anger and at other times from shame. The remedy consists of one tael each of ginseng, Chaihu (Bupleurum), Angelica, calamus, and jujube seeds; four taels of white peony; five qian each of licorice, tian nanxing (Arisaema), turmeric, and shenqu; one qian of aconite; three taels of poria; and ten bowls of water, boiled down to one bowl for administration. The patient will likely refuse to drink the medicine. To facilitate the process, two individuals should hold the patient's hands while one supports their chin, another inserts a blunt sheep horn into their mouth, and yet another holds the patient's head to pour the medicine into the horn. If the patient vomits, it is no concern; the focus should be to administer the entire dose. The patient may scream and curse, but after a while, they will become tired and want to sleep. It is important to allow them to wake up on their own without disturbance. If they awaken naturally, they will fully recover; if startled awake, their recovery will be only partial. This is one method of treating this condition.[57p]
    Treatment for Mania

    When phlegm accumulates in the stomach and cannot be expelled, it leads to maniacal speech as if seeing ghosts, intermittently appearing and disappearing, causing a blockage in the chest. One should boil five pounds of beef and two dou of water into a soup and drink it until one can no longer eat. With a goose feather, probe for vomiting, and one will surely expel a large amount, specifically until a lump of thick yellow phlegm is expelled before ceasing. If it does not come out, drink again, ensuring it is completely expelled before stopping, or the previous condition will suddenly worsen. Afterwards, gradually drink a decoction of dried tangerine peel, Poria, licorice, and white atractylodes to restore balance.

    In cases of fever leading to mania, where one might climb high and sing, discard clothing and run, dive into water, shout and curse without regard for kin, such beings are far from life. Zhongjing saved them with a decoction of bamboo leaves and gypsum, which is quite wonderful. The fire of Yangming is the most intense; once it erupts, it cannot be saved without a large dose of White Tiger Decoction to halt its overwhelming spread. However, people often fear using too much, thus employing only a small amount, akin to using a cup of water to extinguish a burning pile of firewood. Therefore, gypsum must be used in a dose of three or four taels or even half a pound, prepared in one decoction, for the fire's intensity to begin to diminish, and mania can also be somewhat alleviated. Yet, gypsum has a strong nature; though it effectively cools the fire, it can still damage the stomach's qi, hence it must be used in conjunction with ginseng for optimal effect.

    Currently, there is a formula that uses half the White Tiger Decoction while adding other medicinal ingredients, named the Stomach-Replenishing Decoction. It consists of three taels each of gypsum, Scrophularia, and Ophiopogon, three qian of Anemarrhena, five qian each of ginseng and Plantago, and one tael of Poria, all combined with water for decoction.[58p]
    This formula uses gypsum and Anemarrhena as a remedy to drain stomach fire, ginseng to generate stomach qi, and Yuan Shen to eliminate excess heat. Ophiopogon nourishes the yin of the lungs, while Poria and Plantago help direct fire downward to the bladder, allowing it to exit through urination. Furthermore, when there is excessive fire, one’s mouth must be dry; with thirst comes increased water intake. I employ these two ingredients to disperse moisture, so that when water flows, the fire dissipates alongside it. This formula drains fire without harming qi, appearing superior to Bai Hu Tang. One dose calms the delirium, two doses reduce thirst by half, and three doses stop the thirst completely, also extinguishing the fire, thus four doses are unnecessary.

    For those experiencing fire heat leading to delirium, or sweating profusely like rain, with dry mouth and tongue, or sensations like thorn pricks, this formula will yield immediate effects, ensuring it does not lead to death. "Living treatment" refers to situations where a person is on the brink of death, but not yet dead, and medication is used to restore them. For instance, cases of manic or comatose illness are often due to heat illness, characterized by singing high, running while discarding clothing, jumping into water, and incessantly shouting violent words, with protruding tongue and relentless thirst, producing bright phlegm and a face resembling an inflamed state.

    The formula uses half a pound of gypsum, one pound of Yuan Shen, three taels of white mustard and pinellia each, one tael of Anemarrhena, ginseng, and licorice, along with five taels of Ophiopogon and several hundred pieces of bamboo leaves. First, half a sheng of glutinous rice is boiled to create a broth, with the rice grains removed. Half a pot of this broth is then used to brew the previously mentioned herbs, with several bowls taken to provide in response to requests for water. Offer it continuously and, once finished, sleep will follow. Promptly use another pound of Yuan Shen and half a pound of Ophiopogon for brewing while waiting.[59p]
    When someone awakens and calls for water, give them this soup, and they will surely drink it with joy. After finishing it, they will likely fall into a deep sleep again, and then prepare more soup with the residue for when they wake. When they wake again, if they do not want to drink as before, do not force them; let it happen naturally. Later, use three taels of cooked rehmannia and ophiopogon, six taels of codonopsis, one tael of cornus, decocted into two bowls to give them. One dose will surely cure them, and there is no need to repeat it. This is one method of treatment.

    As for those who have a fit of madness but stop to curse at others, not thirsty, and refuse to drink the offered water, this is madness caused by cold. It arises from stagnation of Qi and repressed anger; such individuals typically display weakness and lack of spirit, and the madness manifests abruptly. The treatment should focus on expelling phlegm while also supplementing Qi. The prescription includes one tael each of ginseng and poria, five qian of white atractylodes, one qian each of pinellia, nux vomica, and aconite, and three fen of calamus, all decocted and taken. The brilliance of this formula lies in supplementing Qi while not excessively expelling phlegm. Cold-induced madness is treated similarly to epilepsy, and aconite is included to eliminate cold Qi, while calamus directs the remedy to the heart channel, letting it naturally soothe the throat for sound sleep, as if lost to the disease. Adding one qian of bupleurum helps to relieve the stagnation of the liver wood Qi, further enhancing effectiveness.

    Some individuals may have persistent madness that does not improve; they might attack others with a knife, curse officials loudly, fail to recognize family, or have children unaware of them, showing joy at the sight of water but anger at food. This reflects a deficiency of heart Qi and an invasion by heat evil, along with phlegm Qi encumbering them.[60p]
    These ailments desire to dispel fire, yet fire resides within the heart, making it impossible to disperse; they want to eliminate phlegm, yet phlegm is also in the heart, making it difficult to dissolve. Only by strengthening the energy of the spleen and stomach can the heart receive nourishment on its own. There’s no need to eliminate phlegm; it will naturally transform, and there’s no need to dispel fire; it will naturally cease. This method is named "Transforming Madness Elixir," using one tael each of ginseng, white atractylodes, and poria, one fen (a unit), and three qian each of pinellia and cuscus, one qian each of calamus and licorice, boiled in water for consumption. One dose will calm the madness, and the second will heal the illness. This method is excellent for nourishing the heart, spleen, and stomach while transforming phlegm without dispelling fire. For if fire is dispelled, the heart's energy becomes more injured, and phlegm accumulates further; how can madness be stopped? Notably, the use of one fen of aconite is brilliant, facilitating the nourishing of the heart and the dissolving of phlegm directly into the heart, allowing energy to be easily replenished and phlegm to be easily dissolved.

    When a person is ill and becomes mad, as if seeing ghosts, it is due to the deficiency of righteous energy and the invasion of邪 (evil). It seems appropriate to rectify the邪. However, since邪 gathers where energy is weak, if we do not treat the deficiency, how can we talk of the rest? Thus, it is urgent to support the righteous energy and lightly assist with medications to eliminate phlegm and邪. For those who see ghosts in madness, it is a deficiency. Therefore, use one tael each of ginseng and white atractylodes, three qian each of pinellia and tian nanxing, and one qian of aconite, and administer a large dose; the madness will calm itself.

    For those who are mad, do not recognize people, and do not see ghosts, this signifies heat. They should not be given the previous decoction. Seeing ghosts indicates deficiency and not true heat, so the method includes ginseng, added to medications for eliminating phlegm and邪, as it is a reversal for treatment.[61p]

    Baodai Pill treats all forms of wind-induced madness in men and women, or caused by shock and fear; also for women having postpartum blood deficiency, where fear enters the heart, and for maidens where menstrual flow is obstructed by trapped evil.
    Two taels of mercury, one tael each of finely ground frankincense (de-oiled) and cinnabar; one and a half taels of black lead.
    Combine the black lead in a small pan, add the mercury to form granules, then add cinnamon, and drop in frankincense. While hot, use a willow wood pestle to blend, forming pills the size of a chick's head. Take one pill on an empty stomach, swallowed with water from a deep well. If the patient sleeps, do not disturb them; upon waking, if necessary, another pill can eliminate the issue completely.[63p]
    Wuxie Decoction: It treats stroke with dimming of the mind, invaded by the Five Evils, causing one to sing, cry, laugh, rejoice, or become angry at any time.

    Ingredients:

    • Fangfeng
    • Gui Xin (Cinnamomum cassia heart)
    • Bai Shao (White Peony root)
    • Yuan Zhi (Polygala root)
    • Du Huo (Angelica
    • Gan Cao (Licorice) (roasted)
    • Bai Zhu (Atractylodes)
    • Ren Shen (Ginseng)
    • Qin Jiao (Gentian)
    • Duan Mu Li (Calcined Oyster Shell)
    • Shi Gao (Gypsum)
    • Yu Yu Liang (a type of vinegar) (each two liang)
    • Xiong Huang (Realgar powder) (water-flying)
    • Fangfeng
    • Shi Chao Pu (Acorus calamus)
    • Fu Shen (Poria)
    • She Dui Pi (Snake skin) (stir-fried) (each one liang)

    Take four qian with two bowls of water, decoct to one bowl, strain it and take warm without time restrictions, two doses per day.

    Jiu Jing Pill: Also known as Jiu Wu Niu Huang Pill. It treats men who feel haunted by evil spirits, experiencing fear and a desire to run, with no moment of rest, unable to rid themselves of evil qi.

    Ingredients:

    • Niu Huang (Bovine bile)
    • Tu Jing (earth essence, also fire essence)
    • Long Gu (Dragon bone)
    • Shui Jing (water essence)
    • Jing Shi (Schizonepeta)
    • Ren Jing (human essence)
    • Yuan Shen (speculated essence)
    • Yuan Wu (one original essence)
    • Chi Shi Zhi (Red stone resin)
    • Zhu Que (Vermilion bird essence)
    • Yu Xie (jade powder, finely ground)
    • Bai Hu Jing (White tiger essence)
    • Ceng Qing (formerly only Cang Long essence)
    • Kong Qing (empty blue powder, ground)
    • Tian Jing (heaven essence)
    • Xiong Huang (Realgar)
    • Di Jing (earth essence); if no stones are available, roast and grind, each one liang.

    These nine flavors collectively form the Nine Essentials, connecting to the nine heavens above and the nine realms below. Grind into a fine powder, refine with honey, and form into pills the size of small beans. Take one pill three times a day, adjusting dosage as needed.[64p]
    Gansui San (also known as Suixin Dan) is used to treat epilepsy and women's heart wind blood evil.

    Ingredients: 1 qian of Gansui.

    Preparation: Grind the Gansui into powder, then take three tubes of blood from a pig's heart, mix with a corresponding amount of Gansui. Cut the heart into two pieces, place the medicine inside, stitch it up, wrap it in damp paper, and simmer it on low heat until thoroughly cooked, or until it is scorched. Take the medicinal mixture, grind it finely, add 1 qian of cinnabar powder, mix well, and divide into four pills. Each time, take one pill dissolved in decoction of the simmered pig's heart. It is also acceptable to use another pig's heart for subsequent doses. After half a day, when the unpleasant material is expelled through bowel movement, it helps to harmonize stomach qi. This treatment is effective for sudden onset or awakening aggression but is not suitable for those who are excessively hungry or confused.

    Xiexin Tang treats accumulated heat in the heart, leading to delirium and madness, including climbing walls.

    Ingredients: 5 qian each of Dahuang (Rhubarb), Huangqin (Scutellaria), and Huanglian (Coptis).

    Preparation: Grind the above ingredients into powder, and take 4 qian with 1.5 cups of water for decoction.

    Yinshen Guishe Dan is used to treat heart qi and also addresses heart wind.[65p]
    Heavenly South Star: Scrape off the skin and take the heart; take one tael each of vermilion water and flying water; one piece of aconite, weighing at least seven qian, remove the skin and umbilicus. Grind these into a fine powder. Use pig heart blood to form into pills the size of wutong seeds. If it is not sticky enough, add a little flour paste. Boil in the broth of forgetfulness root and take one dose at each time of Zi and Wu.

    Secret Recipe Banxia Pill (from "Collected Experience Recipes"): Treats heart wind madness. Zhang Deming transmitted this; his wife lost her mind for several years, and after taking this medicine, she recovered. Later, she took ginseng amber pills for stability.

    Take one tael of Banxia, boil with fresh ginger juice until it reaches fifty boils. After removing, cut it into pieces, and continue to boil until cooked. Dry and powder finely. Take one qian of musk, grind; half qian of mercury; a large handful of fresh mint, and mix mercury until it becomes mud.

    Mix all these medicines into the mint mud and grind extensively. Form into pills the size of mustard seeds. Take fifteen pills each time with golden or silver liquor before bed, and repeat after three days.

    Ginseng Amber Pills: Treats epilepsy and heart wind.

    Ingredients: Ginseng, amber, and powdered Rehmannia, Reishi, stone calamus, and Polygala each half a tael; soak in warm wine for half a day and remove the heart; additional separately ground frankincense; sour jujube seeds soaked in warm wine for half a day, shell removed, and roasted on clean paper until fragrant; separately ground vermilion, each two and a half qian.

    Make a fine powder and mix with honey to form pills the size of wutong seeds. Take twenty pills after meals with warm wine; take daily. If unable to drink, use jujube soup instead. Can be taken regularly.[66p]
    Ningzhi Pill [from "De Xiaofang"]

    For treating heart wind.

    Take one tael of good cinnabar, and a small piece of cooked silk, wrap it up and tie it with a string, without grinding. Use one pig's heart, cut open with a bamboo knife, avoiding iron. Wipe away the blood with paper, place the wrapped cinnabar inside the pig's heart, and tie it with string.

    Then wrap it heavily with the shell of sweet bamboo shoots, secure it with hemp cloth. In two liters of weak wine, put it in a silver vessel or clay pot and boil it until the wine is completely gone, then remove the wrapping and take out the cinnabar. Grind the pig's heart finely with the bamboo knife in a mortar, and mix it with the following powdered ingredients:

    Cured red ginseng, white poria, angelica (washed to remove dirt), acorus, and frankincense (grind separately), about five taels of sour jujube seeds (soak to remove the skin, fry the clean seeds until red, and fragrant). Use equal quantities of these ingredients, mix them into a powder, and form into pills the size of a wutong seed, using the reserved cinnabar as a coating.

    Take fifty pills with ginseng soup each time.[67p]
    Rui Zhu Wan treats mania.
    One piece of pig's heart, one tael of blood, and one spoon of indigo flower ground together. First, grind the indigo flower and pig's blood together, then mix with the ground cinnabar to form pills the size of a walnut. Take twenty pills each time, with tea or wine, at any time.

    Tian Men Dong decoction treats wind-induced madness.
    Ten jin of Tian Men Dong, soaked in broth to remove the heart; thirty jin of fresh Rehmannia, cleaned and fat. Place these two ingredients in a wooden mortar, pound with one to two thousand pestle strokes to extract the juice. Then, add warm broth and continue to pound, extracting the juice again. Repeat this process until the two ingredients have no flavor, then simmer with gentle and vigorous heat until it becomes a paste, storing it in ceramic containers. Take one spoon each time, dissolving in warm wine, at any time, three times a day.[68p]
    Raw iron falls into the drink.

    Forty pounds of raw iron, heated in the fire until red, are hammered on the anvil until flowers resembling orchids and moths emerge, falling to the ground. This is called iron drop. Use two ditches of water to boil down to one ditch, adding the following medicine: gypsum three taels, dragon’s brain one and a half taels, white poria one and a half taels, fang feng one and a half taels, yuan shen one tael, and qin jiao one tael. This mixture is a coarse powder, added to the iron juice, simmered to yield five pounds. Strain out the dross and mix with one liter of bamboo juice, taking two doses warm, without a fixed time, five times a day.

    The cinnabar pill calms the mind, transforms phlegm, reduces tidal heat, benefits the throat, and alleviates thirst. The following ingredients are used: iron powder, sea gold sand, and天竺黄 (similar to turmeric), each one tael; half a cash of powdered brain; twenty sheets of gold and silver foil; one cash of fresh musk; two taels each of ginseng, light powder, and genuine rhinoceros horn; five taels of cinnabar. These are ground into a powder, made into water pills, and coated in cinnabar, forming six hundred pills.

    For each pill, take up to five, when phlegm is abundant and tidal heat is present; use mint, sugar, fresh kudzu juice, and well water to wash down. For wild talk and delirium, thick phlegm blocking the throat, use three taels of earth dragon, powdered mint, and sugar water. For restlessness of the mind, dissolve gold and silver foil in mint soup and take.[69p]
    Lai Su Gao, Rui Zhu Tang
    For treating wind diseases that have persisted for many years, such as wind convulsions, heart conditions, violent wind, stroke, excessive saliva and froth, inability to open the jaw, and tetanus spasms.
    One liang of soapberry, large and uninfested, peel and string it.
    First chop the soapberry into small pieces, soak in a large bowl of water for three to four days in spring and autumn, seven days in winter, and one to two days in summer. After soaking, squeeze out the juice into a silver vessel or a clay pot. Use both gentle and strong heat to boil, stirring with fresh willow twigs or locust branches. Cook until it resembles an ointment, then spread it on parchment and let it dry in the shade. When a patient arrives, take a piece the size of a palm, dissolve it in warm water in a small bowl, and use a small bamboo tube to administer the medicine by blowing it into both nostrils while the patient is seated upright with their head slightly elevated. After a while, help the patient up; the presence of saliva will indicate efficacy. To stop saliva, have the patient drink one or two sips of warm saline solution. Avoid chicken, fish, and hard, moist dough.

    Xi Xin San He Jian
    For treating wind obstruction and excessive saliva, accumulated heat in the heart, bitter mouth and dry lips, excessive tearing from the eyes, and constipation with dark red urine.
    One and a half liang of white atractylodes, with equal parts of:
    Ephedra, Angelica sinensis, Schizonepeta spikes, Peony, Licorice, and six liang of rhubarb wrapped in flour and stewed, then remove the flour, cut, and roast.
    The above should be ground into a powder; each dose is three qian, with one and a half cups of water, three slices of fresh ginger, and seven leaves of mint, boiled and taken as a decoction. It can also be taken as a fine powder mixed with clear tea.[70p]
    Ning Zhi Gao [from "Ben Shi Fang"]

    For treating madness and heart ailments.

    2. Sour Jujube Seed - 1 tael
    3. Cinnabar - 5 qian
    4. Frankincense - 2.5 qian

I used this prescription for my cousin who lost his mind due to war; after taking twenty pills, he recovered. It has been passed down among relatives and has proven effective for all who have taken it.

    Ling Yuan Cinnabar Powder
    For addressing wind-phlegm and various seizures, delusions, erratic behavior, mental confusion, sudden singing and weeping, irregular eating habits, seizures causing falls, drooling and vacant eyes, and loss of spirit.
    Ingredients:

    1. Cinnabar - 1 tael
    2. Lightly roasted Sour Jujube Seed - 0.5 tael
    3. Frankincense - 0.5 tael

    Based on the amount of alcohol the patient usually consumes, let them drink freely to get drunk but avoid vomiting. Once in a quiet room, take the prepared medicine and mix it with warm wine to make a drink, instructing them to drink it all at once. If they are not used to drinking, monitor the amount to ensure they become drunk. After taking the medicine, prepare a bed and a pillow for them to lie down. Those with mild conditions will recover in half a day to one day; those with severe conditions may take two to three days. Family members should monitor their breathing, ensuring it is steady, but do not wake them or startle them. Wait for them to awaken naturally, at which point their spirit will stabilize. Should they be startled awake, further treatment is not advisable.

    The Duke of Wu Zhengsu experienced heart issues in his youth; after taking this remedy once, he slept for five days before waking and subsequently recovered.[71p]

    Angelica Purging Decoction

    For treating Yang collapse and mania.

    • 1 tael of Angelica
    • 1 tael of Rhubarb
    • 1/2 tael of Licorice
    • 7 qian of Glauber's Salt

    Grind those to the size of broad beans. For every 2 taels, use a large bowl of water, 5 slices of ginger, and 10 jujubes, decocted to half. Remove the dregs and drink warm.

    If Yang energy is excessive, leading to running about, scolding, and not recognizing relatives, this indicates an excess of Yang and a deficiency of Yin. Rhubarb and Glauber's Salt will dispel excess heat from the stomach, Angelica nourishes blood and replenishes Yin, Licorice moderates the middle; ginger and jujubes are included because they belong to Earth, and this helps draw the remedy into the stomach. As the classics say, when the symptoms are mild, go against it; when severe, follow it—this is the principle.

    By taking a significant quantity, with a mild and slow pace, use gourd stem powder, adding Fangfeng powder and Liulian powder to induce vomiting; the illness will quickly settle.     Dried Ginger and Aconite Decoction: Treats cold damage and manic symptoms in yin conditions. Take one liang of dried ginger and one piece of aconite, peeled and broken into eight pieces. Combine these two ingredients with three sheng of water, boil until reduced to one sheng, strain and take immediately.

    Er Bai Pill: Treats diseases caused by phlegm, leading to epilepsy, mania, palpitations, and other symptoms. Use one liang of white alum and a pinch of powdered light mineral, adjusting the amount based on the condition. Wrap in a raw steamy round dough, steam until cooked, peel, form into pills, and roll in the powdered light mineral to the size of the seeds of a phoenix tree. Take two to thirty pills with ginger soup. For children, size should be like millet.

    Bi Xia Pill: Treats phlegm and mucus blockage, urgent jaw tightness, upward eye movement, epilepsy, and mania. Use half a liang of stone green, water-milled nine times, along with twenty pieces each of aconite, Chuan wu, and scorpion tails. Grind these into a powder, mix in with the stone green, form into pills the size of chicken heads. Take one pill dissolved in peppermint soup. Additionally, drink with half a cup of warm wine; shortly afterward, expectorate phlegm, and then treat with other medications according to the symptoms. If the mouth is locked, administer by opening and injecting.[83p]
    Niu Huang Qing Xin Wan treats deficiencies of heart qi, unstable mind, fear and madness, nonsensical speech, restlessness and little sleep, and even cases of abandoning clothes and running away, singing while climbing high, or jumping over walls and roofs, among other symptoms.

    Ingredients include:

    • One tael each of antelope horn, musk, and borneol;
    • Two and a half taels each of ginseng, fried shenqu, and fried cattail pollen;
    • One tael and two qian each of white poria, prepared niuhuang, chaihu, and platycodon;
    • One tael and two and a half qian each of chuanxiong, peeled bitter almond with double kernels, and fried wheat bran;
    • One and a half taels each of defatted astragalus, white peony, and ophiopogon;
    • One and a half taels each of huangqin and prepared danggui (without heads);
    • Seven and a half qian each of fried ejiao, dried ginger, and white renshen;
    • Eight qian of water-fried realgar;
    • Five taels of sliced licorice;
    • Seven taels of fried yam;
    • One and seven and a half taels each of fried soybean yellow rolls and cinnamon (without skin);
    • One thousand four hundred pieces of gold leaf;
    • One hundred steamed black jujubes, peeled and pitted, ground into paste;
    • Two taels of rhinoceros horn.

    Except for the jujubes, almonds, and gold leaf, grind the niuhuang, borneol, musk, and realgar into fine powder, mix with the remaining herbs, incorporate honey into the jujube paste to form pills, making ten pills for every two taels. Encase each with gold leaf. Take one pill after meals with warm water.[84p]
    Ningzhi Huatan Decoction, a recipe by Chen Baiye, treats symptoms of epilepsy and mania caused by heart deficiency and phlegm excess.

    Ingredients:

    • Dandelion

    Clear Heart Nourishing Blood Decoction: Treats heart deficiency and mania.
    Add the following ingredients, each weighing one qian: ginseng, white atractylodes, poria, distant wisdom, fried jujube seed; and each weighing one qian and five fen: angelica sinensis; five fen of licorice. Grind the above into a powder, add five longan fruits, two cups of water, and simmer until reduced to one cup. Consume on an empty stomach.

    He Che Wan: Treats long-term heart wind epilepsy due to deficiency of both qi and blood.
    Use as much purple river car as desired, thoroughly baked and dried. Grind into a powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a wutong seed. Take seventy pills with liquor on an empty stomach.

    Kai Mi San: Treats women's epilepsy, characterized by singing at all times and climbing over walls and roofs, resulting from blood stagnation in the heart membrane.
    Ingredients: each weighing one qian—angelica sinensis, fried white atractylodes, white peony root, sappan wood, safflower; each weighing eight fen—bupleurum, white poria; seven qian of prepared licorice; each weighing one qian and five fen—peach kernel, distant wisdom, fresh rehmannia root. Grind these, decoct with fresh ginger for consumption; alternatively, prepare pills with honey, coated with cinnabar.

    Fang Feng Tong Sheng San: Treats all forms of mania and sudden wind disease.
    Ingredients: each weighing four fen—fang feng, chuanxiong, angelica sinensis, white peony, rhubarb, mirabilite, forsythia; a whole ephedra without removing the nodes; peppermint; each weighing eight fen—gypsum, balloonflower, and yellow qin; two qian and four fen of talc; two fen each of white atractylodes, gardenia seed, and schizonepeta. One qian of prepared licorice. Grind the ingredients, add three slices of fresh ginger, two cups of water, and simmer to one cup. Consume warm.[86p]

    Yujin Pill (from "Liangfang") - Treats heart disturbances and wind-initiated disorders.
    Ingredients:

Those suffering from madness for several years will recover after taking this. When someone first takes it, they may feel a sensation in the chest as if something has been expelled, and after taking it again, they will revive. This condition arises from worry and phlegm obstructing the heart orifices.

    Clearing Heart Decoction: Treats heat evil affecting the heart, making one speak wildly and lose normal movement. Ingredients: equal parts of Huang Lian, Huang Qin, Bo He, Lian Qiao, Zhi Zi Ren, Gan Cao, Da Huang, and Mang Xiao.     Baodan Pills: Treats all types of mania and epilepsy in men and women, as well as postpartum seizures in women, and excessive anxiety in virgins during menstruation. Taking this medicine often yields results. Ingredients: two taels of Zhu Sha, one and a half taels of black lead, finely ground Frankincense, and one tael of mercury. Combine lead in a pan, add mercury to form sand, then add Frankincense and pound evenly with a willow stick while hot. Form pills the size of a chicken egg. Take one pill on an empty stomach with well water. Avoid disturbance during sleep; if you wake up, remain calm. Take another pill to eliminate the root cause.

    Wudang Pills: Treats wild mania and epilepsy that causes wandering thoughts. Ingredients: one piece each of sheep bile, pig bile, dog bile, chicken bile, and carp bile, combined to catch the juice. Five taels of snake gall, calcined red, add the bile juice until the prescribed dose is reached. Grind to powder, and form pills the size of a Mung bean, coated with Zhu Sha. Take fifteen pills after meals, swallowed with sharpened knife juice; alternatively, use the powder mixed with sharpened knife water for ingestion.

    Duomeng Dan: Treats epilepsy with excessive phlegm. Use one tael of Qing Meng Shi mixed with one tael of fire nitrate, refined until golden. Grind to powder, taking one qian at a time, mixed with natural mint juice and honey for ingestion. After a while, the medicine naturally expels phlegm. In severe cases, three doses may cure.[88p]
    Niu Huang Pill treats epilepsy, wind mania, heart wind, evil spirit startling the heart, lack of awareness, episodic outbursts, drooling on the ground, and self-unconsciousness.

    Zheng Xin Decoction treats long-standing emotional disturbances and confusion, heart wind, nonsensical speech and laughter, lack of awareness of suffering.

    Qingxin Pill: Treats heart affected by evil spirits, leading to disorientation, wild talk and shouting, and restless sleep. It consists of one qian each of ginseng, raw rehmannia, turmeric, and tianma; two qian each of zhush
    a and niudan nansheng. Grind to a powder, steam into pills the size of millet, coat with zhush
    a, and take thirty pills with ginseng decoction.

Prepare the amber and horn separately, boil with two dou of water and one liang each of gold and silver until reducing to eight parts, strain, then mix in the powdered amber and horn, and take uniformly.

    Amber and Poria Syrup: Treats loss of spirit, gradually leading to heart wind. It consists of one liang of ginseng, half liang of dried tangerine peel, two liang of angelica (soaked in wine), boiled into a thin syrup; two liang of white poria, ground into powder; half liang of amber, ground separately. Mix the ginseng syrup with the powders of amber and poria until uniform. If too thick, add honey to adjust. Take two to three spoonfuls, chew and swallow, and taking before sleep is also beneficial.[90p]
    Return of the Spirit Elixir

    This remedy treats all cases of fright and anxiety, excessive thinking and forgetfulness, insufficient heart energy, epilepsy, and mania.

    Ingredients:

    • Two pieces of wild boar heart, sliced
    • Two taels of large red cinnabar
    • Three taels of lampwick

    Preparation:
    Combine these ingredients; boil them in a stone pot once. Grind the cinnabar into powder, mix in two taels of Polygala root powder, and form small pills the size of a tung seed. Take them in doses of nine, fifteen, or twenty-five pills, swallowed with Ophiopogon decoction. In severe cases, take with a decoction of frankincense and ginseng.
