    If a woman experiences excessive menstrual bleeding, with blood and qi disturbing the heart, or suffers from postpartum lochia rushing upward leading to disordered speech and mental confusion, this is due to blood deficiency and spirit depletion. It is advisable to use a calming essence balm, but one must avoid solely relying on heart-replenishing and spirit-consolidating medicines. For blood heat, a Xiaochaihu decoction should be prepared with ginger and fresh earth, taken for more than a hundred doses to stabilize.

    If blood confuses the heart covering, causing one to climb the walls and sing at any time, a carefree powder with the addition of distant wisdom, peach kernel, red flower, and su mu should be given. After taking it, if the illness recedes, use a Pingwei powder with less common magnolia bark, but double the amount of Atractylodes and Ascending Peony for regular use to eradicate the root of the illness.

    Furthermore, if a man has stagnant blood, one should use Tao's angelica active blood decoction. If someone experiences acute symptoms resembling cholera, with vomiting and diarrhea, or behaves deliriously like a drunk person, one should know that the issue has arisen from the heart. If deceased and the mouth cannot open, urgently administer the typhoid chasing soul decoction. Externally, the dispelling evil pill should be used for nasal administration.[33p]

    　　　　　伤寒发狂

    　　发狂者，热毒在胃，并入于心，遂使神昏不定，言动急速，妄辨妄笑，甚则登高而歌，弃衣而走，逾墙上屋，不饥不卧，皆因汗下失宜，阳气亢极，阴气暴虚，非大吐下不止。伤寒四五日身热烦躁，不得汗发狂者，表里俱热，三黄石膏汤、双解散。伤寒六七日壮热，胸满便秘，脉实数发狂者，大承气汤加黄连。阳毒暴盛发狂，多干呕，面赤发斑，咽痛，下利黄赤，壮热而不得汗者，葶苈苦酒汤。咽痛吐脓血者，阳毒升麻汤。潮热甚者，栀子仁汤。潮热大便闭者，升麻葛根汤加大黄，或三黄汤。发斑不可下者，草龙胆一味，水煎服。狂走者瓜蒂散吐痰。时行热毒发狂者，黑奴丸，通用水渍法、火劫法、王氏元明粉。凡发狂见阳证阳脉者顺，见阴证阴脉及舌卷囊缩者即死。[34p]

    Frigid Fever Madness

    Madness occurs when the heat and toxins enter the stomach and combine with the heart, leading to confusion of the mind, rapid speech and action, nonsensical discernment and laughter. In severe cases, one may sing atop high places, discard clothing and run, leap over walls and roofs, with no hunger or sleep, all due to inappropriate sweating, excessive yang energy, and a violent deficiency of yin. This is not remedied without significant purging.

    In cases of cold damage lasting four to five days with body heat and agitation, and one cannot sweat leading to madness, both exterior and interior present with heat; the treatment is San Huang Shi Gao Tang or Shuang Jie San.

    In cases of cold damage lasting six to seven days with strong heat, chest fullness, constipation, and a strong, rapid pulse leading to madness, the remedy is Da Cheng Qi Tang plus Huang Lian.

    When yang toxicity abounds causing madness, with much dry heaving, a red face with spots, sore throat, and yellow or red diarrhea, along with strong heat and inability to sweat, the treatment is Ting Li Ku Jiu Tang.

    If there is a sore throat with phlegm and blood, treat with Yang Du Sheng Ma Tang. For severe tidal heat, use Zhi Zi Ren Tang. If tidal heat comes with constipation, the treatment is Sheng Ma Ge Gen Tang plus Da Huang, or San Huang Tang.

    For rashes that should not be purged, use Cao Long Dan alone, boiled in water. For those who run wildly, use Gua Di San to induce vomiting of phlegm.

    In seasonal heat toxicity leading to madness, use Hei Nu Wan while employing both water soaking methods, fire scorching methods, and Wang’s Yuan Ming Powder.

    In all cases of madness presenting with yang symptoms and pulse, treatment should proceed cautiously; if encountering yin symptoms, yin pulse, or a curled tongue and contracted throat, it indicates imminent death.[34p]

    　　　　　如狂

    　　有阴盛发躁，欲坐井地如狂者；有火邪，惊惕不安如狂者。然如狂有三证，与阳毒如狂相似，故举言之。　　如狂属瘀血者，脉沉实，多漱水不咽，有无表证，但血蓄下焦，小便自利如狂者；有无表里证，脉数善饥不大便如狂者；有太阳初证，热结下焦如狂者，血自下者即愈。如外未解者桂枝汤、陶氏桂苓饮；外已解但小腹急结者，桃仁承气汤；挟血传心脾者，当归活血汤。有太阴身黄，溺濇如狂者，五苓散。此皆如狂，但睡中或欲起行，错言妄语，犹知谏阻，尚可制御，非若发狂势凶，莫能御也。[35p]

    Like Madness

    There are those with excessive yin causing agitation, wanting to sit in the well like a madman; there are those affected by fire, alarmed and restless like a madman. Nevertheless, there are three signs of madness that resemble the madness induced by yang poison, which is why they are mentioned.

    Madness due to the stagnation of blood presents with a deep and solid pulse, frequent rinsing of the mouth without swallowing, showing no outward symptoms; yet blood is accumulated in the lower part of the body, and urination is smooth like madness. With or without exterior and interior symptoms, if the pulse is rapid, good appetite but no bowel movement, it is like madness.

    In the initial signs of taiyang, heat is trapped in the lower part of the body like madness, and if blood flows downward, recovery follows. If the exterior has not been resolved, use Guizhi Decoction or Tao’s Gui Ling Drink; if the exterior has cleared but with urgent distension in the lower abdomen, use Taoren Chengqi Decoction; if there is blood affecting the heart and spleen, use Danggui Huoxue Decoction.

    If there is taiyin with a yellowish hue and cloudy urination like madness, use Wuling Powder. All these conditions are akin to madness; however, if in sleep one wishes to rise and walk, speaking erratically, still knowing to advise against it, this can still be controlled. It is different from the fierceness of true madness, which cannot be restrained.[35p]

    　　　　古今医统 【明　徐春甫】

    　　　　　癫狂有同异之分

    　　癫狂之病，总为心火所乘，神不守舍，一言尽矣。癫者至高也，火性炎上，正如经云阳气太上则狂癫，狂则孔子所谓狂狷者之狂也。《灵枢经》曰：狂病始发，少卧不饥，自高贤也，自辨智也，自尊贵也，故曰狂者进取，志大而言大者也。前谓狂言如有所见，斯得之矣。盖心火暴炽，言语善恶，不避亲疏，此神明之乱也，此之所谓狂也。盖谓火炽之甚，阳气太上，则病人亦乘阳火之上炎，故弃衣而登高，由狂而又癫，此则圣人命名之义而有同中之异耳。
    　　　　　癫痫辨混同之误[36p]

    In ancient and modern medical teachings, the distinction between madness and insanity is discussed.

    The illness of madness is primarily driven by excessive heart fire, causing the spirit to lose its residence; this sums it up. Madness reaches its peak; fire has an upward nature, just as the classics state that when the Yang energy is excessively elevated, it leads to madness. The “Ling Shu” states: when the disease of madness begins, there is little sleep and lack of appetite, arising from a sense of superiority, self-knowledge, and self-worth. Thus, the mad are driven to pursue, speaking grandly and with great ambition. Previously, it was said that insane speech appears as though they have seen something; indeed, this arises from extreme heart fire where words may mix good and evil, showing no regard for closeness or distance; this is the chaos of the spirit, which is termed madness. It indicates that when the fire is exceedingly intense and Yang energy is too elevated, the patient also rides on this fiery ascent, hence they discard their garments and climb heights, transitioning from madness to insanity. This is a way the sages have named a phenomenon that shares similarities but also has differences within.[36p]

    　　古方每以癫痫并治出方，乃大误也。盖癫为心病而属实者多，痫为五脏兼病而属虚者多。盖因《灵枢》云：癫痫瘈瘲，不知所苦，后人不察，遂认为一证。殊不知《灵枢》癫痫自以两证而言。不知所苦，皆言不能自知其病之所苦也。《玉机微义》始分别之，而亦未尝白《灵枢》之旨也。
    　　　　　治法当分

    　　登高弃衣，引重致远者为癫，乃痰火亢炽之甚而然，治宜降下之剂，滚痰丸之属是也。　　自高辨智，妄语狂言，神明失守为狂，治宜镇心安神，清上之剂，牛黄朱砂丸之属是也。
    　　　　　心风证治

    　　心风病，诸书鲜有载之，而多附癫痫门，混同论治。心风虽出于世俗之称，深中病情，诚为切当。古人谓风善行而数变，风痹为不仁。此曰心风者，非若外风入中，甚言其变常无定，恍惚不仁，而心之病诚若风之魔也。此皆七情五志，久逆所生，而与癫痫则又不同矣。癫狂痫证主于火炽，风痰之盛，涎及于心，属实者多。[37p]

    In ancient medicine, treating epilepsy and insanity with the same formula is a great error. Insanity is primarily a disease of the heart and often arises from excess, while epilepsy involves multiple organ systems and tends to be of a deficiency nature. The "Lingshu" states that insanity, epilepsy, and seizures are labels for conditions where one does not understand their suffering; later practitioners misinterpreted this as a single condition. However, the "Lingshu" discusses insanity and epilepsy as distinct conditions. The phrase “not knowing one's suffering” refers to a lack of awareness of the exact nature of the ailment.

    Treatment methodologies should be differentiated.

    High elevation and shedding of clothing, which leads to excessive weight and distance, are linked to insanity; the treatment should focus on reducing and eliminating phlegm and excessive fire, utilizing methods like rolling phlegm pills. In contrast, those who become overly discerning, speak irrationally, and lose their mental acuity are experiencing mania; the treatment should stabilize the heart and calm the spirit, employing methods such as pills of cow bile and vermilion.

    Regarding heart wind diseases, few texts provide detailed accounts and many confuse them with epilepsy, treating them indistinctly. Although "heart wind" appears to be a term from the secular realm, it truly reflects serious illness. The ancients noted that wind moves swiftly and with various changes; wind causing paralysis is unaffectionate. 'Heart wind' does not refer to external wind invading the interior, but rather signifies an internal change that is erratic and unkind, akin to a demonic infestation of the heart. This condition typically arises from long-term emotional strife and differs significantly from epilepsy. Epilepsy and mania are primarily characterized by intense heat and abundant wind-phlegm, with an overflow affecting the heart, which is often a condition of excess.[37p]

    心风则由七情五志，久逆不遂，戴人所谓肝屡谋，胆屡不决，屈无所申，怒无所泄，心之官则思，甚则心血日涸，脾液不行，痰迷心窍，则成心风，属虚者多。治法须以七情相胜，五志遂心，养血豁痰，引神归舍，标本兼治，此疾可愈矣。至若混同癫痫攻治，是谓虚虚而速其死也，噫！　　心风初作，多属虚候。何则？思虑伤脾，则谷气寖少，血液日亏，则心神漫散，神不守舍，卒成心风，故知其始皆属虚也，归脾汤、养心汤、定志丸之类。至于病久，则心志变而美恶不知，无思无虑，饮食如故，杀　　气颇增，病根已固。郁痰不解者，可用子和法治之，随证调理，无不愈也。[38p]

    When the heart wind arises, it is caused by the seven emotions and five desires being persistently thwarted. The liver often schemes, the gallbladder is frequently indecisive, and feelings have no outlet. The heart’s function is thought, and if this becomes severe, the heart’s blood diminishes daily, the spleen's fluids do not circulate, and phlegm obstructs the heart's orifices, leading to the formation of heart wind, which is mostly of a vacuous nature. The treatment must counter the seven emotions, fulfill the five desires, nourish the blood, clear phlegm, and bring the spirit back to the residence, addressing both the root and branches; this condition can be cured.

    However, if one confuses this with epilepsy and hastily treats it, that is to invite an accelerated demise. Oh! When heart wind first manifests, it often pertains to a vacuous condition. Why is this? Excessive thinking harms the spleen, leading to diminished essence, daily depletion of blood, and the spirit becomes dispersed, no longer residing in its abode, which suddenly results in heart wind. Thus, it is known that its beginnings are all related to vacuity— prescriptions like Gui Pi Decoction, Yang Xin Decoction, and Ding Zhi Pill can be applied.

    As for prolonged illness, the heart’s intentions change, leading to ignorance of beauty and ugliness, thoughts and worries disappear, and dietary habits remain the same, while aggressive energies increase, solidifying the roots of the disease. For those who have unresolved phlegm stagnation, the Zihua Method can be used for treatment, adjusting according to the symptoms, and nothing will fail to cure.[38p]

    　　　　　贵贱系难易

    　　心风病，贵者为难。膏粱素积，耗散良多，一经病作，则正气虚而邪气盛，所以难。贱者为易。素甘淡薄，禀受颇厚，虽是病此，则正气实而邪气轻，所以易。
    　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

    　　　　　总论

    　　《素问》止言癫而不及痫，《灵枢》乃有痫瘈、痫厥之名。诸书有言癫狂者，有言癫痫者，有言风痫者，有言惊痫者，有分癫痫为二门者，迄无定论。究其独言癫者，祖《素问》也；言癫痫，言癫狂者，祖《灵枢》也。要之癫痫狂，大相径庭，非名殊而实一之谓也。《灵枢》虽编癫狂为一门，而形证两具，取治异途，较之于痫，又不侔矣。徐嗣伯曰：大人曰癫，小儿曰痫。亦不然也。[39p]

    On Wealth and Poverty in Relation to Difficulty and Ease

    The heart and mind disease is difficult for the wealthy. Those with rich and extravagant diets accumulate excess, and when illness strikes, their righteous energy is weak while pathogenic energy is strong, making it hard to cure. For the poor, it is easier. They have a simple and sparse diet, and their constitution is generally robust; even if they fall ill, their righteous energy remains abundant while pathogenic energy is light, making it easier to treat.

    General Discussion

    The "Suwen" only mentions mania without addressing epilepsy, whereas the "Lingshu" includes names for epilepsy and seizures. Various texts refer to mania in different ways—some mention madness, some refer to epilepsy, and others speak of wind-associated epilepsy or shock-related epilepsy, with divisions within epilepsy itself, yet none provide a definitive conclusion. Those who solely mention mania trace back to the "Suwen"; discussions on epilepsy or madness originate from the "Lingshu." Importantly, mania and epilepsy are fundamentally different; it is not merely a case of differing terminologies but of distinct conditions. Although the "Lingshu" classifies mania and madness under one category, their manifestations are twofold, and their treatment varies, thus they differ significantly from epilepsy. Xu Sibo stated: adults have mania while children have epilepsy. However, this distinction is not entirely accurate.[39p]

    《素问》谓癫为母腹中受惊所致，今乃曰小儿无癫可乎？痫病大人每每有之，妇人尤多。今据经文分辨于后。　　癫者，或狂或愚，或歌或笑，或悲或泣，如醉如痴，言语有头无尾，秽洁不知，积年累月不愈，俗呼心风，此志愿高而不遂所欲者多有之。　　狂者病之发时，猖狂刚暴，如伤寒阳明大宁发狂，骂詈不避亲疏，甚则登高而歌，弃衣而走，逾垣上屋，非力所能，或与人语所未尝见之事，如有邪依附者是也。　　痫病发则昏不知人，眩仆倒地，不省高下，甚而瘈瘲抽掣，目上视，或口眼喎斜，或口作六畜之声。古今图书集成医部全录卷二百九十六[40p]

    The "Suwen" states that madness comes from the shock received in the mother’s womb. Now, can we say that children do not have madness? The elderly frequently experience fits, and women are particularly affected. Based on the texts, we will distinguish further below.

    Madness can manifest as either wildness or foolishness, sometimes as singing or laughing, other times as sorrow or weeping, resembling drunkenness or daze. Their speech lacks coherence, and they are oblivious to cleanliness or filth. This state lasts for many years without recovery, commonly referred to as "heart wind," which often occurs in those whose aspirations are high but whose desires are unmet.

    During a fit of madness, the patient is often frenzied and violent, similar to how one with a fever might behave, shouting and cursing indiscriminately, regardless of kinship. In severe cases, they may climb to heights and sing, discard their clothes and run, leap over walls and rooftops, acting beyond their physical strength or speaking of things they have never witnessed—this indicates an evil influence attaching to them.

    When epilepsy strikes, individuals may become disoriented, unable to recognize people, dizzy, and may collapse, completely unconscious of their surroundings. In severe instances, they may experience convulsions and rigidity, their eyes rolling upwards, or their mouths and eyes skewed, sometimes producing sounds akin to that of livestock.[40p]

    癫狂门

    　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

    　　　　　论证

    　　癫狂之病，病本不同。狂病之来，狂妄以渐而经久难已；癫病之至，忽然僵仆，而时作时止。狂病常醒，多怒而暴；癫病常昏，多倦而静。由此观之，则其阴阳寒热，自有冰炭之异。故《难经》曰：重阳者狂，重阴者癫。义可知也。后世诸家有谓癫狂之病，大概是热，此则未必然也。此其形气脉气，亦自有据，不可不辨察阴阳分而治之。　　癫，即痫也，观《内经》所言癫证甚详，而痫则无辨，即此可知。后世有癫痫、风痫、风癫等名，所指不一，则徒滋惑乱，不必然也。又如《别录》所载五痫，曰马痫，牛痫、猪痫、羊痫、鸡痫者，即今人之谓羊癫、猪癫也。此不过因其声之相似，遂立此名。可见癫痫无二，而诸家于癫证之外，又有痫证，诚属牵强，无足凭也。又《千金方》有风痫、惊痫、食痫及阴痫、阳痫之说，皆所当辨。[41p]

    The Door of Madness

    From "The Complete Book of Jingyue" by Zhang Jiebin (Ming Dynasty)

    Discussion and Evidence

    The diseases of madness and epilepsy are fundamentally different. The onset of manic illness develops gradually through prolonged delusions; whereas, the onset of epilepsy occurs suddenly, with moments of rigidity and intermittent episodes. Individuals with mania are often conscious, quick to anger, and violent; whereas those with epilepsy frequently experience confusion, fatigue, and tranquility. From this perspective, the distinctions in aspects of yin and yang, as well as cold and heat, are evident. Thus, the "Nan Jing" states: "The prevalence of yang indicates mania, while the prevalence of yin suggests epilepsy." This meaning is clear. Later generations of scholars have proposed that both mania and epilepsy are generally caused by heat, but this is not necessarily the case. The characteristics of qi and pulse also have their own basis, and one must carefully differentiate and treat them according to the principles of yin and yang.

    Epilepsy is indeed the same as "dian." In the "Inner Canon," the description of the dian ailment is very detailed, while the distinction of "xian" (epilepsy) is unclear, which can be observed from this. Later generations have used terms like "epileptic fits," "wind epilepsy," and "wind dian," which refer to different meanings and only serve to cause confusion, not necessarily providing clarity. For instance, "Bie Lu" mentions five types of "xian": horse epilepsy, bovine epilepsy, porcine epilepsy, ovine epilepsy, and chicken epilepsy, which correspond to what is now called sheep and pig epilepsy. This naming is merely due to phonetic similarity and lacks substantial ground. Therefore, epilepsy is singular, while various schools have added further distinctions outside the dian syndrome but also considered as "xian," which truly appears forced and lacks sufficient evidence. Additionally, "Qian Jin Fang" mentions concepts of wind epilepsy, fright epilepsy, food-induced epilepsy, as well as yin and yang epilepsy, which all require discernment.[41p]

    　　　　　论治

    　　凡狂病多因于火，此或以谋为失志，或以思虑郁结，屈无所伸，怒无所泄，以致肝胆气逆，木火合邪，是诚东方实证也。此其邪乘于心则为神魂不守，邪乘于胃则为暴横刚强，故治此者当以洽火为先，而或痰或气，察其甚而兼治之。若止因火邪而无胀闭热结者，但当清火，宜抽薪饮、黄连解毒汤、三补丸之类主之。若水不制火，而兼心肾微虚者，宜朱砂安神丸，或服蛮煎、二阴煎主之。若阳明火盛者，宜白虎汤、玉泉散之类主之。若心脾受热，叫骂失常而微兼闭结者，宜清心汤、凉膈散、三黄丸、当归龙荟丸之类主之。若因火致痰者，宜清膈饮、抱龙丸、生铁落饮主之，甚者宜滚痰丸。若三焦邪实热甚者，宜大承气汤下之。[42p]

    On Treatment

    Generally, manic conditions are often caused by fire. This may stem from ambitions leading to loss of spirit, or from worries and repressed emotions, where one feels constrained with no outlet for anger. This results in the liver and gallbladder's energy becoming rebellious, with the combination of wood and fire creating a harmful influence, which indeed reflects Eastern practical evidence. When this harmful influence affects the heart, it results in the spirit not being anchored; when it affects the stomach, it leads to violent and aggressive behaviors. Therefore, those treating this should prioritize harmonizing fire, and depending on whether phlegm or qi is involved, they should examine the severity and treat both. If the issue is solely due to fire without swelling, obstruction, or heat accumulation, it is simply necessary to clear the fire. Treatments like "Withdraw the Fuel Decoction," "Huanglian Jiedu Decoction," or "Sanbu Pill" should be used. If water does not control fire and there is a slight deficiency in both heart and kidney, "Zhusha Anshen Pill," or herbal preparations like "Manjiao Decoction" and "Er Yin Decoction" should be used. If the yangming fire is excessive, "Baihu Decoction" or "Yuqian Powder" is recommended. If both the heart and spleen are overheated, with unusual outbursts and slight blockage, "Qingxin Decoction," "Liangge Powder," "Sanhuang Pill," or "Danggui Longhui Pill" should be used. If fire causes phlegm, "Qingge Drink," "Baolong Pill," or "Shengtie Luo Drink" should be used, with "Gun Tan Pill" for severe cases. If the three burners are affected by severe heat, "Da Chengqi Decoction" should be administered.[42p]

    若痰饮壅闭，气道不通者，必须先用吐法，并当清其饮食。此治狂之要也。　　癫病多由痰起。凡气有所逆，痰有所滞，皆能壅闭经络，格塞心窍，故发则旋晕僵仆，口眼相引，目睛上视，手足搐搦，腰脊强直，食顷乃苏。此其倏病倏已者，正由气之倏逆倏顺也。故治此者当察痰察气，因其甚者而先治之。若火之有无，又当审其脉证而兼为之治也。气滞者，宜排气饮、大和中饮、四磨饮，或牛黄丸、苏合丸、集成润下丸之类主之。痰盛者，宜清膈饮、六安煎、二陈汤、橘皮半夏汤，或抱龙丸、朱砂滚涎丸之类主之。兼痰兼火者，宜清膈饮、朱砂安神丸、丹溪润下丸之类主之。痰逆气滞之甚者，必用吐法，吐后随证调理之。　　癫痫证无火者多。若无火邪，不得妄用凉药，恐伤脾气以致变生他证。[43p]

    If phlegm and fluid obstruct the pathways and obstruct the flow of Qi, one must first use methods to induce vomiting and also clear dietary factors. This is essential for treating mania.

    Epileptic conditions often arise from phlegm. Whenever there is a reversal of Qi or stagnation of phlegm, it can obstruct the meridians and block the heart's gateways, leading to symptoms such as sudden fainting, drooping of the mouth and eyes, upward rolling of the eyeballs, spasms of the hands and feet, rigidity of the waist and spine, and recovery only after a while. This sudden onset and resolution of symptoms is due to the erratic flow of Qi.

    Thus, for treatment, one should examine the phlegm and the Qi, prioritizing the more severe condition. If there is an issue of fire, one should also assess the pulse and clinical manifestations and treat accordingly. For Qi stagnation, it is advisable to use methods such as Qi-releasing drinks, harmonizing drinks, or formulations like Niuhuang Wan, Suhe Wan, or Jicheng Runxia Wan. For excessive phlegm, it is suitable to use drinks that clear the diaphragm, Liugan Decoction, Erchen Decoction, or Chenpi Banxia Decoction, or formulations like Baolong Wan and Zhushayunxian Wan. For cases with both phlegm and fire, use drinks that clear the diaphragm, Zhushay Anshen Wan, or Danqi Runxia Wan. For severe cases of phlegm reversing and Qi stagnation, one must use methods to induce vomiting and then adjust treatment according to the symptoms afterward.

    Epileptic symptoms without fire are more common. If there is no fire pathogen, one should not recklessly use cooling medicines, for fear of harming the spleen Qi and causing the emergence of other conditions.[43p]

    且复有阴盛阳衰，及气血暴脱而绝无痰火气逆等病者，则凡四君、四物、八珍、十全大补等汤，或干姜、桂、附之类，皆所必用，不得谓癫痫尽属实邪，而概禁补剂也。若真阴大损，气不归根，而时作时止，昏沉难愈者，必用紫河车丸，方可奏效。其有虚中挟实，微兼痰火不清而病久不愈者，集验龙脑安神丸，最得其宜，随证增减，可为法也。　　痴呆证，凡平素无痰而或以郁结，或以不遂，或以思虑，或以疑贰，或以惊恐而渐致痴呆，言辞颠倒，举动不经，或多汗，或善愁，其证则千奇万怪，无所不至，脉必或弦或数，或大或小，变易不常。此其逆气在心，或肝胆二经气有不清而然，但察其形体强壮，饮食不减，别无虚脱等证，则悉宜服蛮煎治之，最稳最妙。[44p]

    Furthermore, if there are conditions of excessive yin and declining yang, or if there is a sudden loss of qi and blood with absolutely no phlegm, heat, or rebellious qi, then prescriptions such as the Four Gentlemen, Four Substances, Eight Treasures, or Ten Complete Great Supplements are essential. Additionally, ingredients like dried ginger, cinnamon, and aconite must be used; one should not claim that epilepsy is entirely due to true evil and thus prohibit tonics. If there is a significant loss of true yin and qi does not return to its roots, leading to intermittent symptoms that are hard to cure and accompanied by cloudiness, one must use Ziheche Pill to achieve effectiveness. For those with a mixture of deficiency and excess, with mild phlegm-heat complicating a long-standing illness, the Lingnao Anshen Pill is most appropriate; adjustments can be made based on symptoms.

    In cases of dementia, where there is usually no phlegm but could be due to emotional distress, unsatisfied desires, overthinking, ambivalence, or fear leading to gradual onset of dementia—with disordered speech, inappropriate actions, excessive sweating, or a tendency to worry—the manifestations can be numerous and peculiar. The pulse will typically be either wiry or rapid, large or small, changing frequently. If the reverse qi is in the heart, or if the liver and gallbladder channels have unclear qi, but the person appears strong in body, with no decrease in appetite, and lacks signs of collapse, then it is advisable to use Mianjian (a herbal decoction) for treatment; this is the most stable and effective approach.[44p]

    然此证有可愈者，有不可愈者，亦在乎胃气元气之强弱，待时而复，非可急也。凡此诸证，若以大惊猝恐，一时偶伤心胆，而致失神昏乱者，此当以速扶正气为主，宜七福饮，或大补元煎主之。　　小儿无狂证，惟病癫者常有之。凡小儿之病，有从胎气而得者，有从产后受惊而得者。盖小儿神气尚弱，惊则肝胆夺气，而神不守舍，舍空则正气不能主，而痰邪足以乱之。故治小儿之惊痫，必先审正气，然后察其病邪，酌宜治之。诸法俱载小儿门。　　愚按《千金方》论小儿风惊食三痫，陈无择论痫病由于三因之说，虽若切当，然风寒外感自有表证，饮食内伤自有里证，俱未必乱神若此。而癫痫为病，则忽尔昏厥，此其病则专在心经，以及肝胆二脏，又非风寒饮食所能顿病若此者。且风痫之义，本以木邪所属为言，亦非外感之谓。即有外感，或有饮食，亦无非因惊因恐相兼为病耳。若以三因并列之，则有未必然也。[45p]

    However, this condition has both those that can be cured and those that cannot, depending on the strength of the stomach and vital energy. Recovery must await the right time; it cannot be rushed. In cases where great fear suddenly injures the heart and gallbladder, leading to confusion and loss of spirit, the primary treatment should focus on quickly restoring the vital energy. The Qifuding or the Great Tonic Decoction can be used for this.

    For children, they do not typically show symptoms of mania, but they often suffer from epilepsy. Children's illnesses may arise from prenatal influences or from being frightened after birth. Children’s spirits are relatively weak; when frightened, the liver and gallbladder lose their essence and the spirit cannot maintain residence. If the residence is empty, the vital energy cannot govern, allowing phlegm and evil influences to disrupt it. Thus, in treating children’s fright and seizures, one must first assess the vital energy, then examine the nature of the illnesses, and treat them accordingly. All methods are documented in pediatric texts.

    I opine that "Qianjin Fang" discusses the conditions of childhood fright, shock, and epilepsy. Chen Wuze discusses the causes of epilepsy based on three factors, which, although precise, imply that external wind and cold lead to manifest symptoms, while internal injury from food leads to latent symptoms; neither necessarily disrupts the spirit to this extent. Epilepsy, as a disease, is characterized by sudden fainting, particularly concerning the heart and the liver and gallbladder. It is not something that can simply arise from wind, cold, or diet. Moreover, the concept of wind-related epilepsy primarily pertains to influences of the wood element and is not described as an external affliction. Even if there are external influences or dietary issues, they are also due to the combination of fright and fear causing illness. If one lists these three causes together, it does not necessarily follow that they are equivalent.[45p]

    　　　　　伤寒发狂

    　　伤寒发狂，本阳明实热之病。然复有如狂证者，虽似狂而实非狂，此中虚实相反，最宜详辨，不可忽也。凡实热之狂，本属阳明。盖阳明为多气多血之经，阳邪传入胃腑，热结不解，因而发狂。《内经》阳明脉解篇曰：胃者土也，故闻木音而惊者，土恶木也。其恶火者，热甚则恶火也。其恶人者，以阳明厥则喘而惋，惋则恶人也。其病甚则弃衣而走，登高而歌，或数日不食，或逾垣上屋者，以四肢为诸阳之本，阳盛则四肢实，实则能登高也。其弃衣而走者，以热甚于身也。其妄言骂詈，不避亲疏而歌者，以阳盛为邪也。又曰：阴不胜其阳，则脉流薄疾，并乃狂。又曰：邪入于阳则狂。[46p]

    Heat Stroke and Mania

    Heat stroke and mania arise from a true heat disease of the Yangming channel. However, there are cases that resemble mania yet are not genuinely so; this distinction between false and true must be carefully analyzed and not overlooked. In instances of true heat mania, it belongs to the Yangming channel. This is because the Yangming channel is characterized by abundant qi and blood. When the pathogenic heat enters the stomach and intestines, and the heat accumulates without resolution, mania ensues. The "Inner Canon" states that the stomach is associated with earth, and thus it is startled by the sound of wood, as earth is antagonistic to wood. When the fire is harmful, excessive heat causes serious harm. Those suffering extreme illness may shed their clothes and flee, sing atop heights, or go several days without food; this is because the limbs are the foundation of all Yang, and when Yang is vigorous, the limbs are solid and capable of climbing heights. Shedding clothes and fleeing happens due to excessive heat affecting the body. Uttering nonsensical statements, cursing without concern for kin or distance while singing, indicates that excessive Yang has become pathological. It is also said that when yin cannot withstand yang, the pulse becomes thin and swift, leading to mania. Furthermore, when pathogens invade the Yang, mania results.[46p]

    是皆以阳明热邪上乘心肺，故令神志昏乱若此。此阳狂也。然伤寒病至发狂，是为邪热已极，使非峻逐火邪则不能已。故但察其大便鞕结，或腹满而坚，有可攻之证，则宜以大小承气，或凉膈散、六一顺气汤之类下之可也。如无胀满实坚等证，而惟胃火致然者，则但以白虎汤、抽薪饮之类泄去火邪，其病自愈。　　如狂证本非实热发狂，其证亦有轻重。如仲景曰：太阳病不解，热结膀胱，其人如狂，其外不解者，尚未可攻，当先解外；外已解，但少腹急结者，乃可攻之，宜桃仁承气汤。又曰：太阳病六七日，表证仍在，脉微而沉，反不结胸，其人如狂者，以热在下焦，少腹当鞕满，小便自利者，下其血乃愈，抵当汤主之。[47p]

    This condition arises from the invasion of Yangming heat that ascends to disrupt the heart and lungs, resulting in confusion of spirit and mind. This is called Yang madness. However, when a person with a cold illness exhibits madness, it indicates that the heat pathogen has reached an extreme, and without vigorously expelling this fiery pathogen, it cannot be resolved. Thus, if one observes signs of constipation or a firm, distended abdomen, with indications to attack, it is appropriate to use methods such as the Da Xian Chui Qi (Da Xiao Cheng Qi) as well as Liang Ge San or Liu Yi Shun Qi Decoction to purge. If there are no signs of distension or firmness, and it is solely due to gastric fire, then one should simply use Bai Hu Tang or Chou Xin Yin to drain the fire pathogen, and the illness will recover on its own.

    If the madness is not due to actual heat, there can be varying degrees of symptoms. As Zhang Zhongjing states: "In cases of Taiyang disease that has not resolved, if heat has settled in the bladder, the person may appear mad, but if the exterior has not yet been resolved, it is not advisable to attack; one must first resolve the exterior. If the exterior has been resolved and there is only urgency in the lower abdomen, then it is appropriate to attack, and one should use the Tao Ren Cheng Qi Tang." He also says: "In Taiyang disease that lasts six or seven days with exterior symptoms still present, when the pulse is weak and profound, and there is no sensation of fullness in the chest—if the person appears mad, this indicates heat in the lower jiao, with the lower abdomen likely feeling distended and urination flowing freely; in such a case, one should drain the blood to enable recovery, as indicated by Di Dang Tang."[47p]

    按此二条以太阳热邪不解，随经入腑，但未至发狂，故曰如狂。此以热搏血分，蓄聚下焦，故宜下也。　　近见伤寒家则别有如狂之证，古人所未及言者。盖或由失志而病，其病在心也；或由悲忧而病，其病在肺也；或由失精而病，其病在肾也；或由劳倦思虑而病，其病在肝脾也。此其本病已伤于内，而寒邪复感于外，则病必随邪而起矣。其证如狂，亦所谓虚狂也。而虚狂之证，必外无黄赤之色，刚暴之气，内无胸腹之结，滑实之脉，虽或不时躁扰，而禁之则止，口多妄诞而声息不壮，或眼见虚空，或惊惶不定，察其上则口无焦渴，察其下则便无鞕结，是皆精气受伤，神魂不守之证，此与阳极为狂者，反如冰炭。[48p]

    According to these two points, if the heat of the sun's evil does not dissipate and enters the organs through the channels, but does not lead to true madness, it is therefore described as “like madness.” This is because the heat attacks the blood aspect and accumulates in the lower regions, hence it should be cleared downward.

    Recently, I have observed in cases of typhus that there are also symptoms resembling madness, which ancient scholars did not mention. This may derive from loss of ambition, affecting the heart; or from sorrow and worry, affecting the lungs; or from loss of essence, affecting the kidneys; or from exhaustion due to overthinking, affecting the liver and spleen. When the root condition has already damaged the interior, and the cold evil affects from the outside, then the illness inevitably arises with the evil influence. The symptoms appear as madness, which is also referred to as “false madness.”

    However, the signs of false madness must not display a yellow or red complexion, nor exhibit violent temperament; internally, there should be no obstruction in the chest and abdomen, and the pulse should not be slippery or solid. Although there may be intermittent agitation, if restrained, it will cease. The mouth may often speak nonsensically, and the voice will be weak. There may be visions of emptiness or a state of anxiety and instability. If we examine the upper part, the mouth will not be scorched with thirst, and if we examine the lower part, there will be no constipation. All these indicate that the essence and qi are injured, and the spirit and mind are not anchored. This condition contrasts sharply with true madness caused by extreme yang, much like the difference between ice and fire.[48p]

    而时医不能察，但见错乱便谓阳狂，妄行攻泻，必致杀人。凡治此者，须辨阴阳。其有虚而挟邪者，邪在阳分，则宜补中益气汤之类；邪在阴分，则宜补阴益气煎之类。虚而无邪者，在阳分，则宜四君、八珍、十全大补汤大补元煎之类；在阴分，则宜四物、六味、左归饮、一阴煎之类。阴虚挟火者，宜加减一阴煎、二阴煎之类；阳虚挟寒者，宜理中汤、回阳饮、八味汤、右归饮之类等方治之。然大略如此，而变证之异，则有言不能传者。能知意在言表，则知所未言矣。　　凡身有微热，或面赤带黄，或烦躁不宁，欲坐卧于泥水中，然脉则微弱无力，此阴证似阳也，名为阴躁。盖以阳虚于下，则气不归原，故浮散于上而发躁如狂，速当温补其下，命门暖则火有所归，而病当自愈。若医不识此，而误用寒凉者，必死。[49p]

    At times, doctors cannot discern the condition, and upon seeing chaos, they mistakenly label it as Yang frenzy, leading to reckless purging which surely results in death. In treating this, one must differentiate between Yin and Yang. If there is deficiency combined with pathogenic factors, and the pathogen resides in the Yang aspect, then one should use remedies like the Middle-Replenishing and Qi-Increasing Decoction; if it is in the Yin aspect, remedies like the Yin-Replenishing and Qi-Increasing Decoction are appropriate. If there is deficiency without pathogens and it is in the Yang aspect, then one should use formulas such as the Four Gentlemen, Eight Treasures, or the Complete Great Replenishing Decoction; if in the Yin aspect, use formulas like the Four Substances, Six Flavors, Left Gui Decoction, or the One Yin Decoction. In cases of Yin deficiency with fire, one should add or modify the One Yin Decoction or the Two Yin Decoction; for Yang deficiency with cold, remedies such as the Regulating Middle Decoction, Resuming Yang Drink, Eight Flavor Decoction, or Right Gui Decoction should be employed. This is a general outline; however, there are different manifestations that cannot be fully communicated in words. Understanding the intention behind the words allows one to grasp what has not been said.

    If there is slight heat in the body, or a yellowish-red face, or restlessness with a desire to sit or lie in muddy water, yet the pulse is weak and lacking strength, this resembles a Yin condition manifesting as Yang, termed Yin agitation. This occurs because Yang deficiency below prevents the Qi from returning to its source, causing it to float and disperse above, resulting in agitation like madness. Therefore, one must promptly warm and tonify below; when the life gate is warmed, the fire will return to its source, and the illness will naturally resolve. If a doctor does not recognize this and mistakenly uses cold treatments, death is inevitable.[49p]

    　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈士铎】

    　　　　　癫病治法

    　　癫痫之证，亦累岁经年而未愈，乃痰入于心窍之间而不能出，喜食炭者，盖心火为痰所迷，不得发泄，炭乃火之余，与心火气味相投，病人食之，其甘如饴也。方用人参一两，南星、鬼箭、柴胡、白芍各三钱，附子、肉桂各一钱，半夏、菖蒲、丹砂末各二钱，先将前药煎汤二碗，分作二服，将丹砂一半调入药中，与病人服之。彼不肯服，即以炭给之，服了与汝炭吃，彼必欣然服之。索炭，也不妨仍与之炭。第二服亦如前法，则彼不若前之欣然，当令人急灌之。不听不妨打之，以动其怒气，怒则肝木火起以生心，反能去痰矣。　　癫痫之病，虽时常食物，肠中有水谷之气，可以养生不死，亦其心之不死也。[50p]

    Secret Formula of the Stone Chamber [Qing Dynasty, Chen Shiduo]

    Method for Treating Epilepsy

    The symptoms of epilepsy that have persisted for many years indicate phlegm trapped between the heart's orifices, unable to be released. Patients who enjoy eating charcoal likely have their heart's fire obscured by phlegm, unable to express itself. Charcoal, being a residue of fire, harmonizes with the heart's fire and flavors, making it taste sweet like honey to the patient.

    The formula includes one ounce of ginseng, three qian each of southern star, ghost arrow, burdock root, and white peony, one qian each of aconite and cinnamon, and two qian each of pinellia, acorus, and cinnabar powder. First, boil the above herbs in two bowls of water and divide it into two doses, mixing half of the cinnabar into the medicine for the patient to take. If the patient refuses to take it, give them charcoal; after consuming it, they will be happy to eat it. If they ask for more charcoal, it is fine to provide them with it. The second dose should be prepared in the same way. If the patient does not respond as well as before, they should be made to drink it quickly. If they resist, it is permissible to strike them to provoke their anger; anger will stir the liver's wood fire, generating heat for the heart, thus helping to dispel phlegm.

    Although patients with epilepsy often eat regularly, the qi of food within their intestines can nourish their life without dying; it is, however, the heart that remains unyielding.[50p]

    倘心早死，即无病之人食谷亦亡，况有癫痫之证，吾见其早亡不能待于今日。惟其中心不死，不过痰邪有碍，一时癫痫，其脾胃尤有生气也，故用人参以治心，加附子、菖蒲、肉桂温中以祛邪，加柴胡舒肝平木，加南星、鬼箭、半夏逐痰荡邪，加丹砂定魂镇魄，自然邪气少而正气多也。　　别有治癫之方，亦奇妙。方用柴胡、白芥子各五钱，白芍、半夏、牛胆制过南星、茯神、菖蒲各三钱，附子、人参各一钱，水十碗，煎二碗，先与一碗，服之必倦怠，急再灌一碗，必熟睡。有睡至一二日者，切不可惊醒，如死人一般，任其自醒。醒来病如失，即索饮食，说从前之病，不可即与饮食。饿半日，与之米粥，汤内加人参、陈皮各五分，煎粥与之。[51p]

    If the heart dies early, then even a healthy person consuming grains will also perish; how much more so for those with epilepsy? I have seen those who perish early cannot wait until today. As long as the heart remains alive, it is merely phlegm and evil that obstructs it. At that moment of epilepsy, the spleen and stomach still hold vitality. Therefore, I use ginseng to treat the heart, adding aconite, calamus, and cinnamon to warm the center and dispel the evil. I add bupleurum to soothe the liver and balance the wood element, along with nux vomica, ghost arrow, and pinellia to expel phlegm and eliminate the evil. I add cinnabar to stabilize the spirit and calm the soul, naturally reducing the evil qi and increasing the righteous qi.

    There is another remarkable method for treating epilepsy. The formula includes five qians each of bupleurum and white mustard seed, three qians each of white peony, pinellia, processed nux vomica, poria, and calamus, and one qian each of aconite and ginseng. Boil with ten bowls of water until reduced to two bowls. Give the patient one bowl to drink first, which will certainly cause fatigue. Then immediately administer another bowl, which will induce deep sleep. If they sleep for one or two days, do not awaken them suddenly, as if they were dead; let them wake naturally. When they awaken and are confused, ask for food and drink. If they mention their previous condition, do not give them anything immediately. After half a day of fasting, give them rice porridge, adding five fen each of ginseng and aged tangerine peel to the soup, and cook the porridge to serve.[51p]

    再用人参三钱，白朮一两，甘草一钱，茯苓、白芥子各五钱，陈皮五分，水煎与之，彼必欣然自服。服后再睡，亦听其自醒，则永不再发，亦奇妙法也。　　如人病花癫，妇人忽然癫痫，见男子抱住不肯放，此乃思慕男子不可得，忽然得病，如暴风疾雨，罔识羞耻，见男子则为情人也。此肝木枯槁，内火燔盛，脉必弦出寸口，法当用平肝散郁祛邪之味，用柴胡、当归、麦冬、白芥子各五钱，白芍一两，炒栀子、茯神、元参各三钱，甘草、菖蒲各一钱，水煎服。如不肯服，用人灌之，彼必骂詈不休。久之人倦欲卧，卧后醒来，自家羞耻，紧闭房门者三日，少少与之饮食自愈。一剂后，不必更与之药也。[52p]

    Use three qian of ginseng, one liang of atractylodes, one qian of licorice, five qian each of poria and white mustard seed, and five fen of dried tangerine peel. Boil these in water and give it to them, and they will surely take it willingly. After taking it, let them sleep again; listen for them to wake up on their own, and then they will never have another episode, which is a marvelous method.

    In cases where a person suffers from an illness analogous to flower mania, a woman might suddenly have epilepsy, seeing a man and refusing to let go of him. This represents an intense longing for a man that cannot be fulfilled, suddenly manifesting as a disease, like a violent storm, losing all sense of shame; upon seeing a man, she behaves as if he were her lover. This is due to the liver's wood being withered and an inner fire raging strongly, and the pulse will definitely be tight at the cun position. The treatment should use a formula to soothe the liver, disperse stagnation, and expel evil. Use five qian each of bupleurum, angelica, ophiopogon, and white mustard seed; one liang of white peony; and three qian each of stir-fried gardenia, poria spirit, and scrophularia; with one qian each of licorice and calamus, boiled in water to be taken.

    If she refuses to take it, force it into her via a syringe; she will undoubtedly curse incessantly. After a while, the person will become weary and want to lie down. After they awaken, feeling shame, they will tightly close the room's door for three days, and gradually, with a little food and drink, will recover on their own. After one dose, there is no need to give her more medicine.[52p]

    　　癫病之生也，多生于脾胃之虚寒；脾胃虚寒，所食水谷不变精而变痰，痰凝胸膈之间，不得化流于心而癫证生矣。苟徒治痰而不补气，未有不速之死者。方用祛癫汤，人参、白芥子各五钱，白朮一两，肉桂、干姜、陈皮各一钱，甘草、菖蒲各五分，半夏三钱，水煎服。此方用人参、白朮专补脾胃，用干姜以祛寒邪，用白芥子、半夏以消顽痰，用甘草、菖蒲以引入心而开窍，自然正气回而邪痰散。一剂神定，再剂神旺，又何癫病之不能愈哉？惟是花癫之证，乃女子思想其人而心邪，然亦因脾胃之寒而邪入也。本方加入白芍一两，柴胡二钱，炒栀子三钱，去肉桂治之，亦最神，一剂而癫止矣。盖柴胡、白芍、炒栀子皆入肝以平木，祛火而散郁，故成此奇功也。[53p]

    Epileptic illness often arises from the weakness and coldness of the spleen and stomach. When the spleen and stomach are weak and cold, the food consumed does not transform into essential qi but instead becomes phlegm. This phlegm condenses between the chest and diaphragm, unable to flow to the heart, leading to the manifestation of epilepsy. If one only treats phlegm without nourishing qi, there will inevitably be cases of sudden death.

    The recipe for the treatment is as follows: Take five qian each of ginseng and white mustard seed, one liang of white atractylodes, one qian each of cinnamon, dried ginger, and tangerine peel, five fen each of licorice and fragrant calamus, and three qian of pinellia; decoct these herbs in water to take. This formula uses ginseng and atractylodes specifically to nourish the spleen and stomach, dried ginger to dispel cold pathogens, white mustard seed and pinellia to eliminate stubborn phlegm, and licorice and fragrant calamus to guide the formula into the heart and open the orifices. Naturally, the righteous qi returns, and the phlegm disperses.

    With one dose, the spirit stabilizes; with a second dose, the spirit flourishes. What epilepsy cannot be cured? As for the manifestation of flower-related epilepsy, it stems from a woman's obsession with someone, which is also due to the coldness of the spleen and stomach allowing the evil to invade. For this condition, add one liang of white peony root, two qian of bupleurum, and three qian of stir-fried gardenia to the original recipe, omitting the cinnamon; it is also very effective, often stopping the epilepsy with just one dose. The reason is that bupleurum, white peony, and stir-fried gardenia all enter the liver to balance the wood element, dispel fire and scatter stagnant qi, thus achieving this extraordinary effect.[53p]

    　　　　　呆病治法

    　　呆病如痴而默默不言，如饥而悠悠如失也，意欲癫而不能，心欲狂而不敢，有时睡数日不醒，有时坐数日不眠，有时将己身衣服密密缝完，有时将他人物件深深藏掩，与人言则无语而神游，背人言则低声而泣诉，与之食则厌薄而不吞，不与食则吞炭而若快。此等证虽有祟凭之，实亦胸腹之中无非痰气，故治呆无奇法，治痰即治呆也。[54p]

    Treatment of Stupor

    Stupor resembles madness, silent and uncommunicative; like hunger, it lingers but feels lost. The mind desires to act wildly yet cannot; the heart wishes to be frantic but is afraid. Sometimes one may sleep for days without waking, at other times sit for days without sleeping. Occasionally, they meticulously mend their own clothes, or deeply hide and cover someone else's belongings. When speaking with others, they are mute and seem to drift away; when alone, they whisper quietly and cry. They may express aversion to food and refuse to swallow, yet when not offered food, they consume charcoal as if it were delightful. Although these symptoms may be attributed to possession or evil influence, they are essentially caused by phlegm and qi obstructing the chest and abdomen. Thus, the treatment for stupor is no mystery; treating phlegm is the same as treating stupor.[54p]

    然而痰势最盛，呆气最深，若以寻常二陈汤治之，安得获效？方用逐呆仙丹，人参、白芥子、菟丝子各一两，白朮二两，茯神三两，半夏五钱，附子五分，白薇、丹砂各三钱，研末，先将各药煎汤，调丹砂末与半碗。彼不肯服，以炭给之，欣然服矣。又给之又服半碗，然后听其自便，彼必倦怠欲卧矣。乘其睡熟，将其衣服被褥，尽行火化，单留身上所服之衣，另用新被盖之，切不可惊醒。此一睡有睡至数日者，醒来必觅衣而衣无，觅被而被非故物，彼必大哭。然后又以前药与一剂，必不肯服，即给之炭亦断不肯矣。不妨以鞭责之，动其怒气，用有力之人，将前药执而灌之，彼必大怒，已而又睡去矣。[55p]

    However, when phlegm is at its peak and dullness is profound, how can it be effectively treated with ordinary Erchen Decoction? Therefore, the method uses the Immortal Pill to expel dullness: one tael each of ginseng, white mustard seed, and dodder seed; two taels of white atractylodes; three taels of poria; five qian of pinellia; five fen of aconite; three qian each of white wood蘇 and cinnabar, ground into powder. First, decoct each herbal ingredient, then mix the cinnabar powder with half a bowl of the decoction. If he refuses to take it, administer it with charcoal, and he will gladly drink it. After giving him another half bowl, allow him to act as he wishes; he will certainly feel tired and want to sleep.

    Take advantage of his deep sleep to burn all his clothing and bedding, leaving only the garments he is wearing, and cover him with a new blanket, being careful not to wake him. This sleep may last several days; when he wakes, he will surely look for his clothes and find nothing, search for his bedding and discover it is not familiar, leading him to cry out in distress. Then present him with the same medicine again; he will surely refuse to take it, and even refuse the charcoal. It may be effective to whip him to provoke his anger, using strong individuals to hold him down and force the previous medicine into him; he will undoubtedly become very angry, and afterward, he will fall asleep again.[55p]

    此时断须预备新鲜衣服被褥等项，俟其半日即醒，彼见满房俱是亲人，心中恍然如悟，必又大哭不已。诸人当以好言劝之，彼必说出鬼神之事。亲人说幸某人治疗，已将鬼神尽行祛遣，不必再虑，彼听之欣然，而病亦全愈矣。此方之妙，妙在大补心脾，以茯神为君，使痰在心者尽祛之而出，其余消痰之药，又得附子引之无经不入，将遍身上下之痰，尽行祛入膀胱之中而消化矣。白薇、菟丝子皆是安神妙药，而丹砂镇魂定魄，实多奇功，所以用之而奏效也。[56p]

    At this time, one must prepare fresh clothing, bedding, and other items, awaiting his awakening in half a day. When he sees that the whole room is filled with relatives, his heart will suddenly clear as if he understands, and he will undoubtedly weep greatly. Others should gently persuade him, and he will surely speak of matters concerning spirits and deities. Relatives will then say that a certain person has treated him and has already dispelled all the spirits, so there is no need for further worry. Upon hearing this, he will feel joyful, and his illness will be completely cured. The key to this method lies in greatly nourishing the heart and spleen, using Fuling (Poria) as the primary agent, which helps to expel phlegm from the heart; the remaining phlegm-dissolving medicine, along with Aconite, guides it throughout the body, sending all phlegm into the bladder for digestion. Baiwei (White Clay) and Tusizi (Cuscuta) are both excellent soothing herbs, while Cinnabar stabilizes the soul and calms the spirit, thus having remarkable effects, which is why they are used and produce results.[56p]

    　　呆病乃郁抑不舒，愤怒而成者有之，羞恚而成者有之。方用人参、柴胡、当归、菖蒲、生枣仁、半夏各一两，白芍四两，甘草、天南星、郁金、神曲各五钱，附子一钱，茯苓三两，水十碗，煎一碗灌之。彼必不肯饮，以双手执其头发，两人拿其左右手，以一人托其下颏，一人将羊角去尖，插入其口，一人以手拿住其头，一人倾药入羊角内灌之。倘或吐出，不妨益妙，以灌完为主。彼必骂詈，少顷，人困欲睡，听其自醒，切勿惊动使醒。自醒来则全愈，惊醒来则半愈矣。此生治之一法也。[57p]

    The condition of "stupor" arises from a blockage of emotions, sometimes resulting from anger and at other times from shame. The remedy consists of one tael each of ginseng, Chaihu (Bupleurum), Angelica, calamus, and jujube seeds; four taels of white peony; five qian each of licorice, tian nanxing (Arisaema), turmeric, and shenqu; one qian of aconite; three taels of poria; and ten bowls of water, boiled down to one bowl for administration. The patient will likely refuse to drink the medicine. To facilitate the process, two individuals should hold the patient's hands while one supports their chin, another inserts a blunt sheep horn into their mouth, and yet another holds the patient's head to pour the medicine into the horn. If the patient vomits, it is no concern; the focus should be to administer the entire dose. The patient may scream and curse, but after a while, they will become tired and want to sleep. It is important to allow them to wake up on their own without disturbance. If they awaken naturally, they will fully recover; if startled awake, their recovery will be only partial. This is one method of treating this condition.[57p]

    　　　　　狂病治法

    　　痰结在胃中，不能吐出，狂言如见鬼状，时发时止，气塞胸膛，以牛肉五斤、水二斗煎汤饮之，至不可食而止。以鹅翎探吐，必大吐，必吐至如块黄色顽痰而后止。若不吐出，再饮之，必以吐尽而止，前病顿失。后以陈皮、茯苓、甘草、白朮汤徐徐饮之，平复如故。　　伤寒发狂，至登高而歌，弃衣而走，见水而入，骂詈呼号，不避亲疏者，去生远矣。仲景以竹叶石膏汤救之，妙矣。盖阳明之火，其势最烈，一发而不可救，非用大剂白虎汤，何能止其燎原之势？而世人畏首畏尾，往往用之而特少其剂，是犹杯水救车薪之焰也。故用石膏，必须至三四两或半斤，一剂煎服，火势始能少退，狂亦可少止也。然石膏性猛，虽善退火，未免损伤胃气，必须与人参兼用为妙。今有一方，用白虎汤之半，而另加药味，方名祛热生胃汤。石膏、元参、麦冬各三两，知母三钱，人参、车前子各五钱，茯苓一两，水煎服。[58p]

    Treatment for Mania

    When phlegm accumulates in the stomach and cannot be expelled, it leads to maniacal speech as if seeing ghosts, intermittently appearing and disappearing, causing a blockage in the chest. One should boil five pounds of beef and two dou of water into a soup and drink it until one can no longer eat. With a goose feather, probe for vomiting, and one will surely expel a large amount, specifically until a lump of thick yellow phlegm is expelled before ceasing. If it does not come out, drink again, ensuring it is completely expelled before stopping, or the previous condition will suddenly worsen. Afterwards, gradually drink a decoction of dried tangerine peel, Poria, licorice, and white atractylodes to restore balance.

    In cases of fever leading to mania, where one might climb high and sing, discard clothing and run, dive into water, shout and curse without regard for kin, such beings are far from life. Zhongjing saved them with a decoction of bamboo leaves and gypsum, which is quite wonderful. The fire of Yangming is the most intense; once it erupts, it cannot be saved without a large dose of White Tiger Decoction to halt its overwhelming spread. However, people often fear using too much, thus employing only a small amount, akin to using a cup of water to extinguish a burning pile of firewood. Therefore, gypsum must be used in a dose of three or four taels or even half a pound, prepared in one decoction, for the fire's intensity to begin to diminish, and mania can also be somewhat alleviated. Yet, gypsum has a strong nature; though it effectively cools the fire, it can still damage the stomach's qi, hence it must be used in conjunction with ginseng for optimal effect.

    Currently, there is a formula that uses half the White Tiger Decoction while adding other medicinal ingredients, named the Stomach-Replenishing Decoction. It consists of three taels each of gypsum, Scrophularia, and Ophiopogon, three qian of Anemarrhena, five qian each of ginseng and Plantago, and one tael of Poria, all combined with water for decoction.[58p]

    此方石膏、知母以泻胃火，人参以生胃气，元参去浮游之热，麦冬生肺中之阴，茯苓、车前引火下行于膀胱，从小便而出。且火盛者口必渴，口渴必多饮水，吾用此二味以分湿，则水流而火自随水而散矣。方中泻火又不伤气，似胜于白虎汤。一剂而狂定，二剂而口渴减半，三剂而口渴止，火亦息，正不必用四剂也。凡有火热而发狂，或汗如雨下，口渴舌燥，或如芒刺者，以此方投之立效，断不至于死也。　　生治者，乃人未死而若死者，用药以生之也。譬如发狂呆病是也。发狂多是热病，登高而歌，弃衣而走，见水而入，骂詈之声，叫喊杀人之语，不绝于口，舌如芒刺，饮水不休，痰色光亮，面如火肿是也。方用石膏半斤，元参一斤，白芥子、半夏各三两，知母、人参、甘草各一两，麦冬五两，竹叶数百片，先用糯米半升煎汤一锅，去其米粒，用汤半锅将前药煎之，取数碗，彼索水时与之饮。随索随与，饮尽必睡。急再用元参一斤，麦冬半斤，煎汤候之。[59p]

    This formula uses gypsum and Anemarrhena as a remedy to drain stomach fire, ginseng to generate stomach qi, and Yuan Shen to eliminate excess heat. Ophiopogon nourishes the yin of the lungs, while Poria and Plantago help direct fire downward to the bladder, allowing it to exit through urination. Furthermore, when there is excessive fire, one’s mouth must be dry; with thirst comes increased water intake. I employ these two ingredients to disperse moisture, so that when water flows, the fire dissipates alongside it. This formula drains fire without harming qi, appearing superior to Bai Hu Tang. One dose calms the delirium, two doses reduce thirst by half, and three doses stop the thirst completely, also extinguishing the fire, thus four doses are unnecessary.

    For those experiencing fire heat leading to delirium, or sweating profusely like rain, with dry mouth and tongue, or sensations like thorn pricks, this formula will yield immediate effects, ensuring it does not lead to death. "Living treatment" refers to situations where a person is on the brink of death, but not yet dead, and medication is used to restore them. For instance, cases of manic or comatose illness are often due to heat illness, characterized by singing high, running while discarding clothing, jumping into water, and incessantly shouting violent words, with protruding tongue and relentless thirst, producing bright phlegm and a face resembling an inflamed state.

    The formula uses half a pound of gypsum, one pound of Yuan Shen, three taels of white mustard and pinellia each, one tael of Anemarrhena, ginseng, and licorice, along with five taels of Ophiopogon and several hundred pieces of bamboo leaves. First, half a sheng of glutinous rice is boiled to create a broth, with the rice grains removed. Half a pot of this broth is then used to brew the previously mentioned herbs, with several bowls taken to provide in response to requests for water. Offer it continuously and, once finished, sleep will follow. Promptly use another pound of Yuan Shen and half a pound of Ophiopogon for brewing while waiting.[59p]

    一醒呼水，即以此汤与之，彼必欣然自饮。服完又必大睡，又将滓煎汤候之。醒后再与，彼即不若从前之肯服，亦不必强，听其自然可也。后用熟地、麦冬各三两，元参六两，山茱萸一两，煎二碗与之，一剂必愈，不必再与。此生治之一法也。　　凡人发狂而止骂詈人，不口渴，索饮与之水不饮者，乃寒证之狂也。此得之气郁不舒，怒气不能发泄，其人平日必懦弱不振，今一旦而狂病发作，法宜祛痰为主，而佐以补气之药。方用人参、茯神各一两，白朮五钱，半夏、南星、附子各一钱，菖蒲三分，水煎服。此方之妙，全在补气而不十分祛痰。盖寒证发狂，与痫证同治，加入附子以消其寒气，菖蒲引入心经，自然下喉熟睡，病如失也。加柴胡一钱，以舒其肝木之郁气，尤易奏效。　　人有终年狂病而不愈者，或拿刀杀人，或见官大骂，亲戚不认，儿女不知，见水则喜，见食则怒，此乃心气之虚，而热邪乘之，痰气侵之也。[60p]

    When someone awakens and calls for water, give them this soup, and they will surely drink it with joy. After finishing it, they will likely fall into a deep sleep again, and then prepare more soup with the residue for when they wake. When they wake again, if they do not want to drink as before, do not force them; let it happen naturally. Later, use three taels of cooked rehmannia and ophiopogon, six taels of codonopsis, one tael of cornus, decocted into two bowls to give them. One dose will surely cure them, and there is no need to repeat it. This is one method of treatment.

    As for those who have a fit of madness but stop to curse at others, not thirsty, and refuse to drink the offered water, this is madness caused by cold. It arises from stagnation of Qi and repressed anger; such individuals typically display weakness and lack of spirit, and the madness manifests abruptly. The treatment should focus on expelling phlegm while also supplementing Qi. The prescription includes one tael each of ginseng and poria, five qian of white atractylodes, one qian each of pinellia, nux vomica, and aconite, and three fen of calamus, all decocted and taken. The brilliance of this formula lies in supplementing Qi while not excessively expelling phlegm. Cold-induced madness is treated similarly to epilepsy, and aconite is included to eliminate cold Qi, while calamus directs the remedy to the heart channel, letting it naturally soothe the throat for sound sleep, as if lost to the disease. Adding one qian of bupleurum helps to relieve the stagnation of the liver wood Qi, further enhancing effectiveness.

    Some individuals may have persistent madness that does not improve; they might attack others with a knife, curse officials loudly, fail to recognize family, or have children unaware of them, showing joy at the sight of water but anger at food. This reflects a deficiency of heart Qi and an invasion by heat evil, along with phlegm Qi encumbering them.[60p]

    此等证欲泻火而火在心之中，不可泻也；欲消痰而痰在心之中，不易消也。惟有补脾胃之气，则心自得养，不必祛痰痰自化，不必泻火火自无矣。方名化狂丹，人参、白朮、茯神各一两，附子一分，半夏、菟丝子各三钱，菖蒲、甘草各一钱，水煎服。一剂狂定，再剂病痊。此方妙在补心脾胃之三经，而化其痰，不去泻火。盖泻火则心气愈伤，而痰涎愈盛，狂将何止呼？尤妙用附子一分，引补心消痰之剂，直入心中，则气尤易补而痰尤易消也。　　凡人有病发狂，如见鬼状，此乃正气虚而邪气犯之也，似宜正治邪为是。然而邪之所凑，其气必虚，不治其虚，安问其余？此所以急宜固其正气，而少佐以祛痰祛邪之药为妙。如发狂见鬼者，乃虚也。方用人参、白朮各一两，半夏、天南星各三钱，附子一钱，大剂灌之，狂自定矣。　　发狂不知人而不见鬼者，乃热也，不可与前汤。此见鬼为虚而非实热，方用人参同入于祛痰祛邪之药内，乃因其反而反治之也。[61p]

    These ailments desire to dispel fire, yet fire resides within the heart, making it impossible to disperse; they want to eliminate phlegm, yet phlegm is also in the heart, making it difficult to dissolve. Only by strengthening the energy of the spleen and stomach can the heart receive nourishment on its own. There’s no need to eliminate phlegm; it will naturally transform, and there’s no need to dispel fire; it will naturally cease. This method is named "Transforming Madness Elixir," using one tael each of ginseng, white atractylodes, and poria, one fen (a unit), and three qian each of pinellia and cuscus, one qian each of calamus and licorice, boiled in water for consumption. One dose will calm the madness, and the second will heal the illness. This method is excellent for nourishing the heart, spleen, and stomach while transforming phlegm without dispelling fire. For if fire is dispelled, the heart's energy becomes more injured, and phlegm accumulates further; how can madness be stopped? Notably, the use of one fen of aconite is brilliant, facilitating the nourishing of the heart and the dissolving of phlegm directly into the heart, allowing energy to be easily replenished and phlegm to be easily dissolved.

    When a person is ill and becomes mad, as if seeing ghosts, it is due to the deficiency of righteous energy and the invasion of邪 (evil). It seems appropriate to rectify the邪. However, since邪 gathers where energy is weak, if we do not treat the deficiency, how can we talk of the rest? Thus, it is urgent to support the righteous energy and lightly assist with medications to eliminate phlegm and邪. For those who see ghosts in madness, it is a deficiency. Therefore, use one tael each of ginseng and white atractylodes, three qian each of pinellia and tian nanxing, and one qian of aconite, and administer a large dose; the madness will calm itself.

    For those who are mad, do not recognize people, and do not see ghosts, this signifies heat. They should not be given the previous decoction. Seeing ghosts indicates deficiency and not true heat, so the method includes ginseng, added to medications for eliminating phlegm and邪, as it is a reversal for treatment.[61p]

    　　　　方

    　　芎藭酒 【《千金方》，下同】 　治风乘虚经五脏六腑为癫狂，诸邪病悉主之。　　芎藭　辛夷　天雄　人参　天门冬　柏子仁　磁石　石膏　茵芋　山茱萸　白头翁　桂心　秦艽各三两　松萝　羚羊角　细辛　薯蓣　菖蒲　甘草各二两　云母烧令赤为粉，一两　防风四两　　右二十一味(口父)咀，以酒二斗渍七日，初服二合，渐加至五合，日三。
    　　续命风引汤　治中风癫眩不知人，狂言舌肿出。　　麻黄　芎藭　石膏　人参　防风各三两　桂心　甘草　独活各二两　防己　附子　当归各一两　杏仁三十枚　陈姜三两　　右十三味(口父)咀，以酒三升、水一斗合煎，取四升，分四服，日三夜一。[62p]

    Treats wind-induced insanity affecting the five organs and six bowels, and is effective for various邪病.
    Ingredients:

      Total of 21 ingredients.
      Crush and steep in 2 dou of wine for 7 days, initially taking 2 he, gradually increasing to 5 he, three times a day.

    Continuation of Life Wind Induction Decoction
    Treats apoplexy, madness, and insensibility, causing swelling of the tongue and wild speech.
    Ingredients:

    • Ma Huang: 3 taels
    • Xiongshen: 3 taels
    • Shi Gao: 3 taels

    • Gui Xin: 2 taels

      Total of 13 ingredients.
      Crush and decoct with 3 sheng of wine and 1 dou of water to obtain 4 sheng, divided into four doses, taken three times a day and once at night.[62p]

    　　鸱头丸　治风癫。
    　　葶苈子　鉛丹　虎掌　乌头　(艹舌)蒌根各三分　甘遂　天雄　蜀椒　大戟各二分　铁精　(艹闾)茹各一两　鸱头一枚　　右十二味为末，蜜丸如梧子大，酒下二丸，日三服。　　又方　治狂邪发无常，披发大叫唤，欲杀人，不避水火。　　虎睛　露蜂房　鸱头各一具　枫上寄生五分　石长生十分　茯苓　桂心　防风各三两　独活　甘草　人参　天雄各一两　　右十二味(口父)咀，以水一斗二升，煮取三升，分四服，日三夜一。
    　　抱胆丸 【《准绳》，下同】 　治男妇一切癫痫风狂，或因惊恐怖畏所致；及妇人产后血虚，惊气入心，并室女经脉通行，惊邪蕴结，累效。　　水银二两　乳香去油细研　朱砂各一两，细研　黑铅一两半　　右将黑铅入铫子内，下水银结成砂子，次下朱砂、滴乳，乘热用柳木槌研匀，丸鸡头大，每服一丸，空心，井华水吞下。病者得睡，切莫惊动，觉来即安，再一丸可除根。[63p]

    Chitou Pill treats wind-induced madness.
    Three fen each of the following: Tingli (Tinglizi), lead (qian dan), tiger's paw (huzhang), aconite (wutou), (herb) tianling; two fen each of gansui, tianxiong, Shu pepper, and daqi; one tael each of iron essence and (herb) lü; one Chitou.
    Grind the twelve ingredients into powder, form pills the size of walnuts, take two pills with wine, three times a day.
    Another formula is for treating unpredictable manic episodes, where the patient yells with hair disheveled and has violent urges without fear of water or fire:
    One each of tiger’s eye, bee's nest, and Chitou; five fen of mistletoe, ten fen of Shichangsheng, and three taels each of Fu Ling, cinnamon heart (guixin), and fangfeng; one tael each of Duhuo, licorice, ren shen, and tianxiong.
    Grind these twelve ingredients, add to 1 dou 2 sheng of water, boil down to 3 sheng, and divide into four doses, to be taken three times a day and once at night.

    Baodai Pill treats all forms of wind-induced madness in men and women, or caused by shock and fear; also for women having postpartum blood deficiency, where fear enters the heart, and for maidens where menstrual flow is obstructed by trapped evil.
    Two taels of mercury, one tael each of finely ground frankincense (de-oiled) and cinnabar; one and a half taels of black lead.
    Combine the black lead in a small pan, add the mercury to form granules, then add cinnamon, and drop in frankincense. While hot, use a willow wood pestle to blend, forming pills the size of a chick's head. Take one pill on an empty stomach, swallowed with water from a deep well. If the patient sleeps, do not disturb them; upon waking, if necessary, another pill can eliminate the issue completely.[63p]

    　　五邪汤　治中风神思昏愦，五邪所侵，或歌或哭，或笑或喜或怒，发则无时。　　防风　桂心　白芍药　远志　独活　甘草炙　白朮　人参　秦艽　牡蛎煅　石膏　禹余粮酢淬各二两　雄黄水飞　防风　石菖蒲　茯神　蛇蜕皮炒，各一两　　每服四钱，水二盏，煎一盏，去渣温服，不拘时候，日进二服。
    　　九精丸　一名九物牛黄丸。治男子沾鬼魅欲死，所见惊怖欲走，时无休止，邪气不能自绝者。　　牛黄土精，一云火精　龙骨水精　荆实人精　元参元武精　赤石脂朱雀精　玉屑细研，白虎精　曾青苍龙精　空青研，天精　雄黄地精，无石者炒研，各一两　　右九味，名九精，上通九天，下通九地。为细末，炼蜜和丸如小豆大，每服一丸，日三服，以知为度。[64p]

    Wuxie Decoction: It treats stroke with dimming of the mind, invaded by the Five Evils, causing one to sing, cry, laugh, rejoice, or become angry at any time.

    • Gui Xin (Cinnamomum cassia heart)

    Jiu Jing Pill: Also known as Jiu Wu Niu Huang Pill. It treats men who feel haunted by evil spirits, experiencing fear and a desire to run, with no moment of rest, unable to rid themselves of evil qi.

    Ingredients:

    • Niu Huang (Bovine bile)
    • Tu Jing (earth essence, also fire essence)
    • Long Gu (Dragon bone)

    • Di Jing (earth essence); if no stones are available, roast and grind, each one liang.

    These nine flavors collectively form the Nine Essentials, connecting to the nine heavens above and the nine realms below. Grind into a fine powder, refine with honey, and form into pills the size of small beans. Take one pill three times a day, adjusting dosage as needed.[64p]

    　　甘遂散 【《得效方》，下同】 　一名遂心丹。治癫痫及妇女心风血邪。　　甘遂一钱
    　　右为末，用猪心取三管血三条，和甘遂多少和之，将心批作二片，入药在内，合之线缚，外用皮纸裹湿，慢火煨熟，或令焦，取药细研，入辰砂末一钱，和匀，分作四丸，每服一丸，将所煨猪心煎汤化下。再服用别猪心亦可。过半日，大便下恶物后，调和胃气。凡此病乍作乍醒者，苏不食，迷痴者，不治。

    Gansui San (also known as Suixin Dan) is used to treat epilepsy and women's heart wind blood evil.

    Ingredients: 1 qian of Gansui.

    Preparation: Grind the Gansui into powder, then take three tubes of blood from a pig's heart, mix with a corresponding amount of Gansui. Cut the heart into two pieces, place the medicine inside, stitch it up, wrap it in damp paper, and simmer it on low heat until thoroughly cooked, or until it is scorched. Take the medicinal mixture, grind it finely, add 1 qian of cinnabar powder, mix well, and divide into four pills. Each time, take one pill dissolved in decoction of the simmered pig's heart. It is also acceptable to use another pig's heart for subsequent doses. After half a day, when the unpleasant material is expelled through bowel movement, it helps to harmonize stomach qi. This treatment is effective for sudden onset or awakening aggression but is not suitable for those who are excessively hungry or confused.

    Xiexin Tang treats accumulated heat in the heart, leading to delirium and madness, including climbing walls.

    Ingredients: 5 qian each of Dahuang (Rhubarb), Huangqin (Scutellaria), and Huanglian (Coptis).

    Preparation: Grind the above ingredients into powder, and take 4 qian with 1.5 cups of water for decoction.

    Yinshen Guishe Dan is used to treat heart qi and also addresses heart wind.[65p]

    　　生天南星刮去皮取心　朱砂水飞各一两　附子一枚，重七钱已上者，炮去皮脐　　右为末，用猪心血，丸梧子大，如不稠粘，用面糊少许，煎忘忧草根汤下，子午之交，各一服。
    　　秘方半夏丸 【《集验方》】 　治心风狂。张德明传，其内人失心狂数年，服此药而愈，后再作服人参琥珀丸而安。　　半夏一两，用生姜汁煎五十沸，取出，切作块，更煎令熟，焙干为细末　麝香一钱，研　水银半钱　生薄荷一大握，和水银研如泥　　右件药入薄荷泥内，更研千百下，丸如芥子大，每服十五丸，金银汤临卧下，三日再服。

    Heavenly South Star: Scrape off the skin and take the heart; take one tael each of vermilion water and flying water; one piece of aconite, weighing at least seven qian, remove the skin and umbilicus. Grind these into a fine powder. Use pig heart blood to form into pills the size of wutong seeds. If it is not sticky enough, add a little flour paste. Boil in the broth of forgetfulness root and take one dose at each time of Zi and Wu.

    Secret Recipe Banxia Pill (from "Collected Experience Recipes"): Treats heart wind madness. Zhang Deming transmitted this; his wife lost her mind for several years, and after taking this medicine, she recovered. Later, she took ginseng amber pills for stability.

    Take one tael of Banxia, boil with fresh ginger juice until it reaches fifty boils. After removing, cut it into pieces, and continue to boil until cooked. Dry and powder finely. Take one qian of musk, grind; half qian of mercury; a large handful of fresh mint, and mix mercury until it becomes mud.

    Mix all these medicines into the mint mud and grind extensively. Form into pills the size of mustard seeds. Take fifteen pills each time with golden or silver liquor before bed, and repeat after three days.

    Ginseng Amber Pills: Treats epilepsy and heart wind.

    Ingredients: Ginseng, amber, and powdered Rehmannia, Reishi, stone calamus, and Polygala each half a tael; soak in warm wine for half a day and remove the heart; additional separately ground frankincense; sour jujube seeds soaked in warm wine for half a day, shell removed, and roasted on clean paper until fragrant; separately ground vermilion, each two and a half qian.

    Make a fine powder and mix with honey to form pills the size of wutong seeds. Take twenty pills after meals with warm wine; take daily. If unable to drink, use jujube soup instead. Can be taken regularly.[66p]

    　　宁志丸 【《得效方》】 　治心风。　　好朱砂一两，将熟绢一小片，包裹线扎，不用研　獖猪心一枚，竹刀切开，不犯铁，用纸拭去血，入朱砂包于猪心内，再用线缚合　　右再用甜笋壳重裹，麻皮扎定，无灰酒二升，入银器或砂罐内煮，酒尽，去包取出，朱砂另研。将猪心竹刀细切，砂盆内研烂，却入后药末，朱砂、枣肉为丸，留少朱砂为衣，药末须隔日研下，枣肉于煮猪心日绝早煮熟，去皮核取肉四两，入后药：　　人参　白茯苓　当归洗去土及芦　石菖蒲　乳香另研　酸枣仁五两许，汤浸去皮，净仁炒令赤，香熟为度，各半两　　右为末和丸如梧子大，以留下朱砂为衣，每服五十丸，人参汤下。[67p]

    Ningzhi Pill [from "De Xiaofang"]

    For treating heart wind.

    Take one tael of good cinnabar, and a small piece of cooked silk, wrap it up and tie it with a string, without grinding. Use one pig's heart, cut open with a bamboo knife, avoiding iron. Wipe away the blood with paper, place the wrapped cinnabar inside the pig's heart, and tie it with string.

    Then wrap it heavily with the shell of sweet bamboo shoots, secure it with hemp cloth. In two liters of weak wine, put it in a silver vessel or clay pot and boil it until the wine is completely gone, then remove the wrapping and take out the cinnabar. Grind the pig's heart finely with the bamboo knife in a mortar, and mix it with the following powdered ingredients:

    Cured red ginseng, white poria, angelica (washed to remove dirt), acorus, and frankincense (grind separately), about five taels of sour jujube seeds (soak to remove the skin, fry the clean seeds until red, and fragrant). Use equal quantities of these ingredients, mix them into a powder, and form into pills the size of a wutong seed, using the reserved cinnabar as a coating.

    Take fifty pills with ginseng soup each time.[67p]

    　　蕊珠丸　治癫狂。
    　　大猪心一枚，取血　朱砂一两，为末　青靛花一匙　　右先将青靛花、猪心血一处同研，次以朱砂末共丸如梧子大，每服二十丸，茶酒任下，不拘时。
    　　天门冬煎　治风癫。
    　　天门冬十斤，汤浸去心　生地黄肥净者，三十斤　　右二味，安木臼内，捣一二千杵，取其汁，再入温汤，更捣，又取其汁，不论几次，直待二药无味方止，以文武火熬成膏子，盛磁器内，每服一匙，温酒化下，不拘时，日进三服。[68p]

    Rui Zhu Wan treats mania.
    One piece of pig's heart, one tael of blood, and one spoon of indigo flower ground together. First, grind the indigo flower and pig's blood together, then mix with the ground cinnabar to form pills the size of a walnut. Take twenty pills each time, with tea or wine, at any time.

    Tian Men Dong decoction treats wind-induced madness.
    Ten jin of Tian Men Dong, soaked in broth to remove the heart; thirty jin of fresh Rehmannia, cleaned and fat. Place these two ingredients in a wooden mortar, pound with one to two thousand pestle strokes to extract the juice. Then, add warm broth and continue to pound, extracting the juice again. Repeat this process until the two ingredients have no flavor, then simmer with gentle and vigorous heat until it becomes a paste, storing it in ceramic containers. Take one spoon each time, dissolving in warm wine, at any time, three times a day.[68p]

    　　生铁落饮。
    　　生铁四十斤，入火烧赤，砧上锻之，有花出如兰如蛾、纷纷堕地者，名铁落，用水二斗，煮取一斗，入后药　石膏三两　龙脑研　白茯苓　防风各一两半　元参　秦艽各一两　　右为粗散，入铁汁中，煎取五斤，去滓，入竹沥一升和匀，温服二合，无时，日五服。
    　　朱砂丸　镇心神，化痰涎，退潮热，利咽膈，止烦渴。　　铁粉　海金砂　天竺黄各一两　脑子半钱　金银箔各二十片　生麝香一钱　人参　轻粉　真犀角各二钱　朱砂五钱　　右为末，水丸，朱砂为衣，共丸作六百丸。每一丸至五丸，痰盛潮热，薄荷砂糖生葛自然汁井水下。狂言谵语，涎壅膈上，地龙三两，薄荷及砂糖水研。心神不宁，金银箔薄荷汤化下。[69p]

    Raw iron falls into the drink.

    Forty pounds of raw iron, heated in the fire until red, are hammered on the anvil until flowers resembling orchids and moths emerge, falling to the ground. This is called iron drop. Use two ditches of water to boil down to one ditch, adding the following medicine: gypsum three taels, dragon’s brain one and a half taels, white poria one and a half taels, fang feng one and a half taels, yuan shen one tael, and qin jiao one tael. This mixture is a coarse powder, added to the iron juice, simmered to yield five pounds. Strain out the dross and mix with one liter of bamboo juice, taking two doses warm, without a fixed time, five times a day.

    The cinnabar pill calms the mind, transforms phlegm, reduces tidal heat, benefits the throat, and alleviates thirst. The following ingredients are used: iron powder, sea gold sand, and天竺黄 (similar to turmeric), each one tael; half a cash of powdered brain; twenty sheets of gold and silver foil; one cash of fresh musk; two taels each of ginseng, light powder, and genuine rhinoceros horn; five taels of cinnabar. These are ground into a powder, made into water pills, and coated in cinnabar, forming six hundred pills.

    For each pill, take up to five, when phlegm is abundant and tidal heat is present; use mint, sugar, fresh kudzu juice, and well water to wash down. For wild talk and delirium, thick phlegm blocking the throat, use three taels of earth dragon, powdered mint, and sugar water. For restlessness of the mind, dissolve gold and silver foil in mint soup and take.[69p]

    　　来苏膏瑞竹堂　治远年近日风痫，心病，风狂，中风，涎沫潮闭，牙关不开，及破伤风搐。　　皂角一两，肥大不蛀者，去皮弦
    　　右将皂角切碎，用浆水一大碗，春秋浸三四日，冬七日，夏一二日，揉开取净浸透皂角汁入银器，或砂锅内，用文武火熬，用新柳条槐枝搅，熬似膏药取出，摊于夹纸上，阴干收顿，如遇病人，取手掌大一片，用温浆化在盏内，用小竹管盛药水，将病人扶坐定，头微抬起，以药吹入左右鼻孔内。良久，扶起，涎出为验。要欲涎止，将温盐汤令病人服一二口，便止。忌鸡鱼生硬湿面。

    Lai Su Gao, Rui Zhu Tang
    For treating wind diseases that have persisted for many years, such as wind convulsions, heart conditions, violent wind, stroke, excessive saliva and froth, inability to open the jaw, and tetanus spasms.
    One liang of soapberry, large and uninfested, peel and string it.
    First chop the soapberry into small pieces, soak in a large bowl of water for three to four days in spring and autumn, seven days in winter, and one to two days in summer. After soaking, squeeze out the juice into a silver vessel or a clay pot. Use both gentle and strong heat to boil, stirring with fresh willow twigs or locust branches. Cook until it resembles an ointment, then spread it on parchment and let it dry in the shade. When a patient arrives, take a piece the size of a palm, dissolve it in warm water in a small bowl, and use a small bamboo tube to administer the medicine by blowing it into both nostrils while the patient is seated upright with their head slightly elevated. After a while, help the patient up; the presence of saliva will indicate efficacy. To stop saliva, have the patient drink one or two sips of warm saline solution. Avoid chicken, fish, and hard, moist dough.

    Xi Xin San He Jian
    For treating wind obstruction and excessive saliva, accumulated heat in the heart, bitter mouth and dry lips, excessive tearing from the eyes, and constipation with dark red urine.
    One and a half liang of white atractylodes, with equal parts of:
    Ephedra, Angelica sinensis, Schizonepeta spikes, Peony, Licorice, and six liang of rhubarb wrapped in flour and stewed, then remove the flour, cut, and roast.
    The above should be ground into a powder; each dose is three qian, with one and a half cups of water, three slices of fresh ginger, and seven leaves of mint, boiled and taken as a decoction. It can also be taken as a fine powder mixed with clear tea.[70p]

    　　宁志膏 【《本事方》】 　治癫狂心恙。　　人参　酸枣仁各一两　辰砂五钱　乳香二钱半　　右为细末，炼蜜和丸如弹子大，每服一丸，薄荷汤送下。予族弟缘兵火失心，制此方与之，服二十粒，愈。亲旧传去，服之皆验。
    　　灵苑辰砂散　洽风痰诸痫，狂言妄走，精神恍惚，思虑迷乱，乍歌乍哭，饮食失常，疾发仆地，吐沫戴目，魂魄不守。　　辰砂一两　酸枣仁微炒　乳香各半两　　右，量所患人饮酒几何，先令恣饮沉醉，但勿令吐，至静室中，以前药都作一服，温酒调作一盏，调之令顿饮。如饮酒素少人，但以随量取醉。服药讫，便安置床枕，令卧。病浅者半日至一日，病深者三两日，令家人潜伺之，鼻息匀调，但勿唤觉，亦不可惊触使觉，待其自醒，即神魂定矣。万一惊寤，不可复治。吴正肃公少时心病，服此一剂，寐五日方醒，遂瘥。[71p]

    Ning Zhi Gao [from "Ben Shi Fang"]

    For treating madness and heart ailments.
    Ingredients:

    1. Ginseng - 1 tael
    2. Sour Jujube Seed - 1 tael
    3. Cinnabar - 5 qian
    4. Frankincense - 2.5 qian

    Grind these into a fine powder, mix with honey, and form into pills the size of a marble. Take one pill with mint tea. I used this prescription for my cousin who lost his mind due to war; after taking twenty pills, he recovered. It has been passed down among relatives and has proven effective for all who have taken it.

    Ling Yuan Cinnabar Powder
    For addressing wind-phlegm and various seizures, delusions, erratic behavior, mental confusion, sudden singing and weeping, irregular eating habits, seizures causing falls, drooling and vacant eyes, and loss of spirit.
    Ingredients:

    1. Cinnabar - 1 tael
    2. Lightly roasted Sour Jujube Seed - 0.5 tael
    3. Frankincense - 0.5 tael

    Based on the amount of alcohol the patient usually consumes, let them drink freely to get drunk but avoid vomiting. Once in a quiet room, take the prepared medicine and mix it with warm wine to make a drink, instructing them to drink it all at once. If they are not used to drinking, monitor the amount to ensure they become drunk. After taking the medicine, prepare a bed and a pillow for them to lie down. Those with mild conditions will recover in half a day to one day; those with severe conditions may take two to three days. Family members should monitor their breathing, ensuring it is steady, but do not wake them or startle them. Wait for them to awaken naturally, at which point their spirit will stabilize. Should they be startled awake, further treatment is not advisable.

    The Duke of Wu Zhengsu experienced heart issues in his youth; after taking this remedy once, he slept for five days before waking and subsequently recovered.[71p]

    　　祛风一醉散　治阳厥气逆，多怒而狂。　　朱砂水飞，半两　曼陀罗花二钱半
    　　右为细末，每服二钱，温酒调下。若醉便卧，勿令惊觉为佳。有痰者，先服胜金丸。一方加乳香二钱，依前法服之。

    To Treat Wind and Intoxication
    This formula is for treating reverse flow of Yang Qi characterized by excessive anger and frenzy.
    Ingredients:

    • Half a tael of vermilion water
    • Two and a half qian of mandrake flower

    Grind these into a fine powder. Take two qian mixed with warm wine. If intoxicated, it's best to lie down and avoid being startled awake. For those with phlegm, first take victory gold pills. An alternative adds two qian of frankincense, prepared in the same manner.

    Defensive Water and Yellow Decoction
    This treats manic conditions without signs of cold or fever, where the pulse is floating and the patient speaks erratically without pause.
    Ingredients:

    • One qian of prepared leech
    • Three qian each of cinnamon twig and wind protective herbs
    • Two qian of licorice

    These four ingredients should be soaked in a cup of water overnight, then squeezed for the juice. Add two pounds of raw rhubarb pounded and steamed like milled rice. The juice should be mixed again and divided for consumption.

    Cattle Gall Ointment
    This treats heat entering the blood chamber leading to insanity where the person fails to recognize others.
    Ingredients:

    • Two and a half qian of cattle gall
    • Three qian each of vermilion, safflower, and peony bark
    • One qian each of brain and licorice

    Grind these ingredients into a fine powder, then mix with honey to form pills the size of soap beans, and swallow them with freshly drawn water.[72p]

    Ginseng Powder: Treats wind evil of the heart, causing ghostly speech, confusion, and disorientation. Ingredients: Dragon tooth (one tael), Ginseng, red poria, stone calamus, ghost arrow, and rhinoceros horn shavings, each seven and a half qian. Prepare by chewing the above (ingredients), and take four qian, mixed with one middle cup of water, decoct until reduced by three-tenths, strain and take warm, without regard for time.

    Poria Powder: Treats wind evil of the heart, causing hallucinations of ghostly speech, with tangible sensations and heart palpitations. Ingredients: Poria, distant wisdom (yuan zhi), yellow bitter (huang lian), and sand fruit (sha ren), each half a tael; stone calamus, ginseng, and antelope horn shavings, each seven and a half qian; forty-nine red beans; and two and a half qian of roasted licorice. Prepare by chewing the above, and take five qian with one middle cup of water, decoct until reduced by three-tenths, strain and take warm, without regard for time.

    Gold Leaf Pills: Treats wind evil of the heart, causing confusion and erratic speech, and uncertainty of will. Ingredients: Two hundred pieces of gold leaf, half a tael of greasy powder. Use a new small pot, line the bottom with gold leaf, and separate layers with powder, then add a small cup of cow's milk. Simmer over low heat until the milk evaporates and the gold leaf becomes like mud, then roast over the fire until dry, grind into powder, mix with steamed cake to form pills the size of small beans. Take five pills after meals, with fresh spring water.[73p]

    Wuling Powder (Zhong Jing): Treats emaciated individuals experiencing palpitations below the navel, excessive salivation, and dizziness due to water retention.

    Buxin Pill (Hua Tuo): Treats loss of mind due to shock, or excessive worry, causing unstable heart energy, ranting, shouting, and running about.

    Xiongci Pill: Treats wind-induced seizures leading to loss of consciousness and a sense of impending death.

    Another formula: Treats 120 types of wind epilepsy with frenzied behavior, where the person may drool and not recognize others; best taken in April or May.
    Ingredients: 2 taels each of purple quartz, peony, dragon bone (or yellow root), and green stone resin; 2 taels of white lichen skin; 2 taels of ephedra (with branches removed); 2 taels of angelica; 2 taels of licorice; 2 taels of (plant) root; 2 taels of cinnamon heart; 2 taels of ginseng; 3 taels of oyster; and 5 taels of rhubarb.

    These thirteen ingredients, crushed into a coarse powder, are divided into seven portions. Each portion is boiled with 10 large jujubes and 3 sheng of water until reduced to 2.5 sheng. After straining, add one portion to the juice of a large jujube and boil until reduced to 1 sheng, then strain and take immediately. This should be done every seven days until cured.[76p]

    Shou Xing Pill (from "Ji Sheng Fang"): Treats mental distress from illness and worry, phlegm accumulating in the heart cavity, causing lack of spirit, delirium, and inability to sleep soundly.

    　　桃核承气汤　太阳病不解，热结膀胱，其人如狂，血自下者愈。其外不解者，尚未可攻，当先解其外。外解已，但少腹结者乃可攻之，宜用此药。　　大黄四两　桂枝去皮　甘草炙　芒硝各二两　桃仁去皮尖双仁者，五十个，捶碎　　右銼如麻豆大，每服五钱匕，以水二大盏，煎至八分，去滓，下硝煎化，温服，以微利为度，未利再服。
    　　抵当丸　治畜血如狂。
