    Peach Kernel Chengqi Decoction: For Taiyang disease that does not resolve, with heat accumulating in the bladder, the patient behaves like they are insane; if blood flows downward, they will recover. If there is still no resolution from the outside, it is not yet advisable to attack; one must first resolve the exterior. Once the exterior is resolved, if there is still distention in the lower abdomen, then it can be attacked; this medicine should be used.

    Ingredients: 4 taels of Da Huang, peeled Gui Zhi, 2 taels of roasted Gan Cao, and 2 taels of Mang Xiao; 50 pieces of peach kernels (peeled and split), crushed. Prepare as follows: make it the size of a soybean, with each dose being 5 qian (coins) using 2 large cups of water, decoct until reduced to 8 parts. Remove the residue, dissolve the Mang Xiao, and take warm, aiming for a slight effect; if there is no effect, take again.

    Zhidao Pills: Treats excessive blood loss as if one is insane.

    Ingredients: Water leeches, remove the seeds and crush. The water leech reproduces and causes more harm; they must be cut and then stir-fried with lime, then decocted again. Five of the Toad Bug (Bei Zhi Wu), with wings and legs removed; four peach nuts, peeled; 3 fen of Da Huang, cleaned.

    Crush and sift to make one pill. Use one large white cup of water, decoct until reduced to 7 parts, taken at once. It is effective during the onset of bleeding; if bleeding does not occur, repeat the process. Alternatively, make pills the size of a soybean, and prepare two doses using 2 cups of water, decoct until reduced to 7 parts, remove the residue and take warm; this is named Zhi Dao Decoction.[78p]

    Tingli Bitter Wine Decoction: This treats cold damage for seven to eight days, with internal heat unresolved, leading to Yang toxicity acting wildly. Take one and a half sheng of bitter wine, half a sheng of rice vinegar, and half a sheng of fresh mugwort juice; if fresh mugwort is unavailable, use cooked mugwort juice or juice from crushed mugwort roots, along with a measure of Tingli powder. Boil together to extract seven measures, and administer in three doses.

    Yang Toxic Shengma Decoction: This treats cold damage that has transformed into Yang toxicity after one or two days, or has changed due to medication causing vomiting or diarrhea, resulting in lower back pain, agitation, flushed face with wild talk, hallucinations, or diarrhea, with a pulse that is floating and large in number, and a face flushed with spots resembling brocade. If there is throat pain with purulent blood, it can be treated within five days, but not after seven days. Use two fen of Shengma, one fen each of rhinoceros horn powder, bulbus fir, ginseng, scute, and licorice, with each ingredient shaved to the size of a large mung bean. Add three sheng of water, boil down to one and a half sheng, strain out the dregs, drink one cup and take another dose shortly after eating. Warm the hands and feet to induce sweating; if sweating occurs, it resolves the condition; if not, repeat.

    Dahuang Powder: This treats Yang toxicity from cold damage that has not resolved, with heat accumulation internally, causing a state of confusion akin to madness. Use one liang of Sichuan rhubarb, cut in half, three fen of cinnamon heart, slightly burnt licorice, twenty-one peach kernels (soaked, peeled, and split), lightly fried wheat bran until slightly yellow, and one liang each of Akebia and giant taro peel, and two liang of Sichuan Glauber’s salt. Pound these into a coarse powder; take four qian each time, using one medium cup of water, boil down to six parts, strain out the dregs, and take warm without regard to time, adjusting dosage to facilitate movement.[79p]

    Gardenia Seed Decoction treats mania from Yang toxicity.
    Gardenia seeds, Da Qing (Isatis), Anemarrhena, and Red Peony each one tael; Sheng Ma, Huang Qin, Gypsum, and Almonds (peeled and roasted until lightly yellow) each two taels; Chai Hu one and a half taels; Licorice half a tael, roasted and finely chopped.
    Crush the above into a coarse powder. Take four qian each time, with one medium cup of water, add half fen of fresh ginger and one hundred beans of fermented soybean, simmer until reduced to six parts, strain off the residue, and drink warm at any time.

    San Yi Cheng Qi Decoction treats typhoid and miscellaneous disorders, abdominal fullness, dry throat, thirst, confusion, mania, and all forms of real heat.
    Da Huang, Mang Xiao, Hou Po, and Zhi Shi each half a tael; Licorice one tael.
    Chop to the size of broad beans, with one and a half cups of water and three slices of fresh ginger, simmer until reduced to seven parts, add the Mang Xiao and simmer until boiling a few times, strain off the residue to drink.

    Huang Lian Jiedu Decoction treats typhoid and miscellaneous diseases, agitation from heat toxins, irritability, dry retching, dry mouth, groaning, shortness of breath, deep Yang collapse, and severe internal heat. Commonly misunderstood as Yin toxin.
    Huang Lian, Huang Bo, Huang Qin, and Da Zhi Zi each half a tael.
    Chop to the size of broad beans, take half a tael each time, with one small teacup of water, simmer until reduced to four parts, strain off the residue, and drink warm.[80p]

    　　加减小续命汤 【《纲目》，下同】 　治中风，或歌或哭或笑语，无所不及。　　麻黄三两　人参　白朮土炒　桂枝各二两　当归一两　杏仁去皮尖炒研　芎藭酒洗　白芍酒炒　甘草炙　黄芩酒炒　防己各八钱　　右为末，每三钱，水煎服。

    　　一醉膏　治心恙。
    　　无灰酒二碗　香油四两和匀，用杨柳枝二十条，逐条搅一二百下，候香油与酒相入成膏，煎至八分灌之，熟睡则醒，或吐下即安矣。
    　　当归承气汤　治阳厥狂癫。
    　　当归　大黄各一两　甘草半两　芒硝七钱　　右銼如麻豆大，每二两，水一大碗，姜五片，枣十枚，煎至一半，去渣热温服。若阳狂奔走，骂詈不知亲疏，此阳有余，阴不足。大黄芒硝去胃中实热，当归补血益阴，甘草缓中；加姜枣者，胃属土，此引入胃中也。经所谓微者逆之，甚者从之，此之谓也。以大利为度，微缓以瓜蒂散，入防风末、藜芦末吐之，其病立安。后用调心散、洗心散、凉膈散、解毒汤等调之。[81p]

    Add-Subtract Small Life-Preserving Decoction

    For treating stroke, whether singing, crying, or laughing, nothing is beyond reach.

    • 3 taels of Ephedra
    • 2 taels of Ginseng
    • 2 taels of Atractylodes (fried with soil)
    • 2 taels of Cinnamon Twig
    • 1 tael of Angelica
    • 8 almonds (shelled, fried and ground)
    • Aconitum (washed with wine)
    • 8 taels of White Peony (fried with wine)
    • 8 taels of Licorice (with honey)
    • 8 taels of Scutellaria (fried with wine)
    • 8 taels of Stephania

    Grind these into a powder. Take 3 qian (1/10 tael) with water decocted and taken orally.

    Intoxicated Balm

    For treating heart ailments.

    • 2 bowls of pure wine
    • 4 taels of scented oil, mixed together. Use 20 willow branches, stirring each one 100-200 times. Wait for the scented oil and wine to integrate into a balm, boil down to a solid eighth. It can be used when falling asleep, and either vomited out or settled down easily.

    Angelica Purging Decoction

    For treating Yang collapse and mania.

    • 1 tael of Angelica
    • 1 tael of Rhubarb
    • 1/2 tael of Licorice
    • 7 qian of Glauber's Salt

    Grind those to the size of broad beans. For every 2 taels, use a large bowl of water, 5 slices of ginger, and 10 jujubes, decocted to half. Remove the dregs and drink warm.

    If Yang energy is excessive, leading to running about, scolding, and not recognizing relatives, this indicates an excess of Yang and a deficiency of Yin. Rhubarb and Glauber's Salt will dispel excess heat from the stomach, Angelica nourishes blood and replenishes Yin, Licorice moderates the middle; ginger and jujubes are included because they belong to Earth, and this helps draw the remedy into the stomach. As the classics say, when the symptoms are mild, go against it; when severe, follow it—this is the principle.

    By taking a significant quantity, with a mild and slow pace, use gourd stem powder, adding Fangfeng powder and Liulian powder to induce vomiting; the illness will quickly settle. Later administer Heart-Tuning Powder, Heart-Cleansing Powder, Cooling Barrier Powder, Detoxifying Decoction, and other remedies to adjust.[81p]

    Three Liang of Da Huang, soaked in clear wine to remove the skin;

    Half Jin of Mang Xiao.

    Dried Ginger and Aconite Decoction: Treats cold damage and manic symptoms in yin conditions. Take one liang of dried ginger and one piece of aconite, peeled and broken into eight pieces. Combine these two ingredients with three sheng of water, boil until reduced to one sheng, strain and take immediately.

    Er Bai Pill: Treats diseases caused by phlegm, leading to epilepsy, mania, palpitations, and other symptoms. Use one liang of white alum and a pinch of powdered light mineral, adjusting the amount based on the condition. Wrap in a raw steamy round dough, steam until cooked, peel, form into pills, and roll in the powdered light mineral to the size of the seeds of a phoenix tree. Take two to thirty pills with ginger soup. For children, size should be like millet.

    Bi Xia Pill: Treats phlegm and mucus blockage, urgent jaw tightness, upward eye movement, epilepsy, and mania. Use half a liang of stone green, water-milled nine times, along with twenty pieces each of aconite, Chuan wu, and scorpion tails. Grind these into a powder, mix in with the stone green, form into pills the size of chicken heads. Take one pill dissolved in peppermint soup. Additionally, drink with half a cup of warm wine; shortly afterward, expectorate phlegm, and then treat with other medications according to the symptoms. If the mouth is locked, administer by opening and injecting.[83p]

    Niu Huang Qing Xin Wan treats deficiencies of heart qi, unstable mind, fear and madness, nonsensical speech, restlessness and little sleep, and even cases of abandoning clothes and running away, singing while climbing high, or jumping over walls and roofs, among other symptoms.

    Ingredients include:

    • One tael each of antelope horn, musk, and borneol;
    • Two and a half taels each of ginseng, fried shenqu, and fried cattail pollen;
    • One tael and two qian each of white poria, prepared niuhuang, chaihu, and platycodon;
    • One tael and two and a half qian each of chuanxiong, peeled bitter almond with double kernels, and fried wheat bran;
    • One and a half taels each of defatted astragalus, white peony, and ophiopogon;
    • One and a half taels each of huangqin and prepared danggui (without heads);
    • Seven and a half qian each of fried ejiao, dried ginger, and white renshen;
    • Eight qian of water-fried realgar;
    • Five taels of sliced licorice;
    • Seven taels of fried yam;
    • One and seven and a half taels each of fried soybean yellow rolls and cinnamon (without skin);
    • One thousand four hundred pieces of gold leaf;
    • One hundred steamed black jujubes, peeled and pitted, ground into paste;
    • Two taels of rhinoceros horn.

    Except for the jujubes, almonds, and gold leaf, grind the niuhuang, borneol, musk, and realgar into fine powder, mix with the remaining herbs, incorporate honey into the jujube paste to form pills, making ten pills for every two taels. Encase each with gold leaf. Take one pill after meals with warm water.[84p]

    Clear Heart Nourishing Blood Decoction: Treats heart deficiency and mania.
    Add the following ingredients, each weighing one qian: ginseng, white atractylodes, poria, distant wisdom, fried jujube seed; and each weighing one qian and five fen: angelica sinensis; five fen of licorice. Grind the above into a powder, add five longan fruits, two cups of water, and simmer until reduced to one cup. Consume on an empty stomach.

    He Che Wan: Treats long-term heart wind epilepsy due to deficiency of both qi and blood.
    Use as much purple river car as desired, thoroughly baked and dried. Grind into a powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a wutong seed. Take seventy pills with liquor on an empty stomach.

    Kai Mi San: Treats women's epilepsy, characterized by singing at all times and climbing over walls and roofs, resulting from blood stagnation in the heart membrane.
    Ingredients: each weighing one qian—angelica sinensis, fried white atractylodes, white peony root, sappan wood, safflower; each weighing eight fen—bupleurum, white poria; seven qian of prepared licorice; each weighing one qian and five fen—peach kernel, distant wisdom, fresh rehmannia root. Grind these, decoct with fresh ginger for consumption; alternatively, prepare pills with honey, coated with cinnabar.

    Fang Feng Tong Sheng San: Treats all forms of mania and sudden wind disease.
    Ingredients: each weighing four fen—fang feng, chuanxiong, angelica sinensis, white peony, rhubarb, mirabilite, forsythia; a whole ephedra without removing the nodes; peppermint; each weighing eight fen—gypsum, balloonflower, and yellow qin; two qian and four fen of talc; two fen each of white atractylodes, gardenia seed, and schizonepeta. One qian of prepared licorice. Grind the ingredients, add three slices of fresh ginger, two cups of water, and simmer to one cup. Consume warm.[86p]

    Yujin Pill (from "Liangfang") - Treats heart disturbances and wind-initiated disorders.
    Ingredients:

    • Yujin (Curcuma) seven liang
    • White alum three liang

    Grind the above into a fine powder, form into pills the size of a wutong seed, take sixty pills at a time, wash down with soup or water, and take at any time. Those suffering from madness for several years will recover after taking this. When someone first takes it, they may feel a sensation in the chest as if something has been expelled, and after taking it again, they will revive. This condition arises from worry and phlegm obstructing the heart orifices.

    Huangshi Powder (Yang Family Collection) - Treats wind-induced madness.
    Ingredients:

    • Dog liver, one, opened
    • Yellow lead
    • Sal ammoniac, each two and a half qian

    Mix the two ingredients well and stuff them into the liver, binding securely with麻 (hemp). Use one liter of water to boil until well cooked, chew finely, and swallow with the original juice. [87p]

    Clearing Heart Decoction: Treats heat evil affecting the heart, making one speak wildly and lose normal movement. Ingredients: equal parts of Huang Lian, Huang Qin, Bo He, Lian Qiao, Zhi Zi Ren, Gan Cao, Da Huang, and Mang Xiao. Prepare with half a cup of water and ten bamboo leaves, simmer down to eight parts and take warm.

    Baodan Pills: Treats all types of mania and epilepsy in men and women, as well as postpartum seizures in women, and excessive anxiety in virgins during menstruation. Taking this medicine often yields results. Ingredients: two taels of Zhu Sha, one and a half taels of black lead, finely ground Frankincense, and one tael of mercury. Combine lead in a pan, add mercury to form sand, then add Frankincense and pound evenly with a willow stick while hot. Form pills the size of a chicken egg. Take one pill on an empty stomach with well water. Avoid disturbance during sleep; if you wake up, remain calm. Take another pill to eliminate the root cause.

    Wudang Pills: Treats wild mania and epilepsy that causes wandering thoughts. Ingredients: one piece each of sheep bile, pig bile, dog bile, chicken bile, and carp bile, combined to catch the juice. Five taels of snake gall, calcined red, add the bile juice until the prescribed dose is reached. Grind to powder, and form pills the size of a Mung bean, coated with Zhu Sha. Take fifteen pills after meals, swallowed with sharpened knife juice; alternatively, use the powder mixed with sharpened knife water for ingestion.

    Duomeng Dan: Treats epilepsy with excessive phlegm. Use one tael of Qing Meng Shi mixed with one tael of fire nitrate, refined until golden. Grind to powder, taking one qian at a time, mixed with natural mint juice and honey for ingestion. After a while, the medicine naturally expels phlegm. In severe cases, three doses may cure.[88p]

    Niu Huang Pill treats epilepsy, wind mania, heart wind, evil spirit startling the heart, lack of awareness, episodic outbursts, drooling on the ground, and self-unconsciousness.

    Ingredients:

    • Niu Huang, Pearl, Musk, Mercury, each 5 fen;
    • Cinnabar, Dragon Tooth, separately ground;
    • Rhino Horn, Amber each 2 qian;
    • Ginseng, Fuling, Tianmendong, and Maimen Dong (core removed) each 4 qian;
    • Fang Feng, Huang Qin, Zhi Mu, Long Dan Cao, Shi Chang Pu, Quan Xie, Shao Yao, Gan Cao, each 5 liang;
    • Lu Feng Fang 3 qian;
    • Gold and Silver Foil each 70 sheets.

    Except for the separately ground medicines, mix the rest into a fine powder, combine well, mix with processed honey and pound until the size of large apricots. Take 15 pills after meals in the evening, with tea made from young bamboo leaves.

    Wu Ba Pill treats frantic mania with continuous shouting.

    Ingredients:

    • 5 Wu Mei;
    • 5 Ba Dou, processed to powder.

    Combine the two, make pills the size of millet, coat with cinnabar. Adults should take 3 to 5 pills before sleep, accompanied by clear soup. If three or four pills are ingested, white porridge should stop it.

    Zheng Xin Decoction treats long-standing emotional disturbances and confusion, heart wind, nonsensical speech and laughter, lack of awareness of suffering.

    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng, Fuling, Dang Gui (washed in wine), Sheng Di Huang (washed in wine), each 1 qian;
    • Antelope Horn powder, Gan Cao roasted, Jujube seed fried and ground, Yuan Zhi each 8 fen.

    Macerate, add 2 cups of water, 7 lotus seeds, boil down to 7 parts, strain, then mix in antelope horn powder and 1 fen of musk, and consume after meals at bedtime.[89p]

    Qingxin Pill: Treats heart affected by evil spirits, leading to disorientation, wild talk and shouting, and restless sleep. It consists of one qian each of ginseng, raw rehmannia, turmeric, and tianma; two qian each of zhush
    a and niudan nansheng. Grind to a powder, steam into pills the size of millet, coat with zhush
    a, and take thirty pills with ginseng decoction.

    Jin Yin Ding Zhi Decoction: Treats loss of will due to heart wind, with nonsensical behavior and speech. It consists of one qian each of soaked angelica, ginseng, and yi zhi; seven fen each of licorice, poria, and stone calamus; fifteen berries of schisandra; and five fen each of powdered amber and antelope horn. Prepare the amber and horn separately, boil with two dou of water and one liang each of gold and silver until reducing to eight parts, strain, then mix in the powdered amber and horn, and take uniformly.

    Amber and Poria Syrup: Treats loss of spirit, gradually leading to heart wind. It consists of one liang of ginseng, half liang of dried tangerine peel, two liang of angelica (soaked in wine), boiled into a thin syrup; two liang of white poria, ground into powder; half liang of amber, ground separately. Mix the ginseng syrup with the powders of amber and poria until uniform. If too thick, add honey to adjust. Take two to three spoonfuls, chew and swallow, and taking before sleep is also beneficial.[90p]

    Return of the Spirit Elixir

    This remedy treats all cases of fright and anxiety, excessive thinking and forgetfulness, insufficient heart energy, epilepsy, and mania.

    Ingredients:

    • Two pieces of wild boar heart, sliced
    • Two taels of large red cinnabar
    • Three taels of lampwick

    Preparation:
    Combine these ingredients; boil them in a stone pot once. Grind the cinnabar into powder, mix in two taels of Polygala root powder, and form small pills the size of a tung seed. Take them in doses of nine, fifteen, or twenty-five pills, swallowed with Ophiopogon decoction. In severe cases, take with a decoction of frankincense and ginseng.

    Great Tonifying Yuan Decoction

    This remedy treats severe damage to qi and blood, loss of spirit, and symptoms of mania.

    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng: 1-2 qian (coins) (lesser) or 1-2 liang (more)
    • Mountain cornel: 1 qian
    • Fried Chinese yam: 2 qian
    • Eucommia bark: 2 qian
    • Angelica sinensis and goji berries: 2-3 qian each
    • Cooked Rehmannia: 2-3 qian (lesser) or 2-3 liang (more)
    • Honey-fried licorice: 1-2 qian

    Preparation:
    Use two sheng (containers) of water, boil down to seven parts, and take it warm after meals.

    Great Harmony Decoction

    This remedy treats food stagnation and accumulation, symptoms of mania.

    Ingredients:

    • Aged tangerine peel: 1-2 qian
    • Bitter orange: 1 qian
    • Sand cardamom: 5 fen (tenths)
    • Hawthorn berry and malt: 2 qian each
    • Magnolia bark and Alisma: 1.5 qian each

    Preparation:
    Use one and a half sheng of water, boil down to seven or eight parts, and take it warm after meals.[91p]

    Seven Blessings Brew
    For those suffering from madness and symptoms of blood deficiency, this remedy can effectively treat both conditions, truly embodying the essence of the royal path.

    • Ingredients:
      • Ginseng: appropriate amount
      • Cooked Rehmannia: appropriate amount
      • Angelica: 2-3 qian
      • Apricot kernel: 2 qian
      • Fried Atractylodes: 1.5 qian
      • Honey-fried Licorice: 1 qian
      • Polygala: 3-5 fen, prepared
      • Water: 2 zhong, decoct to 7 parts, consume warm on an empty stomach. Optional: add 3-5 slices of fresh ginger.

    Two Yin Decoction
    Treats symptoms of heat in the heart, including anxiety, loss of will, excessive talking and laughing, and is suitable for these conditions.

    • Ingredients:
      • Fresh Rehmannia: 2-3 qian
      • Ophiopogon: 2-3 qian
      • Fried Ziziphus: 2 qian
      • White Poria: 1.5 qian
      • Original Licorice: 1.5 qian
      • Akebia: 1.5 qian
      • Huang Lian: 1-2 qian
      • Licorice: 1 qian
      • Water: 2 zhong, with 20 strands of lamp wick and bamboo leaves if desired, decoct to 7 parts, consume warm on an empty stomach.

    Liu'an Decoction
    Treats symptoms of phlegm stagnation and reversed qi, including madness.

    • Ingredients:
      • Dried Tangerine Peel: 1.5 qian
      • Pinellia: 2-3 qian
      • Poria: 2 qian
      • Licorice: 1 qian
      • Apricot kernel (peeled tip removed): 1 qian
      • White Mustard Seed: 5-7 fen, avoid for the elderly and weak
      • Water: 1.5 zhong, add 3-5 slices of fresh ginger, decoct to 7 parts, consume warm on an empty stomach.

    Chou Xin Yin: For treating various types of mania and madness, where the fire is too intense and should not be supplemented. Ingredients: Huangqin, Shihu, Mutong, Zhizi (fried) each 1-2 qian; Zhike, Zexie each 0.5 qian; Xigancao 0.3 qian. Use 1.5 sheng of water, decoct to 7 parts, and take warm after meals. For severe internal heat, cool consumption is better.

    Qing Ge Jian: For treating phlegm due to fire disturbance, causing qi obstruction, breathlessness and fullness, internal heat, irritability and thirst, mania, and other symptoms. Ingredients: Chenpi 0.5 qian; Beimu 2-3 qian, lightly crushed; Danzhu 1-2 qian; Haishi 2 qian; Baijiezi 5-7 fen; Mutong 2 qian. Use 1.5 sheng of water, decoct to 7 parts, and take warm.

    Fu Man Jian: This formula's properties are extremely light and clear, entering the heart and liver organs, promoting qi flow, relieving stagnation, opening blockages, enlightening the spirit, nourishing the right, and eliminating evil, demonstrating remarkable efficacy. Ingredients: Shengdi, Maidong, Shaoyao, Shichangpu, Shihu, Danpi, Fushen each 2 qian; Chenpi 1 qian; Mutong, Zhimu each 1.5 qian. Use 1.5 sheng of water, decoct to 7 parts, and take after meals.

    Yuqian San: Also known as Yiliu Ganlu San, for treating internal heat of Yangming, mania, and other symptoms. Ingredients: Shengshigao 6 liang; Fengancao 1 liang. Grind finely into powder; each time take 1-3 qian, mix with fresh spring water, hot soup, or ginseng soup for consumption. Adding 3 qian of zhushā is also excellent.[93p]

    癫狂门

    　　　　　单方

    　　凡狂癫，谬乱不识人：伏龙肝末，水服方寸匕，每日三服。 【《千金方》】
    　　失心风疾：水银一两，藕节八个，研成砂子，丸如芡子大，每服二丸，磨刀水下，一二服。【经验方】
    　　病笑不休：沧盐煅赤研，入河水煎沸啜之，探吐热痰数升，即愈。 【《儒门事亲》】
    　　卒发癫狂：葶苈一升，捣三千杵，取白犬血和丸麻子大，酒服一丸，三服取瘥。 【《肘后方》】
    　　风癫发作则吐，耳如蝉鸣，引胁牵痛：天门冬去心皮，暴捣为末，酒服方寸匕，日三服，久服良。【《外台秘要》】
    　　癫痫风疾：九节菖蒲，不闻鸡犬声者，去毛，木臼捣末，以黑獖猪心一个批开，砂罐煮汤，调服三钱，每日三服。【《正传》】
    　　风癫百病：麻子四升，水一升，猛火煮令芽生，去渣煎取二升，空心服之。或发或不发，或多言语，勿怪之，但令人摩手足，须臾即定。凡进三剂无不愈。【《千金方》】[94p]

    Madness and Mania Treatments

    Single Prescription

    1. For mania and madness, when one cannot recognize people: Grind dragon liver into powder, take it with a small amount of water, three doses daily. [From "Thousand Gold Prescriptions"]

    2. For loss of mind due to wind disease: One tael of mercury, eight lotus stalks, grind into sand, form into pills the size of a gourd seed, take two pills with water, one or two times. [From "Experience Prescriptions"]

    3. For incessant laughter: Grind calcined salt until red, boil in river water and drink it until hot phlegm is expelled; after expelling several liters, one is cured. [From "Confucian Family Teachings"]

    4. For sudden onset of madness: One sheng of lepyrous, pound with three thousand pestles, mix with white dog blood and form pills the size of sesame seeds, take one pill with wine, three doses will bring recovery. [From "Elbow Post Prescription"]

    5. For mania triggered by wind, manifested by vomiting, and pain similar to cicadas buzzing in the ears: Remove the heart from the asparagaceae, pound it into powder, take with a small amount of wine, three doses daily; prolonged use is beneficial. [From "Essential Secrets of the External Repository"]

    6. For epilepsy due to wind disease: Use nine-segmented sweet flag, ensure there is no crowing of roosters or barking of dogs; remove the fur, pound it in a wooden mortar, open a black pig’s heart, boil in a clay pot to make soup, take three qian daily, in three doses. [From "Authentic Transmissions"]

    7. For mania from wind and various ailments: Four sheng of adzuki beans, one sheng of water, boil over fierce heat until sprouts appear, remove the residue, extract two sheng of decoction, take on an empty stomach. Whether paroxysms occur or one speaks excessively, do not blame; just have them rub their limbs, and they will settle momentarily. Generally, after three doses, all will be cured. [From "Thousand Gold Prescriptions"][94p]

    　　风痰癫疾：茶芽、栀子各一两，煎浓汁一碗服，良久即吐。 【《摘元方》】
    　　风癫：用地黄三十斤，天门冬十斤，二味捣取汁，作煎，服之瘥。 【《千金方》，下同】　　又方：莨菪子三升捣筛，酒一斗，渍半日绞去滓，汤中煎，令可丸。先食服如小豆二丸，加至如梧子二丸，以知为度。额上手中从文理中赤起，是知也。无此候更服。病日发者三日愈，间日发者十日愈，五日发者二十日愈，半岁发者一月愈。
    　　狂邪风癫，不避水火：苦参五斤，蜜和丸如酸枣大，每服十丸，薄荷汤化下。 【《纲目》】　　又方：令患人着地仰卧，以冷水终日淋其面，良。
    　　癫痫瘈瘲：飞鸱头二枚、铅丹一斤为末，蜜丸梧子大，先食服三丸，日三；剧者夜一，稍加之。【《千金方》】
    　　风狂歌笑，行走不休：用豭猪肉一斤，煮熟切脍，和酱食，或羹粥炒任服之。 【《心镜》】[95p]

    Wind phlegm epilepsy: One tael each of tea buds and gardenia, decoct into a thick soup and take one bowl; soon, it will induce vomiting.

    Wind epilepsy: Use thirty jin of rehmannia and ten jin of asparagus; pound to extract the juice, prepare a decoction, and taking it will cure.

    Another method: Three sheng of datura seeds; pound and sift, then soak in one斗 of wine for half a day and strain, decoct in soup until it can be formed into pills. Take initially two small pills, increasing to two walnut-sized pills as one sees fit. If there is a redness appearing on the forehead or palms, that is a sign. If not, do not take more. For symptoms that appear daily, recovery in three days; for symptoms appearing every other day, recovery in ten days; for symptoms appearing every five days, recovery in twenty days; for symptoms every half year, recovery in one month.

    For manic wind epilepsy that does not avoid water or fire: Five jin of bitter root mixed into pills the size of sour jujubes; take ten pills at a time, dissolving them in mint soup.

    Another method: Have the patient lie on the ground face up and pour cold water on their face all day, and it will be good.

    For epilepsy and spasms: Two pieces of owl heads and one jin of lead powder, ground to a fine powder, mixed into honey into walnut-sized pills; initially take three pills before meals, three times a day; for severe cases, one at night, gradually increasing.

    For wind mania causing laughter, singing, and restlessness: Use one jin of pork from a wild boar, cook it well and chop finely, mix with sauce to eat, or prepare as a stew or porridge and eat as desired.[95p]

    　　风疾恍惚，心烦腹痛，或时闷绝复苏：以青羚羊角屑微炒为末，无时温酒服一钱。 【《圣惠方》】
    　　凡狂发欲走，或自高贵称神，或悲泣呻吟，此为邪祟。以蚕纸烧灰，酒水任下方寸匕。亦可治风癫。【《肘后方》】
    　　久癫失志，气血虚弱者：用河车治净，烂煮食之。 【经验方】
    　　伤寒发狂，逾垣上屋：寒水石二钱、黄连一钱为末，煎甘草冷服，名鹊石散。 【《本事方》】
    　　风热心躁，口干狂言，浑身壮热：寒水石半斤，烧半日，净地坑内，盆合四面，湿土壅起，经宿取出，入甘草末、天竺黄各二两，龙脑二分，糯米糕丸弹子大，蜜水磨下。【《集验方》】
    　　伤寒发狂，惊怖恍惚：用撒法郎二分，水一盏，浸一夕服之。天方国人所传。 【《医林集要》】
    　　癫狂邪疾：防葵研末，温酒服一刀圭，至二三服，身瞤及小不仁为效。 【《肘后方》】[96p]

    • For sudden wind and confusion, with anxiety and abdominal pain, sometimes in a state of fainting and recovery: use finely roasted powder of blue antelope horn, take one qian with warm wine at any time.
    • For madness that desires to run away, whether claiming divinity or expressing sorrow through weeping and moaning, this is due to evil spirits. Burn silkworm paper to ash, mix with wine to drink as needed. This also treats wind madness.
    • For prolonged madness leading to loss of ambition and weak qi and blood: use river cart to cleanse it, boil it thoroughly for food.
    • For madness due to febrile disease and climbing over walls: use two qian of cold water stone and one qian of yellow bitter as powder, decoct with licorice to drink cold; it is called Magpie Stone Powder.
    • For wind-heat restlessness of the heart, dry mouth, and wild speech with fever: use half a jin of cold water stone, burn for half a day, place in a pit on clean ground, cover it with a basin on all four sides, mound the moist earth overnight, then take out and add two liang each of licorice powder and bezoar, two fen of dragon brain, form into balls the size of a glutinous rice cake, and take with honey water.
    • For febrile madness, confusion due to fear: use two fen of safflower, one cup of water, soak overnight and drink. This is transmitted by the people of Tianfang.
    • For madness from evil illness: grind the seeds of the防葵 plant into powder, take one dagger-shaped piece with warm wine, until two or three doses have been taken, manifesting effects with tremors and slight numbness.[96p]

    　　卒发狂癫：烧自经死绳末，水服三指撮，陈蒲煮汁服亦佳。 【藏器】
    　　伤寒发狂，烦躁热极：吞生鸡子一枚，效。 【《食鉴》】
    　　伤寒时气温病六七日，热气发狂，见鬼欲走：取白狗从背破取血，乘热摊胸上，冷乃去之。此治垂死者亦活。无白犬，但纯色者亦可。【《肘后方》】
    　　热病发狂，奔走似癫，如见鬼神，久不得汗，及不知人事者：以人中黄入大罐内，以泥固济煅半日，去火毒研末，新汲水服三钱，未退再服。【《斗门方》】
    　　大热狂渴：干陈人屎为末，于阴地净黄土中作五六寸小坑，将末三两匙，于坑中以新汲水调匀，良久澄清，细细与饮即解，世俗谓之地清。【寇宗奭《衍义》】
    　　人魄：镇心安神魄，定惊怖癫狂，磨水服之。 【时珍】
    　　胞衣水：主治狂言妄语，头上无故发竖，虚痞等证，天行热病，饮之立效。 【藏器】[97p]

    • For sudden madness: burning oneself to death with a rope at the end of the year, or taking three fingers of water, or drinking boiled juice from the herb Chenpu is also good.

    • For madness caused by typhoid fever, extreme agitation, and heat: swallowing a raw egg can be effective.

    • During the period of typhoid fever, lasting six or seven days with an influx of heat causing madness, seeing ghosts and wanting to flee: take blood from a white dog by cutting its back, apply it while warm to the chest, and remove it once it cools. This treatment can also revive those near death; if a white dog is not available, a dog of a pure color will suffice.

    • For madness arising from heat illness, running about crazily as if seeing ghosts, long without sweating, and being unaware of people and events: put human bile into a large container, mix it with clay and bake it for half a day, then grind it into a powder and dilute with fresh water, taking three taels. If symptoms do not subside, take more.

    • For extreme heat and crazy thirst: grind dried human feces into a powder, dig a small pit about five or six inches deep in clean yellow soil in a shaded area, place three spoonfuls of the powder in the pit, mix it well with fresh water, and after a while, let it settle. Gradually give it to drink to alleviate the condition; it is commonly referred to as 'earth clarity'.

    • For calming the mind and settling the spirit, preventing fear and madness: grind and drink with water.

    • Amniotic fluid: mainly used for treating wild speech and nonsensical talk, hair standing up without reason, and symptoms like distended feelings; effective against heat diseases when consumed.[97p]

    　　乌头、附子尖为末，茶服半钱，吐风痰癫痫。 【时珍】
    　　狐肉羹：洽惊痫恍惚，语言错谬，歌笑无度，及五脏积冷，蛊毒寒热诸病。用狐肉一片，及五脏治净，入豉汁煮熟，入五味作羹，或作粥食。京中以羊骨汁鲫鱼代豉汁，亦妙。【《心镜》】
    　　银屑：主治热狂惊悸发痫，水磨服之，功胜紫雪。 【《开宝》】
    　　吐癫狂方：此方可代瓜蒂三圣散之属。凡邪实上焦，或痰或食，或气逆不通等证，皆可以此吐之。用萝卜子捣碎，以温汤和搅，取淡汤徐徐饮之，少顷即当吐出。即有吐不尽者，亦必从下行矣。　　又法：萝卜子为末，温水调服一匙，良久吐涎沫愈。　　又法：用盐少许，于热锅中炒红色，乃入以水，煮至将滚未滚之际，搅匀，试其滋味稍淡，乃可饮之。每用半碗，渐次增饮，自然发吐，以去病为度而止。
    　　癫风：用鲤鱼一尾，制净切成块，以明矾四两为末，腌二日，煎吃，其疾必愈。　　又方：以铁浆服之。[98p]

    Aconite and Fuzi powdered, taken with half a coin of tea, expels wind, phlegm, and treats epilepsy.

    Fox meat soup: Effective for sudden seizures, confusion, erroneous speech, excessive laughter, and accumulation of cold in the five organs, as well as various ailments from poison or heat. Use a slice of fox meat, cleanse the five organs, cook it with fermented soy sauce, and make it into a soup with five flavors, or make it into porridge. In the capital, sheep bone soup and crucian carp are used instead of fermented soy sauce, which is also excellent.

    Silver flakes: Used to treat heat, frenzy, palpitations, and seizures; ground in water, it works better than Zixue.

    Epilepsy vomiting remedy: This formula can replace varieties of Guadi Sansheng Powder. Any pathogenic factors in the upper burner, whether phlegm, food, or obstructed Qi, can be expelled using this. Crush radish seeds, mix with warm water, and drink the diluted soup slowly; after a while, it will induce vomiting. If unable to expel completely, it must pass out through the lower pathway.

    Another method: Radish seeds powdered, take a spoon mixed with warm water; after a long time, one may expel saliva and foam successfully.

    Another method: Take a small amount of salt, fry it in a hot pot until it turns red, then add water, and boil just before boiling. Stir evenly, taste to ensure it is slightly bland, and then it can be drunk. Use half a bowl, gradually increase the intake, and it will naturally induce vomiting; stop once the illness is alleviated.

    For epilepsy: Use one carp, clean and cut into pieces, and crush four taels of alum into powder; marinate for two days, then boil and consume; the illness will surely be cured.

    Another remedy: Take with iron syrup.[98p]

    　　癫狂大叫奔走：用虾蟆一只，去腹中物，洗净，将肠胃复入腹中，入罐固济煅红，土掩定，隔夜取出，入麝香一分，同研极细，每服一钱新汲水下。
    　　暴狂：以朱砂末酒调服方寸匕，日三次。
    　　　　针灸

    　　《素问》曰：病在诸阳脉，且寒且热，诸分且寒且热，名曰狂。刺之虚脉，视分尽热，病已止。　　病初发，岁一发不治，月一发不治。月四五发，名曰癫病。刺诸分诸脉，其无寒者，以针调之，病止。[病止：原作「病已止」，据《素问　长刺节论》改。]　　肝热病者，小便先黄，腹痛多卧，身热，热争则狂言及惊，胁满痛，手足躁，不得安卧。庚辛甚，甲乙大汗。气逆则庚辛死。刺足厥阴少阳。其逆则头痛员员，脉引冲头也。　　《灵枢》曰：足阳明之别，名曰丰隆，去踝八寸，别走太阴；其别者循胫骨外廉，上络头项，合诸经之气，下络喉嗌。其病气逆则喉痹卒喑；实则狂癫；虚则足不收，胫枯，取之所别也。[99p]

    A person in a frenzy shouts and runs: take one toad, extract its innards, clean them, return the intestines to the abdomen, put it in a jar, seal it tightly, and after a night, take it out. Add one part musk and grind it finely. Every dose should be taken with one penny of freshly drawn water.

    For violent mania: mix powdered cinnabar with wine and take with a small knife, three times a day.

    Acupuncture

    The "Su Wen" states: when illness affects the various yang channels, accompanied by both cold and heat, in the various divisions, also presenting cold and heat, it is named mania. Needle the empty channels, observe the divisions; when excessive heat is evident, the illness will stop. If the illness initially occurs and is untreated once a year or monthly, with four to five episodes a month, it is called epilepsy. Needle into the various divisions and channels; of those without cold, adjust with needles, and the illness will cease. [The term "illness has stopped" originally read "the illness has stopped," revised according to the "Su Wen, on Long Needling."] Those with liver-fire conditions will have yellow urine at first, abdominal pain requiring rest, body heat, delusions, and agitation, fullness and pain in the flanks, restlessness in hands and feet, and inability to lie still. Excess of metal (Geng and Xin) leads to great sweating. If the qi is counterflowing, it leads to severe conditions. Needle the foot's jueyin and shaoyang. If counterflowing, headaches result, with a pulse surging toward the head.

    The "Ling Shu" states: the branch of the foot yangming, named "Fenglong," is located eight inches above the ankle and branches to the taiyin; its branch follows the outer edge of the tibia, links to the head and neck, and connects with the energies of the various channels, descending to interweave with the throat. When the illness manifests as qi counterflowing, it results in throat obstruction leading to sudden muteness; when excessive, it leads to mania and frenzy; when deficient, it causes the feet to be unresponsive and the shins to wither, found at the location of the branch.[99p]

    　　癫疾始生，先不乐，头重痛，视举目赤甚作极，已而烦心，候之于颜，取手太阳阳明太阴，血变而止。　　癫疾始作而引口啼呼喘悸者，候之手阳明太阳，左强者攻其右，右强者攻其左，血变而止。　　癫疾始作，先反僵，因而脊痛，候之足太阳阳明太阴、手太阳，血变而止。　　治癫疾者，常与之居，察其所当取之处，病至视之[之：原作「其」，据《灵枢　癫狂》改。]，有过者泻之，置其血于瓠壶之中，至其发时，血独动矣；不动，灸穷骨二十壮。穷骨者，骶骨也。　　筋癫疾者，身倦挛急，大刺项大经之大杼脉。呕多沃沫，气下泄，不治。　　脉癫疾者，暴仆，四肢之脉皆胀而纵，脉满，尽刺之出血；不满，灸之挟项太阳，灸带脉于腰相去三寸，诸分肉本输。呕多沃沫，气下泄，不治。　　狂始生，先自悲也，喜忘苦怒善恐者，得之忧饥，治之取手太阴阳明，血变而止；及取足太阴阳明。[100p]

    When a fit begins, it starts with a lack of joy, a heavy headache, and intense redness in the eyes when looking up. Afterward, there is restlessness and facial changes; one should feel the pulse at the Sun and Yangming points, and once the blood changes, it stops.

    If a fit starts and is accompanied by crying or panting, feel the pulse at the Yangming and Sun points—if the left is strong, attack the right, and if the right is strong, attack the left; once the blood changes, it stops.

    When a fit begins, it initially causes stiffness followed by spinal pain. Feel at the foot points of Sun and Yangming, and the hand points of Sun; once the blood changes, it stops.

    For treating fits, remain close to the patient, observe where treatment should be applied. When the fit arises, examine; if there is excess, drain it, and place the blood in a gourd. When the episode occurs, if the blood moves on its own, it is effective; if not, perform moxibustion at the coccyx twenty times. "The coccyx" refers to the tailbone.

    In cases of muscle fits, there will be fatigue and spasms; perform deep needling at the major points of the governing vessels. If there is vomiting and excessive foaming, and the qi is leaking down, it indicates a worse prognosis.

    In pulse fits, there may be sudden collapse with distended pulses in all four limbs; if the pulse is full, deeply needle to draw blood; if it is not full, perform moxibustion at the points near the neck of the Sun, and moxibustion three inches from the waist along the belt channel. If there is vomiting and excessive foaming, and the qi is leaking down, it indicates a worse prognosis.

    When mania first arises, it starts with sorrow and then forgets joy and bitterness; anger manifests as good fear leading to worries and hunger. Treatment seeks the points of the Taiyin and Yangming on the hands and feet; once the blood changes, it stops.[100p]

    　　狂始发，少卧不饥，自高贤也，自辩志也，自尊贵也，善骂詈，日夜不休。治之取手阳明太阳太阴，舌下少阴。视之盛者，皆取之。不盛，释之也。　　狂言，惊，善笑，好歌乐，妄行不休者，得之大恐，治之取手阳明太阳太阴。　　狂，目妄见，耳妄闻，善呼者，少气之所生也，治之取手太阳太阴阳明、足太阴、头两顑。　　狂者多食，善见鬼神，善笑而不发于外者，得之有所大喜，治之取足太阴太阳阳明，后取手太阴太阳阳明。　　狂而新发，未应如此者，先取曲泉左右动脉，及盛者见血，有顷已。不已，以法取之。灸骨骶二十壮。　　热病数惊，瘈瘲而狂，取之脉，以第四针，急泻有余者。　　癫疾毛发去，索血于心，不得索之水。水者肾也。[101p]

    When mania begins, one sleeps little and is not hungry; this comes from a high sense of worth, self-assertion, and self-respect. Those who are good at speaking abusively do so without rest, day and night. To treat this, one should use the hands in the Yangming, Sun, and Taiyin meridians, and the tongue in the Shaoyin. For those who are in a state of excess, take from them. If it is not excessive, let it go.

    Manic speech causes surprise, laughter, and an unending desire to sing; those who act recklessly will experience great fear. To treat this, one should use the hands in the Yangming, Sun, and Taiyin meridians.

    Those in a manic state see inaccurately with the eyes and hear inaccurately with the ears; those who call out are born of a lack of energy. To treat this, use the hands in the Sun, Taiyin, and Yangming channels, the feet in the Taiyin, and the head at the two temples.

    A manic person often eats a lot, sees spirits and gods, and laughs without openly expressing it; they find great joy. To treat this, use the feet in the Taiyin, Sun, and Yangming channels, and later use the hands in the Taiyin, Sun, and Yangming.

    If mania occurs suddenly and excessively, it should not be treated in this way. First, take from the left and right arteries of the Ququan point, particularly if there is an excess of blood, which happens after a while. If it does not stop, use methods to treat it. Moxibustion on the sacral bones to strengthen twenty times.

    In cases of heat illness with repeated fright, with raving mania, check the pulse and use the fourth needle; if there is excessive diarrhea, be urgent in treatment.

    In cases of epilepsy, where hair is lost and blood is sought from the heart, do not seek it in the water. Water pertains to the kidneys.[101p]

    　　大热遍身，狂而妄见妄闻妄言，视足阳明及大络取之，虚者补之，血而实者泻之。因其偃卧，居其头前，以两手四指，挟按颈动脉，久持之，卷而切之，下至缺盆中，而复止如前，热去乃止。此所谓推而散之者也。　　《甲乙经》曰：癫疾呕沫，神庭及兑端、承浆主之；其不呕沫，本神及百会、后顶、玉枕、天冲、大杼、曲骨、尺泽、阳溪、外丘、当上脘旁五分、通谷、金门、承筋、合阳主之。合阳在委中下二寸。　　癫疾，上星主之，先取譩嘻，后取天牖、风池。　　癫疾呕沫，暂起僵仆，恶见风寒，面赤肿，顖会主之。　　癫疾，狂走瘈瘲，摇头，口喎戾，颈强，强间主之。　　癫疾，瘈瘲狂走，颈项痛，后顶主之。后顶在项后一寸五分。　　癫疾，骨酸眩狂，瘈瘲，口噤 【《千金》作喉噤】 羊鸣，刺脑户。　　癫疾，僵仆目妄见，恍惚不乐，狂走瘈瘲，络却主之。　　癫疾大瘦，脑空主之。[102p]

    Intense heat spreads throughout the body, causing delusions, reckless visions, and irrational words. For conditions affecting the Yangming meridian and the great network, supplement the deficient areas and drain the excessive blood. When the patient lies down, position them with their head forward, using both hands and four fingers to press on the carotid artery for an extended period. Roll and apply pressure down to the suprasternal notch and then release, repeating until the heat dissipates. This is known as dispersing the heat.

    The "Classic of Simple Cures" states: For seizures with foam at the mouth, the points Shen ting, Dui duan, and Cheng jiang are to be treated; if there is no foam, treat the points Shen and Bai hui, Hou ding, Yu zhen, Tian chong, Da zhu, Qu gu, Chi ze, Yang xi, Wai qiu, the area above the upper epigastrium, Tong gu, Jin men, Cheng jin, and He yang. He yang is located two inches below the center of the popliteal fossa.

    For seizures, the point Shang xing is to be treated first, followed by Tian you and Feng chi.

    In case of seizures with foam at the mouth, there may be sudden collapse, an aversion to wind and cold, and facial redness and swelling, with Shao hui being the main point.

    In seizures with mad running and spasms, with head shaking, a crooked mouth, and a stiff neck, the main point is Qiang jian.

    In seizures with mad running and neck pain, the point Hou ding is to be treated, which is located one and a half inches behind the neck.

    In seizures with bone aches and dizziness, spasms, and a locked mouth (as recorded in "Thousand Gold" as 'locked throat'), the point Ci nao hu is to be treated.

    In seizures with collapse, seeing illusions, a lack of joy, mad running and spasms, the main point is Luo que.

    For severe seizures with significant weight loss, the point Nao kong is to be treated.[102p]

    　　癫疾，僵仆狂疟，完骨及风池主之。　　癫疾互引，天柱主之。
    　　癫疾，怒欲杀人 【《千金》又云瘈瘲身热狂走，谵语见鬼，】 身柱主之。　　狂走癫疾，脊急强，目转上插，筋俞主之。　　癫疾发如狂走者，面皮厚敦敦不治，虚则头重，洞泄淋癃，大小便难，腰尻重，难起居，长强主之。　　癫疾，憎风时振寒，不得言，得寒益甚，身热狂走，欲自杀，目反妄见，瘈瘲，泣出，死不知人，肺俞主之。　　癫疾，憎风时振寒，不得言，得寒益甚，身热狂走，欲自杀，目反妄见，瘈瘲，泣出，死不知人，肺俞主之。　　癫疾互引，水沟及龂交主之。[103p]

    Epilepsy, convulsions, and madness are governed by the "Wangu" and "Fengchi" points. The onset of epilepsy is linked with the "Tianzhu" point.

    Epilepsy manifests with violent urges to kill. (As mentioned in "Qianjin," it can lead to high fever, rampant behavior, and hallucinations.) This is associated with the "Shenzhu" point.

    In cases where epilepsy leads to erratic behavior, if the spine feels tense and the eyes roll upward, the "Jinyu" point is involved.

    When epilepsy presents as violent episodes, with a thick and heavy facial appearance that resists treatment, and symptoms such as a heavy head, excessive urination and difficulty with bowel movements, a heavy lower back, and trouble with daily activities, it is governed by the "Changqiang" point.

    Moreover, in cases characterized by aversion to wind and chill, inability to speak, worsening symptoms with cold, a hot body and violent actions, suicidal thoughts, distorted vision, convulsions, and crying out, leading to a state of unawareness, the "Feiyu" point is indicated.

    Epilepsy linked with aversion to wind and chill, leading to difficulty in speaking, worsening with cold, a hot body, violent actions, suicidal tendencies, distorted vision, convulsions, and uncontrollable crying, results in a state of unawareness, again indicates the "Feiyu" point.

    The interrelation of epilepsy can be governed by the "Shuigou" and "Yin Jiao" points.[103p]

    　　癫疾狂，瘈瘲眩仆，癫疾喑不能言，羊鸣沫出，听宫主之。　　癫疾互引，口喎喘悸者，大迎主之；及取阳明太阴，候手足变血而止。　　狂癫疾吐舌，太乙及滑肉门主之。
    　　癫疾多言，耳鸣口僻，颊肿，实则聋龋，喉痹不能言，齿痛鼻鼽衄，虚则痹，膈俞、偏历主之。　　癫疾，吐舌鼓颔，狂言见鬼，温溜主之，在腕后五寸。　　目不明，腕急身热，惊狂躄痿痹瘈瘲，曲池主之。　　癫疾吐舌，曲池主之。[104p]

    The text describes various symptoms and conditions associated with madness and epilepsy. It discusses:

    • Madness and epilepsy characterized by fainting, inability to speak, foaming at the mouth, and listening to the main cause.
    • The interplay of symptoms like mouth twitching and gasping, suggesting reinvigoration.
    • Influences of different body channels on these conditions.
    • Symptoms including excessive talking, ear ringing, swelling of the cheeks, and severe conditions preventing speech.
    • References to throat issues, dental pain, and other physical ailments linked to these disorders.
    • Specific acupuncture points for managing symptoms, such as the position of the wrist for certain symptoms.
    • Finally, it mentions clarity of vision issues and physical agitation linked to these conditions.

    Overall, the focus is on identifying symptoms of madness and epilepsy, along with corresponding treatments through acupuncture points.[104p]

    　　热病汗不出，狂互引，颈嗌外肿，肩臂酸重，胁腋急病不举，痂疥，项不可顾，支沟主之。　　癫疾，吐血沫出，羊鸣，戾颈，天井主之，在肘后。　　热病汗不出，狂互引癫疾，前谷主之。　　狂互癫疾数发，后溪主之。
    　　狂癫疾，阳谷及筑宾、通谷主之。
    　　癫疾狂多，善食善笑，不发于外，烦心，渴，商丘主之。　　癫疾，短气呕血，胸背痛，行间主之。　　痿厥，癫疾，洞泄，然谷主之。
    　　狂癫，阴谷主之。
    　　癫疾，发寒热，欠，烦满悲泣出，解溪[解溪：原作「解谷」，据《甲乙》卷十一阳厥大惊发狂痫改。]主之。　　癫疾互引，僵仆，申脉主之。先取阴蹺，后取京骨、头上五行；目反上视，若赤痛从内眦始，复下半寸各三痏，左取右，右取左。　　寒厥癫疾，噤吤、瘈瘲、惊狂，阳交主之。　　癫疾，狂妄行，振寒，京骨主之。[105p]

    Fever with no sweating, madness alternating, swelling of the neck and throat, heavy shoulders and arms, urgent illness in the side and armpits unable to lift, scabs and eczema, the neck cannot be turned. The governing point is in the inner arm.

    In epilepsy, spitting blood and foam, bleating like a sheep, stiff neck, the governing point is at the elbow's back.

    Fever with no sweating, madness alternating with epilepsy, the governing point is in the front valley.

    For frequent episodes of madness or epilepsy, the governing point is at the back stream.

    For madness and epilepsy, the points of Yang Valley, Earth Mound, and Tong Valley serve as governing points.

    In epilepsy with significant madness, good appetite, and laughter, not manifesting outwardly, feeling uneasy, thirsty, the governing point is in the Commercial Mound.

    In epilepsy, shortness of breath, vomiting blood, chest and back pain, the governing point is in the Interstitial Valley.

    In atrophy and cold limbs, epilepsy, and loose stools, the governing point is in the Yin Valley.

    In madness and epilepsy, the governing point is in the Yin Valley.

    In epilepsy with febrile chills, discomfort, anxiety, and sorrowful crying, the governing point is in the Xie Stream.

    For intersecting epilepsy, rigidity and falling down, the governing point is in the Shin Pulse. First press the Yin Mound, then the Jing Bone and the Five Elements on the head; if the eyes turn up, as if there is a red pain starting from the inner canthus, press down a half inch, three times each side, left for right, right for left.

    In cold limbs and epilepsy, with lockjaw, spasms, and shock, the governing point is in the Yang Intersection.

    In epilepsy, with madness, shaking due to cold, the governing point is in the Jing Bone.[105p]

    　　身痛狂善行，癫疾，束骨主之，补诸阳。　　癫疾，僵仆转筋，仆参主之。
    　　癫疾，目(目巟)(目巟)，鼽衄，昆仑主之。　　癫狂疾体痛，飞扬主之。
    　　癫疾反折，委中主之。
    　　短气，心痹，悲怒，逆气，怒狂易，鱼际主之。　　狂易多言不休，及狂走欲自杀，及目妄见，刺风府。　　身热狂走，讝语见鬼，瘈瘲，身柱主之。　　狂妄言怒，恶火，善骂詈，巨阙主之。　　狂歌妄言怒，恶人与火，骂詈，三里主之。　　狂易，鱼际、合谷、腕骨、支正、少海、昆仑主之。　　狂言，太渊主之。
    　　狂言笑见鬼，取之阳溪，及手足阳明太阴。　　狂疾，掖门主之；又侠溪、丘墟、光明主之。　　狂互引，头痛耳鸣目痹，中渚主之。　　狂仆，温溜主之。[106p]

    Body aches from madness, the condition of mania, bones are bound and managed, supplementing all Yang. In cases of mania, stiffness and spasms of the limbs are overseen. Mania may cause symptoms such as headaches, nasal bleeding; Kunlun regulates this. Madness causing bodily pain and excitement is overseen by Feiyang.

    In severe cases of mania, Yin and Yang manifest as signs of reversal; Weizhong governs this. Shortness of breath, heart afflictions, sadness, anger, and repressed feelings, all surging uncontrollably, are overseen by Yujie. Excessive talk and manic tendencies to run away or self-harm, alongside hallucinations, are governed by Zhi Fengfu. Body heat from madness, running wildly, spouting nonsense, and moments of fainting are overseen by Shenzhu.

    Manic outbursts of anger, excessive heat, verbal abuse, and quarrels are regulated by Jueque. Manic singing, accusing others, and interaction with malevolent beings, along with cursing, falls under Sanli's care. Mania manifests through Yujie, Hegu, Wangu, Zhizheng, Shaohai, and Kunlun. Frivolous speech is tended to by Taiyuan.

    Manic laughter coupled with visions of ghosts is managed at Yangxi, as well as the extremities of Yangming and Taiyin. Severe mania is regulated at Yemmen; additionally, Xiaxi, Qiuxu, and Guangming oversee this. Mania causing mutual triggers, headaches, ear ringing, and eye impediments are governed by Zhongzhu. In cases of collapse from mania, Wenliu is responsible for regulation.[106p]

    　　狂妄走，善欠，巨虚上廉主之。
    　　狂易见鬼与火，解溪主之。
    　　《千金方》曰：解溪、阳蹺主癫疾。　　脑户、听会、风府、听宫、翳风，主骨酸眩狂，瘈瘲口噤，喉鸣沫出，喑不能言。　　臑会、申脉，主癫疾凑气。
    　　五处、身柱、委中、委阳、昆仑，主脊强反折，瘈瘲，癫疾，头痛。　　尺泽、然谷，主癫疾，手臂不得上头。　　曲池、少泽，主瘈瘲癫疾。
    　　飞扬、太乙、滑肉门，主癫疾狂，吐舌。　　温留、仆参，主癫疾，吐舌，鼓颔，狂言，见鬼。　　筋缩、曲骨、阴谷、行间，主惊痫，狂走，癫疾。　　完骨，主癫疾僵仆，狂疟。
    　　天井、小海，主癫疾，羊痫吐舌，羊鸣，戾颈。　　天冲，主头痛，癫疾互引，数惊悸。　　风池、听会、复溜，主寒热，癫仆。　　脑空、束骨，主癫疾大瘦，头痛。[107p]

    Arrogance leads one to wander, fostering goodness and negligence, with the chief overseeing vast emptiness.
    Madness is easily confronted with ghosts and fire, resolved by the solution of the creek.
    The "Thousand Gold Prescriptions" states: the creek and Yangqiao govern manic disorders. The brain door, auditory meeting, wind lord, hearing palace, and wind obstruction govern bone aches, dizziness, madness, mouth lock, throat noises producing foam, and the inability to speak. The shoulder meeting and the shen pulse govern manic conditions and breath gathering.
    The five regions, body pillar, waist middle, yin of the waist, and Kunlun govern spine rigidity, reversals, madness, and headaches. The cubit marsh and burning valley govern manic conditions, preventing the arms from lifting above the head. The crooked pool and lesser marsh govern spasms and manic disorders.
    The soaring, great one, and sliding flesh gate govern madness, with tongue extrusion. The warm retention and servant follower govern manic conditions, tongue extrusion, jaw beating, wild words, and visions of ghosts. The muscle contraction, crooked bone, yin valley, and action space govern fright and seizures, erratic wandering, and manic disorders. The complete bone governs rigid collapses due to mania and frenzy.
    The heavenly well and small sea govern manic conditions, with sheep seizures resulting in tongue extrusion, bleating noises, and neck tilting. Heavenly charge governs headaches and manic conditions inducing palpitations. The wind pool, auditory meeting, and reverting flow govern cold and heat, resulting in collapse from mania. The brain cavity and bound bone govern severe manic conditions and headaches.[107p]

    　　风府、昆仑、束骨，主癫疾，大瘦头痛。　　攒竹、小海、后顶、强间，主痫发瘈瘲，狂走不得卧，心中烦。　　大人癫，小儿惊痫，灸背第二椎及下穷骨两处，以绳度中折绳端一处，是脊骨上也。凡三处毕，复断绳作三折，令各等而参合如　字，以一角注中央，灸下二角，侠脊两端便灸之。凡五处也。故画图法，以丹注所灸五处，各百壮。削竹皮为度，胜绳也。　　卒癫，灸阴茎上宛宛中三壮，得小便通即瘥。 【《千金翼》云当尿孔上是穴。】　　又　灸阴茎头三壮。
    　　又　灸足大趾上聚毛中七壮。
    　　又　灸囊下缝二七壮。
    　　又　灸两乳头三壮。
    　　又　灸督脉三十壮，三报。穴在直鼻中上入发际。　　又　灸天窻、百会，各渐灸三百壮，炷惟小作。　　又　灸耳上发际各五十壮。[108p]

    The Wind Palace, Kunlun, and Bone Binding are associated with epilepsy, severe weight loss, and headaches. The Bamboo Gather, Small Sea, Back Peak, and Strong Interval are related to seizures and madness, causing restless nights and inner turmoil. For adults with epilepsy and children with convulsions, apply moxibustion to the second vertebra of the back and two points at the lower end of the spine, measuring with a rope to find the midpoint. After treating these three points, take the rope and divide it into three folds, aligning them in a manner resembling the character "字," marking the center with one angle and applying moxibustion to the two lower angles, as well as both ends of the spine, totaling five points. Thus, the illustrated method shows that each of the five points should receive one hundred moxibustion applications. Use bamboo skin as a better measuring tool than string.

    For sudden epilepsy, apply three moxibustion treatments to the center of the glans penis; relief is achieved once urination is normal. [As noted in "Qianjin Yi," the acupuncture point is located just above the urinary opening.] Additionally, apply three moxibustion treatments to the head of the penis, seven treatments in the gathering of hairs on the big toe, and twenty-seven treatments to the area below the scrotum. Apply three treatments to each nipple and thirty treatments along the Governing Vessel, dividing into three phases. The point is located directly above the nose, entering at the hairline. Also, apply three hundred gradual moxibustions to the Heavenly Window and Hundred Meetings, using small moxibustion sticks. Furthermore, apply fifty moxibustion treatments at the hairline above each ear.[108p]

    　　仓公法：狂痫不识人，癫病眩乱，灸百会九壮。　　狂走掣瘲，灸玉枕上三寸；一法，顶后一寸，灸百壮。　　狂走癫疾，灸顶后二寸十二壮。
    　　狂邪鬼语，灸天窻九壮。
    　　狂走癫疾，灸大幽百壮。
    　　狂言恍惚，灸天枢百壮。
    　　狂走癫痫，灸季肋端三十壮。
    　　狂痫哭泣，灸手逆注三十壮。穴在左右手腕后六寸。　　狂走惊痫，灸河口五十壮。穴在腕后陷中动脉是。　　狂癫风痫，吐舌，灸胃脘百壮，不针。　　狂邪发无常，披发大呼，欲杀人，不避水火，及狂言妄语，灸间使三十壮。穴在腕后五寸臂上两骨间。　　狂走喜怒悲泣，灸臣觉 【亦作巨搅。】 随年壮。穴在背上甲内侧，反手所不及者，骨芒穴一捻之痛者是也。【骨芒疑膏肓。】　　狂邪鬼语，灸伏兔百壮。 【前作天窻九壮】　　悲泣鬼语，灸天府五十壮。[109p]

    Cang Gong's Method: For mania that causes one to not recognize others, for epilepsy and dizziness, apply moxibustion at Baihui with ninety treatments. For frenzied running and convulsions, apply moxibustion three cun above the Yuzhen point; another method is to moxibustion one cun behind the top of the head with ninety treatments. For mad running and epilepsy, moxibust at two cun behind the top of the head with twelve treatments.

    For speaking madly or being possessed, apply moxibustion at Tiankuang with ninety treatments. For mad running and epilepsy, moxibustion at Dayou with one hundred treatments. For speaking in a daze, apply moxibustion at Tianshu with one hundred treatments.

    For mad running and epilepsy, apply moxibustion at the lower rib sides with thirty treatments. For mad epilepsy crying, moxibustion at the reverse wrist with thirty treatments. The acupoint is six cun behind the left and right wrist. For mad running and startled epilepsy, apply moxibustion at Hejiao with fifty treatments. The acupoint is located in the middle of the wrist, near the radial artery.

    For mad wind-hay sickness, if there is tongue protrusion, apply moxibustion at the stomach area with one hundred treatments, without needles. For mad disturbances manifested by unkempt hair and loud shouting, wishing to harm others, unafraid of water or fire, and speaking nonsensically, apply moxibustion at the wrist for thirty treatments. The acupoint is five cun behind the wrist, between the two bones of the arm.

    For mad running with fluctuating emotions like joy, anger, grief, and crying, moxibustion is applied at the area known as Chanjue (also called Jujao) depending on the year’s cycles. The acupoint is on the back, inside the shoulder-blade, at a point not reachable by a reverse hand; it is where bone pain can be felt.

    For mad speech from disturbances, apply moxibustion at Futu with one hundred treatments. For sadness and ghostly speech, apply moxibustion at Tianfu with fifty treatments.[109p]

    　　悲泣邪语，鬼忙歌哭，灸慈门五十壮。　　狂邪惊痫病，灸承命三十壮。穴在内踝后上行三寸动脉上。 【亦灸惊狂走。】　　狂癫风惊，厥逆心烦，灸巨阳五十壮。　　狂癫鬼语，灸足太阳四十壮。
    　　狂走，惊恍惚，灸足阳明三十壮。
    　　狂癫痫易疾，灸足少阳，随年壮。
    　　狂走，癫厥如死人，灸足大趾三毛中九壮。 【《千金翼》云灸大敦。】　　狂走易骂，灸八会随年壮。穴在阳明下五分。　　狂癫惊走风，恍惚嗔喜，骂笑歌哭鬼语，悉灸脑户、风池、手阳明太阳太阴、足阳明阳蹺少阳太阴、阴蹺足跟，皆随年壮。狂风骂詈挝斫人，名为热阳风，灸两吻边燕口处赤白际各一壮。　　又　灸阴囊缝三十壮。令人立，以笔正注当下已卧卵核上灸之，勿令近前中卵核，恐害阳气也。　　狂走刺人，或欲自死，骂詈不息，称神鬼语，灸口吻头赤白际一壮。　　又　灸两肘内屈中五壮。[110p]

    Weep with sorrowful words, ghosts busy with song and cries, apply moxa to the mercy gate fifty times. For madness and sudden convulsions, apply moxa to the command point thirty times. The point is located three inches above the inner ankle along the artery. [Also apply moxa for sudden madness.] For mania and epileptic fits, with reversed pulse and troubled heart, apply moxa to the great yang fifty times. For mad and crazy ghostly talk, apply moxa to the foot sun for forty times.

    For running wildly and being startled, apply moxa to the foot yangming thirty times. For easy onset of mania and epilepsy, apply moxa to the foot shaoyang, following yearly progress. For chaotic running, with convulsions like a dead person, apply moxa to the middle of the major toe three times. [The "Thousand Gold Supplement" states to apply moxa to the great dun.] For easy scolding and mad running, apply moxa to the eight meeting points according to yearly progress. The point is located five fen below the yangming.

    For mad and wild startled wind, with confusion and alternating anger and joy, scolding, laughing, singing, and ghostly talk; apply moxa to the brain door, wind pool, hand yangming, sun, and taiyin, foot yangming, yang qiao, shao yang, taiyin, and yin qiao at the heel, all according to yearly progress. For wild wind that insults and threatens people, named the hot yang wind, apply moxa to each side of the two lips at the red and white junction once.

    Furthermore, apply moxa to the seam of the scrotum thirty times. Have the person stand, and use a pen to mark where to apply moxa directly on the lying down egg core, ensuring not to get too close to the center of the egg core, for fear of harming the yang energy.

    For violent running and stabbing, or an intention to die, scolding incessantly and speaking of gods and ghosts, apply moxa to the red and white junction of the mouth once.

    Additionally, apply moxa to the inner bends of the elbows five times.[110p]

    　　又　灸背胛中间三壮，报灸之。仓公法神效。　　卒狂言鬼语，以甑带急合缚两手大指，便灸左右胁下对屈肋头两处，火俱起，各七壮。须臾鬼自道姓名，乞去，徐徐问之，乃解其手焉。　　风府、肺腧，主狂走，欲自杀。
