    Additionally, cauterize three points in the center of the back and shoulder blades, as prescribed by the method of Master Cang. In case of delirious talk or ghostly speech, bind both thumbs tightly with a bamboo steamer lid, then cauterize the two points under the sides, at the bending of the ribs—causing fire to rise at each location, a total of seven applications. Shortly, the spirit will reveal its name, pleading to leave; only then may you gradually loosen its restraints.

    The points Fengfu and Feishu are associated with mania, leading to suicidal impulses. Luoque, Tinghui, and Shenzhu are related to mania and convulsions. Tianzhu and Linqi are linked to excessive and incessant talking, with eyes turning upward. Zhizheng, Yujie, Hegu, Shaohai, Quchi, and Wangu are associated with manic speech, filled with shock and fear. Wenliu, Yamen, and Jinggu are connected to fainting spells in mania.

    Shenmen and Yanggu are linked to laughter that appears insane. Yangxi and Yanggu are associated with sticking out the tongue, tilting the neck, and making nonsensical statements. Juque and Zhubin relate to easily manifesting mania, characterized by angry curses and wild speech.[111p]

    　　冲阳、丰隆，主狂妄行，登高而歌，弃衣而走。　　下廉、丘墟，主狂言非常。
    　　劳宫、大陵，主风热善怒，心中悲喜，思慕欷歔，喜笑不止。　　风府、昆仑、束骨，主狂易多言不休。　　《丹溪心法》曰：卒狂言鬼语，针大拇指甲下，即止。　　《医学纲目》曰：秦承祖灸鬼法，狐魅神邪癫狂诸病，并小儿惊痫：两手大拇指，用软绳急缚之，灸三壮艾炷着四处，半在甲，半在肉上，四处尽烧，一处不着，其疾不愈，神效难量。此法累用累效。　　狂发怒，欲杀人，见鬼，灸明堂、身柱、后溪。身柱在三椎节下间。　　呆痴，刺神门一穴，沿皮向前三分，先补后泻。又后溪，补生泻成。　　又法：太锺。
    　　失志，呆痴，取神门、中冲、鬼服、鸠尾、百会。　　心闷不已，取支沟。
    　　伤寒发热，不识尊卑，取曲池、绝骨、百劳、涌泉。　　《本草纲目》曰：癫痫诸风，熟艾于阴囊下，谷道正门当中间，随年岁灸之。[112p]

    Chongyang and Fenglong govern madness and arrogance, climbing high to sing, discarding clothes and running. Xialian and Qiuxu govern wild and extraordinary speech. Laogong and Daling govern wind and heat, prone to anger, experiencing sadness and joy, longing and sighing, unable to stop laughter. Fengfu, Kunlun, and Shugu govern excessive talk and agitation.

    The "Danxi Heart Method" states: if one abruptly speaks wildly of ghosts, needle the area under the thumb to stop it. The "Medical Essentials" states: Qin Chengzu's method for ghost afflictions, fox spirits, demonic disturbances, and madness, including childhood seizures: bind both thumbs tightly with soft rope, applying three moxibustion cones at four points, half on the nail, half on the flesh, burning all areas; if one spot is left untouched, the illness will not be cured, and the effectiveness is hard to measure. This method shows cumulative results when used repeatedly.

    In cases of sudden anger wishing to harm others or seeing ghosts, moxibustion should be applied to Ming Tang, Shen Zhu, and Hou Xi. Shen Zhu is located between the third lumbar vertebra and the sacrum. For dullness and stupidity, needle Shen Men, extending three points forward along the skin, first tonifying then draining. For Hou Xi, tonify and drain.

    Another method: Tai Zhong. In cases of loss of will, dullness, needle Shen Men, Zhong Chong, Gui Fu, Jiu Wei, and Bai Hui. For constant heart oppression, needle Zhi Gou. For febrile diseases and inability to distinguish social ranks, needle Qu Chi, Jue Gu, Bai Lao, and Yong Quan. The "Bencao Gangmu" states: for epilepsy and all winds, apply moxibustion with roasted moxa under the scrotum, directly in the middle of the Gu Dao, according to age.[112p]

    　　　　导引

    　　《保生秘要》曰：风病导引法，先念背而通至四肢，又从四肢转骨轮处，想火烧之，风气结处折开环转推散。　　癫狂导引法：先将手把他手尺部拿住，又将手把他手中指之脉通心者，以指甲掐之，后又把他心头推开痰出，至神定时，教他念脐守之，久久复心头推开，分两边下谷道去。
    　　　　医案

    　　《千金方》曰：唐相国寺僧允惠患癫疾失心，经半年，遍服名医药不效。僧俗兄潘氏家富，召孙思邈疗之。孙曰：今夜睡着，明后日便愈也。潘曰：但告投药，报恩不忘。孙曰：有咸物但与师吃，待渴却来道。夜分僧果渴。孙至，遂求温酒一角，调药一服与之。有顷，再索酒，与之半角。其僧遂睡两昼夜乃觉，人事如故。潘谢孙，问其治法。孙曰：众人能安神矣，而不能使神昏得睡，此乃灵苑方中朱砂酸枣仁乳香散也，人不能用耳。又正肃吴公少时，心病，服前方一剂，五日方寤，遂瘥。[113p]

    Guidance

    The "Essentials of Preserving Life" states: For wind disease, one should first focus on the back and allow the energy to connect to the limbs, then visualize fire burning at the joints, dispersing the energy trapped at the wind-binding points. For treating insanity, first grasp the hand around the wrist, then press the pulse of the middle finger that connects to the heart, pinching it with the fingernail. Afterward, push away the phlegm from the heart, and when the spirit is calm, instruct the individual to focus on the navel. After a long time, push open the heart again, directing it down the two sides toward the valley.

    Medical Case

    The "Thousand Gold Prescriptions" states: A monk named Yunhui from the Tang Prime Minister’s temple suffered from insanity and loss of mind for half a year, having tried all famous doctors’ prescriptions without effect. His brother-in-law, from a wealthy family, invited Sun Simiao to treat him. Sun said: "Tonight, while you sleep, you will be better by tomorrow." The brother-in-law replied: "Just send the medicine, and I will remember your kindness." Sun said: "Only give the monk some salty food to eat; when he gets thirsty, I will come." At midnight, the monk indeed felt thirsty. Sun arrived and requested a bowl of warm wine, mixing a dose of medicine for him. After a while, he asked for more wine, giving him half a bowl. The monk then slept for two days and nights before awakening, returning to normalcy. The brother-in-law thanked Sun and inquired about his method. Sun said: "Many can calm the spirit, but few can make it dim enough to sleep. This is the 'Red Cinnabar, Sour Jujube Seed, and Frankincense Powder' from the spiritual garden, which people cannot rely on to aid sleep." Likewise, Wu Gong, in his youth, suffered from a heart condition; after taking a dose from this prescription, he awoke five days later and was cured.[113p]

    　　《儒门事亲》曰：一叟年六十，值徭役烦扰，而暴发狂，口鼻觉如虫行，两手爬搔，数年不已。戴人诊其两手脉皆洪大如絙绳，断之曰：口为飞门，胃为贲门。曰口者，胃之上源也。鼻者足阳明经起于鼻交頞之中，旁约太阳，下循鼻柱，交人中，环唇下交承浆，故其病如是。夫徭役烦扰，便属火化，火乘阳明经，故发狂。故经言阳明之病，登高而歌，弃衣而走，骂詈不避亲疏。又况肝主谋，胆主决，徭役迫遽而财不能支，则肝屡谋而胆屡不能决，屈无所伸，怒无所泄，心火磅礡，遂乘阳明经。然胃本属土而肝属木，胆属相火，火随木气而入胃，故暴发狂。乃命置燠室中，涌而汗出，如此三次。《内经》曰：木郁则达之，火郁则发之。良谓此也。又以调胃承气汤半斤，用水五升煎半沸，分作三服，大下二十行，血水与瘀血相杂而下数升，取之乃康。以通圣散调其后。[114p]

    The text from "The Rites of Confucianism to Serve Parents" states: A old man, aged sixty, suffered from the burdens of labor and became violently mad, with his mouth and nose feeling as if insects were crawling. He would scratch with both hands, and this persisted for several years. A physician diagnosed that both his wrists had strong pulses like thick ropes. The diagnosis was: the mouth is the "flying gate," and the stomach is the "entrance gate." The mouth is the upper source of the stomach. The nose is where the Foot Yangming meridian begins, connecting at the middle of the nose, alongside the Taiyang, descending along the nasal pillar, crossing the philtrum, encircling the lips, and joining the承浆. Thus, his ailment manifests in this way. The burdens of labor contribute to a fiery condition; fire rides on the Yangming meridian, resulting in madness. Hence, it is said in classical texts that when diseases of Yangming arise, one climbs high to sing, discards clothing, and insults without regard to family ties. Furthermore, the liver governs planning and the gallbladder governs decision-making. When labor is pressing and financial resources cannot sustain, the liver repeatedly plans but the gallbladder cannot decide, leading to a blockage without release. The heart fire becomes overwhelming, thus taking over the Yangming meridian. The stomach belongs to earth while the liver belongs to wood, and the gallbladder corresponds to the fire of mutual relations; this fire follows the energy of wood and enters the stomach, resulting in violent madness. He was commanded to be placed in a warm room, to sweat profusely, and this was repeated three times. The Inner Canon states: "When wood is stagnant, it should be unblocked; when fire is stagnant, it should be unleashed." Indeed, this is the case. He was given half a pound of the Tiaogai Chengqi Decoction, boiled with five liters of water until half-done, divided into three doses, resulting in a major downward purge of twenty measures, with a mixture of blood and stagnant blood excreted, and upon retrieval, he was well. Subsequently, he was treated with Tongsheng Powder.[114p]

    　　项关令之妻，病饥不欲食，常好叫呼怒骂，欲杀左右，恶言不辍。众医皆处药，几半载，尚尔。戴人曰：此难以药治。乃使二娼各涂丹粉，作伶人状，其妇人大笑。次日又作角抵，又大笑。常以两个能食之妇，夸其食美，病妇索其食而一尝之。数日怒减食增，不药而瘥。后得一子。夫医贵有才，无才何足应变无穷？
    　　一男子落马发狂，起则目瞪狂言，不识亲疏，弃衣而走，骂詈涌出，气力加倍，三五人不能执缚，烧符作醮，问鬼跳巫，殊不知顾。丹砂、牛黄、犀、珠、脑、麝备尝，赀财散去，室中萧然，不远二百里而求戴人一往。戴人以车轮埋之地中，约高二丈许，上安之中等车轮，其辋上罄一穴，如作盆之状，缚狂病人于其上，使之伏卧，以软裀衬之。又令一人于下坐机一枚，以棒搅之，转千百遭，病人吐出青黄涎沫一二斗许，绕车轮数匝。病人曰：我不能任，可解我下。从其言而解之。索凉水，与之冰水，饮数升，狂方罢矣。[115p]

    The wife of Xiang Guanling was ill from hunger and did not want to eat. She often yelled and cursed, wanting to harm those around her, and her harsh words never ceased. All the doctors prescribed medicine, but after nearly half a year, she was still the same. A certain man said: "This cannot be treated with medicine." So he had two courtesans apply red powder and act like performers, which made her laugh heartily. The next day, they staged a wrestling match, provoking more laughter. She often praised the food of two women who could eat well, and the sick woman asked for their food and tasted it. After a few days, her anger diminished and her appetite increased, and without medication, she recovered. Later, she bore a son. Physicians are valuable for their talent; without talent, they cannot adapt to endless changes.

    A man fell from his horse and went mad. When he got up, he stared wildly and spoke incoherently, not recognizing kin or stranger, discarding his clothes and running away, cursing as he went. His strength increased, making it impossible for three or five people to restrain him. They burned talismans and performed rituals, asking shamans for guidance, but remained ignorant of the true situation. They tried various substances like cinnabar, ox gall, rhinoceros horn, pearls, amber, and musk, wasting their wealth as their room became desolate. They traveled nearly two hundred miles to find the same man. He buried the madman under the wheel of a cart, about two zhang high, securing it in the center with wheel components. A hole was made in the rim, shaped like a basin, and the madman was tied to it, lying down on a soft mat. Another person was instructed to sit below a machine and stir it with a stick, turning it thousands of times, making the patient vomit a couple of dou of green and yellow froth around the wheel. The madman said: "I can't endure this; let me be released." He was set free as requested. They asked for cold water and gave him ice water to drink by several sheng, and only then did his madness subside.[115p]

    　　一狂人阴不胜其阳，则脉流薄厥，阳并乃狂。《难经》曰：重阳者狂，重阴者癫。阳为腑，阴为脏。非阳热而阴寒也，热并于阳则狂，狂则生寒；并于阴则癫，癫则死。《内经》曰：足阳明实则狂，故登高而歌，弃衣而走，无所不为，是热之极也。以调胃承气大作汤下数十行，三五日复上涌一二升，三五日又复下之。凡五六十日，下百余行，吐亦七八度。如吐时暖室置火，以助其热而汗少解，数汗方平。[116p]

    When a madman cannot withstand his yang, then his pulses become weak and he experiences a fainting spell; when yang is combined, he becomes mad. The "Nan Jing" states: excessive yang leads to madness, while excessive yin leads to insanity. Yang corresponds to the organs, and yin corresponds to the viscera. It is not that yang is hot and yin is cold; when heat combines in yang, it causes madness, and madness leads to cold; when combined in yin, it leads to insanity, and insanity results in death. The "Nei Jing" states: when the foot yangming is full, it leads to madness; thus, one climbs high and sings, discards clothing and runs, and does anything without restraint—this is the extreme of heat. To regulate the stomach and administer a great purging decoction, one should purge dozens of bowel movements; after three to five days, the fluid surges back up by one or two liters, and after another three to five days, it is purged again. After five to sixty days, purge more than a hundred times, and vomit seven or eight times. When vomiting occurs, keep a warm chamber with a fire, to assist the heat and reduce sweating, and after several sweats, balance will be restored.[116p]

    　　《丹溪心法》曰：外弟岁一日醉饱后，乱言妄语，妄见，询之系伊亡兄附体，言生前事甚的。乃叔在边叱之曰：非邪，食腥与酒太过，痰所为耳。灌盐汤一大碗，吐痰一二升，汗因大作，困睡一宵而安。
    　　金氏妇壮年，暑月赴筵，妇乃姑询其坐次失序，遂赧然自愧，因成此病，言语失伦，其中又多间一句，曰奴奴不是，脉皆数而弦。余曰：此非邪，乃病也。但与补脾清热导痰，数日当自安。其家不信，邀数巫者喷水而咒之，旬余而死。或问曰：病非邪而邪治之，何遽至于死？余曰：暑月赴宴，外境蒸热。辛辣适口，内境郁热。[117p]

    The text from "Danxi Heart Method" states: One year, after a day of drunken feasting, a disciple spoke irrationally, claiming to be possessed by the spirit of his deceased elder brother, recounting events from the brother's life with great detail. His uncle reprimanded him, saying it was not a spiritual issue, but rather the result of overindulgence in greasy food and alcohol, causing phlegm. After administering a large bowl of salt water, he expelled one or two liters of phlegm, sweated heavily, and slept soundly for a night, restoring his peace.

    A woman from the Jin family, in her youth, attended a banquet during the hot month. When her aunt questioned her disordered seating, she felt embarrassed and ashamed, leading to the onset of her condition, during which her speech became incoherent. Among her ramblings, she repeatedly stated that "I am not a servant," with a rapid and taut pulse. I said, "This is not a spiritual issue but a sickness." I suggested treating her with remedies to tonify the spleen, clear heat, and resolve phlegm, assuring that she would recover in a few days. However, her family did not believe me and summoned several shamans to spray water and cast spells on her. After about ten days, she died. When asked why a condition that was not spiritual led to death when treated as such, I explained that during the hot month, the external environment was steamy and oppressive, while the internal environment was filled with stagnant heat, exacerbating her condition.[117p]

    而况旧有积痰，加之愧闷，其痰与热，何可胜言！今乃惊以法尺，是惊其神而血不宁也；喷以法水，是实其体密其肤，使汗不得泄也。汗不泄则蒸热内燔，血不得宁则阴消而阳不能独立也，不死何俟！或曰：《外台秘要》有禁咒一科，庸可废乎？予曰：移精变气，乃小术耳，可治小病。若内有虚邪，外有实邪，当用正大之法，自有成式，昭然可考。然符水惟膈上热痰，一呷凉水，胃热得之，岂不清快？亦可取安。若内伤而虚，与冬受严寒，符水下咽，必冰胃而致害。彼郁热在里，热邪在表，须以汗解，卒得清冷，肤腠固密，热何由解？必致内攻阴阳离散，血气乖争，去死为近。[118p]

    Moreover, the old phlegm accumulated, combined with shame and gloom, what can be said of the phlegm and heat! Now, if startled by the measuring rod of the law, it startles the spirit and the blood becomes unsettled; if sprayed with the water of the law, it solidifies the body and tightens the skin, preventing sweat from draining away. If sweat does not drain, then the internal heat steams and burns, and if the blood is not settled, then the yin withers and the yang cannot stand alone—how can one survive this? Some say that the "Secret Essentials of the External Chamber" contains forbidden incantations; should they be abandoned? I say: transforming essence into qi is merely a minor skill, suitable for treating small ailments. However, if there is internal deficiency and external excess, one must use the grand and righteous methods, which have established patterns that are clearly verifiable. Furthermore, talismanic water only addresses heat and phlegm in the diaphragm; a sip of cool water relieves stomach heat, surely it brings comfort? It can also be used for tranquility. However, if there is internal injury and deficiency, akin to enduring severe cold in winter, swallowing talismanic water will assuredly freeze the stomach and cause harm. When there is heat trapped internally, and evil heat on the surface, it is necessary to relieve it through sweat; if one does not attain clarity and coolness, with the skin pores tightly sealed, how can the heat be resolved? This will surely lead to an internal attack, causing the yin and yang to scatter and the vital blood and qi to clash—death is imminent.[118p]

    　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：甲寅岁四月，予随斡耳朵行至界河里住，丑厮兀闽病五七日，发狂乱，弃衣而走，呼叫不避亲疏，手执潼乳与人饮，时人皆言风魔了。巫师祷之，不愈反剧。上闻，命予治之。脉得六至，数日不得大便，渴饮潼乳。予思北地高寒，腠理致密，病伤寒者少。然北地此时乍寒乍热，因此触冒寒邪，失于解利，因转属阳明证，胃实谵语，又食羊肉以助其热，两热相合，是谓重阳者狂，阳胜宜下，急以大承气汤一两半加黄连二钱，水煎服之。是夜下利数行，燥屎二十余块，得汗而解。翌日再往视之，身凉脉静，众人皆喜，曰：罗谦甫医好风魔也。由此见用伤寒非杂病之比，六经不同，传变各异。诊之而疑，不知病源，互相侮谤。呜呼！嗜利贪名，耻于学问，此病何日而愈耶？[119p]

    The "Treasure of Hygiene" states: In the year of Jia Yin, in the fourth month, I traveled to the boundary river and stayed there. A patient from Chou Siew Wen had been ill for five to seven days, raving wildly, tearing off his clothes and running away, calling out without regard for kin or stranger, and offering milk to others. People at the time said that the wind demon had come. The shaman prayed for him, but it only worsened his condition. The emperor heard of this and ordered me to treat him. I found six distinct pulses, and for several days, he could not defecate and was very thirsty, craving milk. I considered that in the northern regions, due to high cold and dense pores, there are few who suffer from cold-induced illness. However, the weather was fluctuating, causing exposure to cold evils and failure to relieve the condition, leading to a Yangming syndrome with fullness in the stomach, delirium, and, additionally, eating mutton to bolster the heat, which resulted in the two heats combining. This is called severe Yang madness, where Yang predominates and relief is urgent. Thus, I administered a large dose of the Da Cheng Qi Decoction with 1.5 liang of Huanglian, boiled in water for him to take. That night, he had several bowel movements, expelling over twenty pieces of dry stool, and he sweated and began to recover. The next day, I visited him again; he was cool to the touch and had a steady pulse. Everyone was delighted, exclaiming that Dr. Luo Qianfu had effectively treated the wind demon. From this, one can see that treating cold damage is not comparable to treating mixed diseases; the six channels differ, and each transmission varies. When diagnosing and uncertain, one does not know the source of the illness and instead insults and defames each other. Alas! The greed for fame and excessive attachment to reputation are shameful in the pursuit of knowledge. When will this illness ever be cured?[119p]

    　　《医学纲目》曰：浙江一妇人癫狂不止，医以瓜蒂半两为末，每一钱重，井华水调满一盏投之，随得大吐。吐后熟睡，勿令惊动，自此无恙。
    　　许氏病阳厥狂怒，骂詈不避亲疏，或哭或歌，六脉举按无力，身表如冰，若发即叫呼声高。洁古云：夺食则已，因不与之食。予用大承气汤下之，得脏腑渣秽数升，狂稍宁。数日复发，复下。如此五七次，行大便数斗，疾瘥，身温脉生，良愈。此易老夺食之法也。[120p]

    "The Essentials of Medicine" states: A woman from Zhejiang was continuously insane. The doctor ground half a tael of gourd seeds into powder, administered each dose weighing a qian, mixed with well water to fill a cup and gave it to her. She subsequently experienced a great vomiting. After vomiting, she fell into a deep sleep; she was not to be disturbed, and from then on, she remained well.

    A patient named Xu suffered from Yang rejection, displaying madness and rage, cursing indiscriminately, whether towards kin or strangers, sometimes crying or singing. The six pulses were weak upon inspection, her body felt like ice, and she would yell loudly if disturbed. Jie Gu stated: If we deprive her of food, it would suffice, thus we did not give her any to eat. I used the Major Order the Qi Decoction to purge her, resulting in several sheng of filthy matter expelled from her internal organs, and her madness moderately settled. After a few days, it recurred, and I purged her again. This was done five or seven times, leading to the expulsion of several dou of feces, and she was cured; her body became warm, and her pulse was restored, achieving complete recovery. This is the method of remedying through food deprivation.[120p]

    　　戊申年一人犯法褫衣，将受刑而得释，精神顿失如痴，予与惊气丸一丸，服讫而寐，及觉，病已失矣。
    　　提辖张载阳，其妻因避寇失心，已数年，予授惊气丸方，不终剂而愈。
    　　黄彦奇妻狂厥者逾十年，诸医不验，予授惊气丸方，去附子加铁粉，亦不终剂而愈。
    　　《古今医鉴》曰：一女子年十五，因气恼，患语言颠倒，欲咬人打物，偷藏东西，时哭时笑，心怕胆小，饮食不知饥饱，身体发热，以防风通圣散加生地黄、牡丹皮，二服即安。
    　　《万病回春》曰：一妇人发狂，弃衣而走，逾垣上屋，不识亲疏，狂言妄语，人拿不住，诸医措手，余令家人将凉水乱泼，不记数，须臾倒仆。诊其脉，六部俱弦数有力，乃热极生风也。用防风通圣散加生地黄、黄连、桃仁、红花、牡丹皮，三剂而安。后服祛风至宝丹，全愈。[121p]

    In the year of Wushen, a man committed a crime and was stripped of his clothes; he was about to be punished when he was released. His spirit suddenly lost its clarity, as if he were mad. I gave him a pill for shock and fear, which he took and then fell asleep. Upon waking, his illness was gone.

    Zhang Zaiyang, a deputy, had a wife who lost her mind due to fear of bandits; this had lasted for several years. I prescribed a pill for shock and fear, and she was cured before completing the dose.

    Huang Yanqi’s wife had been mad and convulsing for over ten years, with no remedy providing results. I prescribed a pill for shock and fear, removing the aconite and adding iron powder. She too was cured before finishing the dose.

    The "Ancient and Modern Medical Guide" states that a girl of fifteen, upset by anger, suffered from reversed speech, wanted to bite and hit people, secretly hid things, laughed and cried intermittently, felt fearful and timid, and could not distinguish hunger from satiety, experienced heat in her body. I treated her with Fangfeng Tongsheng San, adding raw Rehmannia and peony root; after two doses, she calmed down.

    The "Ten Thousand Diseases Returning to Spring" recounts a woman who went mad, discarded her clothes, jumped over walls and rooftops, did not recognize friends or family, spoke wildly, and could not be restrained by others. The doctors were at a loss, and I instructed her family to pour cold water on her chaotically. She was doused numerous times and soon fell down. Upon examining her pulse, all six positions were strong and taut, indicating extreme heat producing wind. I administered Fangfeng Tongsheng San, adding raw Rehmannia, yellow lumbricus, peach kernel, safflower, and peony root; she calmed down after three doses. Later, I prescribed the treasured pill to expel wind, and she was fully cured.[121p]

    　　《薛氏医案》曰：一仆人五月间病热，口干唇干，谵语，诊其脉细而迟，用四君子汤加黄芪、当归、芍药、熟附子，进一服，热愈甚，狂言狂走。或曰：附子差矣！诊其脉如旧，仍增附子，进一大服，遂汗出而热退，脉还四至矣。应天王治中遍身发黄，妄言如狂，苦于胸痛，手不可近。此中焦蓄血为患，用桃仁承气汤一剂，下瘀血而愈。
    　　太守朱阳山弟，下部畜血发狂，用抵当汤而愈。
    　　《证治准绳》曰：滑伯仁治一僧病发狂谵妄，视人皆为鬼，诊其脉累累如薏苡子，且喘且搏。曰：此得之阳明胃实。《素问》云：阳明主内，其经血气俱多，甚则弃衣升高，逾垣妄骂。遂以三化汤三四下，复进以清火之剂即愈。
    　　一人方饭间，坐甫定，即掬炉中火杂饭猛噬，且喃喃骂人。令左右掖而脉之，皆弦直上下行，而左手寸口尤浮滑，盖风痰留心胞证也。法当涌其痰而凝其神，涌出痰沫四五升，即熟睡，次日乃寤，寤则病已去矣。
    [122p]

    The "Xue's Medical Cases" states: A servant fell ill in May with fever, dry mouth, dry lips, and delirium. His pulse was thin and slow. He was given a dose of Si Jun Zi Decoction with added Astragalus, Angelica, Peony, and cooked Aconite. After administration, the fever intensified, leading to more delirium and rampant behavior. Some suggested that Aconite was incorrectly used. Upon checking the pulse, it remained the same, so the Aconite was increased, and a large dose was administered. This resulted in sweating, the fever subsided, and the pulse normalized.

    The King of Heaven treated a patient with a yellow complexion all over, wild speech, chest pain, and an avoidance of touch. The accumulation of blood in the middle jiao was the problem; he was given a dose of Peach Kernel Chengqi Decoction, which expelled the stagnant blood and restored health.

    The governor of Zhumountain's brother went mad due to abundant blood; he was treated successfully with Didao Decoction.

    The "Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment" mentions that Hua Boren treated a monk who was delirious and hallucinating, seeing people as ghosts. His pulse was excessive and slippery, and he was panting. It was determined that he had a full condition of the Yangming stomach. The "Suwen" states: "Yangming governs inside, with an abundance of both blood and qi, leading to extreme states like discarding clothes, climbing higher, and shouting wildly." Therefore, he took Sanhua Decoction three to four times, followed by a fire-clearing formula, which resulted in recovery.

    A person during lunch suddenly grabbed a handful of hot coals from the stove and furiously swallowed them, while also muttering and shouting at others. Those nearby helped and checked his pulse, which was string-like and moving straight up and down, while the pulse at the left wrist was particularly floating and slippery, indicating wind-phlegm obstructing the heart orifices. The method was to bring forth the phlegm and concentrate the spirit. After discharging four to five liters of phlegm, he fell into a deep sleep and awoke the next day, at which point the illness had resolved.[122p]
